# Decisions

Architectural / process decisions. Never deleted ‚Äî strikethrough if reversed.

## 2026-06-02 ‚Äî Agent-bootstrap walk follow-ups (#298 follow-up)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-02 | First-run done-screen unreachability fix: defer the agent-store mutation (`setSelectedAgent` + `hydrateAgentsOnce`) out of AgentBootstrap's `create()` and into a new `finish()` handler on "Start chatting ‚Üí". `create()` only stashes `createdAgentId` + `setStep('done')`, leaving the store empty so App's `noAgents` gate stays true and the done screen paints. | The store mutation mid-`create()` populated the agent list, flipping App.tsx's `noAgents` gate to false; in first-run `createAgentOpen` is false so `createAgentOpen \|\| noAgents` went false and AppContent unmounted AgentBootstrap before 'done' painted. Deferring the mutation keeps the gate open until the user leaves the done screen. | Force `createAgentOpen=true` for first-run (rejected ‚Äî abuses the "+ New agent" flag's meaning and the gate would still need the agent selected later); add a separate `bootstrapDone` flag to the App gate (rejected ‚Äî pushes bootstrap-flow state up into App, more coupling than deferring one store write). |
| 2026-06-02 | Extracted the gate predicate `shouldShowAgentBootstrap(...)` into its OWN module `src/lib/agent-bootstrap-gate.ts` (not exported from App.tsx). | The integration regression test must exercise the real gate predicate against the live agent store, but importing it from `App.tsx` drags the whole chat runtime + admin imports (`SkillEditor` ‚Üí `@ax/skills/manifest`) into the test's vite graph and fails to resolve. A tiny pure module is the faithful, cheap seam. | Keep it in App.tsx and build the runtime (rejected ‚Äî heavy + the test only needs the predicate); copy the predicate into the test (rejected ‚Äî a parallel copy drifts from production). |
| 2026-06-02 | `__LOCALID_` 404 fix: match the literal prefix in history-adapter (`const AUI_LOCAL_ID_PREFIX = '__LOCALID_'`), no import. | assistant-ui mints the placeholder via a template literal `` `__LOCALID_${generateId()}` `` in `@assistant-ui/core` RemoteThreadListThreadListRuntimeCore ‚Äî there's exactly one usage site and NO exported constant, so matching the literal is the only option. A regression test guards the behavior so an assistant-ui upgrade that changes the prefix would surface. | Import a constant (rejected ‚Äî none exported); fetch and swallow the 404 silently (rejected ‚Äî the browser still logs the failed-resource console error, which is the actual complaint). |
| 2026-06-02 | Phase-5 review: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent-dispatch tool (Task/Agent) was NOT available in this orchestrated env (ToolSearch returned no `Task` tool; only `EnterWorktree` matched). Substituted a rigorous whole-branch self-review against `main` + relied on the PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep). Mirrors the documented ARCH-4 fallback (2026-05-24) where a required review tool was genuinely absent. | Can't fabricate a subagent run when the tool is absent. The diff is small + low-risk (pure `@ax/channel-web` UI + one client-internal history-adapter guard; no hook surface, no untrusted-input path), so self-review is adequate; verified each fix goes red against the pre-fix code before declaring the regression tests valid. | Block waiting for the tool (rejected ‚Äî it's absent, not transient, would strand the card); skip review entirely (rejected ‚Äî replaced with documented self-review + hosted CI reviewers). |

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-137 De-flake flush-workspace-host.e2e BUG-W2 resync assertion (residual from TASK-123)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | Root cause of the `flush-workspace-host.e2e.test.ts > "host-side delete ‚Ä¶ resyncs cleanly"` **assertion** flake (not a timeout ‚Äî file ~607ms): the test's `makeHostClient` mock runs **real, fallible `git` subprocesses inside its IPC handlers** (`workspace.commit-notify`‚Üí`mirrorMain` rev-parse + `fetchBundleAdvance` fetch; `workspace.export-baseline-bundle`‚Üí`bundle create`). Under CI's severe multi-package + Docker-testcontainer starvation a SINGLE transient git subprocess hiccup (spawn EAGAIN / a starved non-zero exit) anywhere in the flush‚Üíretire‚Üícommit‚Üíresync sequence is correctly mapped by production `commitNotifyWithResync` to a DEGRADED outcome (`'kept'` on a thrown commit-notify call; `'rolled-back'` when a transient `rev-parse` returns null ‚Üí mock omits `actualParent`). The test then asserts `res.outcome==='accepted'` ‚Üí `expected 'kept' to be 'accepted'`. PROVEN by fault injection: throwing on the resync-retry commit-notify deterministically yields `resyncOutcome=kept`. The git LOGIC is deterministic (200√ó clean standalone sequence; clean even with a dirty-tree `--autostash`); only the subprocess *scheduling under starvation* is not. | This matches the card exactly (assertion flake, not timeout; the host-delete‚Üíflush‚Üírunner-commit resync path). It is NOT a git-ordering race (the parent-mismatch is structural: runner parent=foo-tip vs mirror head=retire) and NOT a fire-and-forget/wall-clock race like memory-strata's Observer ‚Äî so there is no un-awaited promise to await. The "ordering luck" the card names is the implicit bet that all ~6 fallible git subprocesses in the mock succeed on the FIRST try under load. | (a) bump per-test `testTimeout` ‚Äî useless, it's not a timeout (rejected); (b) `.skip` ‚Äî loses real BUG-W2/resync coverage (rejected); (c) loosen the assertion to accept `kept`/`rolled-back` ‚Äî masks a genuine "resync didn't land" regression (rejected). |
| 2026-06-01 | Fix: add a bounded **transient-failure retry seam** to the test's `git()` helper (and the mock's git calls route through it) so a starvation-induced spawn-EAGAIN / transient non-zero git exit is retried-to-completion ("settle") rather than treated as authoritative and mistranslated into a degraded outcome. Regression test: a fault-injecting mock variant that fails a git op on its first attempt and asserts the retry seam still drives the resync to `accepted`. | This is the "await the resync settle via a test seam, not ordering luck" the card asks for, adapted to the actual mechanism (fallible subprocess, not un-awaited async). It keeps the test exercising the REAL resync path while removing the starvation dependence. Production code is UNCHANGED (the degradation behavior is correct; the bug is the TEST betting every git fork succeeds first try). | bump global timeouts (wrong class); add retry to PRODUCTION `runGit` (out of scope + would change real degradation semantics ‚Äî rejected). |

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-133 skill editor form-first (settings-unified epic, design card 10)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|------|----------|-----------|--------------|
| 2026-06-01 | Make `@ax/skills-parser` the single round-trip authority by adding unknown-key preservation: `ParsedManifest` gains `extra: Record<string, unknown>` (the frontmatter keys the parser doesn't model), and `buildSkillManifestYaml` gains an optional `extra?` merged UNDER the known keys (known keys win). | Design card 10 + open-question line 153: "round-trip must preserve unknown frontmatter keys; lean on @ax/skills-parser as the single parse authority." Today's `buildSkillManifestYaml` only emits name/desc/version/connectors ‚Üí unknown keys are silently dropped. Additive `extra` field keeps every existing consumer working (they ignore it). | (a) A separate `parseSkillManifestWithExtra` fn ‚Äî rejected: two parse paths violate "single authority". (b) Preserve raw text instead of structured round-trip ‚Äî rejected: design pins the parser as authority and the form must edit structured fields. |
| 2026-06-01 | The editor's canonical state is `{ name, description, connectors[], body, extra, files, defaultAttached }`. Form mode binds typed fields; Advanced raw mode serializes that state to a SKILL.md string for free editing; toggling raw‚Üíform re-parses (must parse cleanly to return to form, else stay in raw with the error). | One source of truth in the component (structured fields + `extra`), so form‚áÑraw never drift. The parser/build pair is the only (de)serializer. | Keeping two independent states (form fields AND a raw string) and diffing ‚Äî rejected as the classic drift bug. |
| 2026-06-01 | Connectors field = multi-select sourced from `listConnectors()` PLUS free-entry of arbitrary connector ids (chips). | The manifest `connectors:` is a flat list of opaque slugs; a skill may reference a connector not in the user's own list, and the raw round-trip must preserve whatever's there. Load failure must not block authoring. | Plain dropdown limited to owned connectors ‚Äî rejected: drops references on round-trip. |
| 2026-06-01 | Re-export `buildSkillManifestYaml` + `splitSkillMd` (+ types) through the existing `@ax/skills/manifest` subpath so channel-web keeps its single `@ax/skills` dependency + existing eslint-disable import pattern. | channel-web depends on `@ax/skills`, not `@ax/skills-parser` directly; `./manifest` already re-exports `parseSkillManifest`. | Add `@ax/skills-parser` to channel-web deps ‚Äî rejected: extra dep + new import exception for no benefit. |
| 2026-06-01 | No subagent fan-out: Task/Explore/ax-code-reviewer dispatch tools are absent here. Implementing + reviewing inline, keeping context lean; running `/code-review` (high) as the local review gate in place of the ax-code-reviewer subagent. | yolo-ship Phase 5 requires a deep local review before the PR; `/code-review` is the available mechanism. | Skip review ‚Äî rejected, violates the gate. |

### TASK-133 gotchas (for TASK-134 adopt-&-edit, which builds on this editor)
- `SkillEditor` prop contract is UNCHANGED (`skillId?`, `onSaved`, `onCancel`, `api?`). All consumers (SkillsAppStore, CatalogTab, UserSkillsPanelBody) mock SkillEditor in their own tests, so the form-first rewrite didn't touch them. TASK-134 reuses the same component + `userSkillsApi` injection.
- The editor's canonical state is structured (`{name,description,connectors,body,version,extra,files,defaultAttached}`); `extra` carries unknown frontmatter keys + `sourceUrl` (folded in via `formFromParsed`) so the form‚áÑraw round-trip preserves them. Save assembles a SKILL.md via `assembleSkillMd` (form mode) or uses `rawText` (advanced mode) ‚Äî both flow through the same `skills:upsert/update` wire contract `(skillMd,{defaultAttached,files})`.
- TEST GOTCHA: the connector multi-select trigger has `role="combobox"` (not `button`) ‚Äî query it with `getByRole('combobox',{name:'Add a connector'})`, the aria-label is the accessible name. The `@ax/connectors` list lib must be mocked (`vi.mock('@/lib/connectors')`) in any SkillEditor test or `listConnectors()` hits the network.
- Local test env has NO Docker ‚Üí every `@ax/skills`/`@ax/agents`/channel-web *server* test that spins a Postgres testcontainer is auto-skipped + the file is marked "failed" (beforeAll throws). Real assertion failures = 0. CI has Docker. Don't chase these.

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-124 Per-slot credential refs (settings-unified epic, keystone)

- **The collapse-vs-expand rule keys on `connector.capabilities.credentials.length` (the connector's slot COUNT), NOT on whether two slots resolve to the same service tag.** Spec is explicit: exactly 1 slot ‚Üí `account:<service>` (byte-identical to today, no migration); ‚â•2 slots ‚Üí `account:<service>:<slot>` per slot. Rationale: the design wants a connector that declares e.g. CLIENT_ID + CLIENT_SECRET to get two distinct vault rows even though both fall back to the same service tag (the connectorId) ‚Äî that's the collision being fixed. Keying on count is the design's stated rule and is the simplest deterministic predicate every mirror can reproduce from the connector it already holds.
- **`Destination.account` gains optional `slot`; `refForDestination` reconstructs from it.** `{kind:'account', service, slot}` ‚Üí `account:<service>:<slot>` when `slot` present, else `account:<service>`. The PRESENCE of `slot` on the destination (set by the caller per the count rule) drives collapse-vs-expand at the ref layer ‚Äî `refForDestination` stays a pure deterministic function of its input, no count logic inside it. `assertNoColon` runs on `slot` too (slot names are SCREAMING_SNAKE `^[A-Z][A-Z0-9_]{0,63}$` per @ax/connectors SLOT_RE ‚Äî no colon, safe to append). All 3 mirrors + refs-fixtures.ts add a multi-slot fixture (`{service:'github', slot:'GITHUB_TOKEN'}` ‚Üí `account:github:GITHUB_TOKEN`) AND keep the single-slot fixture (`{service:'linear'}` ‚Üí `account:linear`) ‚Äî the byte-identical back-compat assertion.
- **`accountRef` becomes `accountRef(service, slot?)` ‚Äî the single ref-builder used by `deriveCredentialPlan` (both mirrors) and re-derived in the orchestrator fold.** `deriveCredentialPlan` computes `isMulti = connector.capabilities.credentials.length >= 2` once, then maps each slot to `ref: accountRef(serviceTagForSlot(slot, id), isMulti ? slot.slot : undefined)`. `serviceTagForSlot` unchanged. The orchestrator's `foldConnectorCaps` / `connector-card.ts` re-derive the SAME `isMulti`-gated ref locally (I2 ‚Äî no @ax/connectors import), pinned by connector-union.test.ts / connector-card.test.ts.
- **`CredentialPlanEntry` gains the destination-shaping bits so the connect-flow UI does NOT string-parse the ref.** ConnectorConnectDialog today does `entry.ref.slice('account:'.length)` to rebuild `{kind:'account', service}` ‚Äî that breaks for `account:<service>:<slot>` (would yield service=`<service>:<slot>`, failing the account regex). Instead the plan entry carries the structured `account` + optional `slotTag` (or the destination directly) so the UI builds `{kind:'account', service, slot?}` without parsing. This keeps WRITE (card/dialog ‚Üí setDestinationCredential ‚Üí refForDestination) and READ (orchestrator fold ‚Üí resolve vault) addressing the SAME row. Both deriveCredentialPlan copies (connectors + channel-web) carry the field.
- **PermissionCard's two write paths (skill `approveSkill`, connector `approveConnector`) must also emit the per-slot destination.** They currently build `{kind:'account', service: s.account ?? request.connectorId}`. The card's `slots[]` (from connector-card.ts / request-capability.ts) must gain the per-slot `account`+`slotTag` (or a `multiSlot` flag) so the card writes to the same per-slot ref the orchestrator fold reads. `haveExisting` in connector-card.ts / request-capability.ts likewise checks the per-slot ref.
- **Verify-before-merge (acceptance bullet 5): no existing multi-slot connector relies on the colliding `account:<connectorId>` ref.** Checked the codebase ‚Äî there are NO seeded/default multi-slot connectors; the only connectors are test fixtures + admin-authored at runtime. Single-slot back-compat means zero migration for the common case; the per-slot change only activates for ‚â•2-slot connectors, of which none exist with stored keys. Documented in PR.
- **No new service-hook signature.** `credentials:{set,get,list,delete}` unchanged ‚Äî the ref STRING is shaped differently, that's all. Only `Destination` (+ its 3 mirrors + DestinationSchema) gains optional `slot`. Boundary-review: not a new hook surface.
- **`CredentialSlotForm` static `id="cred-payload"` was a latent multi-instance id COLLISION** ‚Äî harmless until a multi-slot connector renders one form per slot (ConnectorConnectDialog). Fixed with `useId()` per instance (label `htmlFor` association); the label text stays "API key" (NOT the slot name) so the existing `getByLabelText(/api key/i)` tests + the parent dialog's `<p>{slot}</p>` heading both hold. The in-chat PermissionCard renders its OWN per-slot Input (`id=perm-cred-<slot>`, labelled by slot name) ‚Äî unaffected.
- **`UserSkillsPanelBody.tsx` authored-skill early-approve slot-write loop is effectively DEAD** ‚Äî `@ax/skills` `pendingCapabilitiesFor` always returns `{}` post-TASK-100 (a skill carries no caps; reach is its connectors, gated by the connector card). So `AuthoredSkillListing.pendingCapabilities` is never populated; its `{kind:'account', service: s.account}` write is the collapsed single-slot form and never sees a multi-slot connector. Left unchanged (changing it = gold-plating dead code); NOT a correctness gap.
- **Verify-before-merge (acceptance bullet 5) CONFIRMED empirically:** no seeded connectors, no migration-inserted connectors (migrations only ADD COLUMNs); all connectors created at runtime by admins/authoring. No multi-slot connector with stored keys exists ‚Üí the colliding `account:<connectorId>` ref has no live dependents ‚Üí zero migration needed.

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-123 De-flake push-to-main full suite (memory-strata + runner e2e)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-06-01 | memory-strata `plugin.test.ts` "writes to inbox" flake (ENOENT scandir on `.../inbox`) is a **fire-and-forget Observer raced by a fixed 50 ms sleep** (`waitForObserverSettle`). Fix DETERMINISTICALLY: add a test-only `onObserverSettleReady(settle: (agentId)=>Promise<void>)` seam mirroring the existing `onConsolidationSettleReady`, so the test `await`s the Observer's real promise instead of sleeping. | The Observer is intentionally fire-and-forget per I6 (chat:end must not block on a 30 s LLM call) ‚Äî that's correct production behavior, NOT the bug. The bug is the TEST betting 50 ms is enough for agents:resolve‚Üíllm:call‚Üífs-writes under parallel CI load; on a starved loop the inbox dir isn't created yet ‚Üí `readdir` ENOENT. Awaiting the actual promise is the same deterministic-seam pattern the consolidator tests already use (TASK-24 family). | (a) bump the sleep to 500 ms ‚Äî still a race, just rarer, and slows every run (rejected); (b) poll-with-retry on readdir ‚Äî masks a real "observer never ran" regression as a slow pass (rejected); (c) `.skip` ‚Äî card forbids unless quarantine-with-reason, and a real deterministic fix exists (rejected). |
| 2026-06-01 | runner `flush-workspace-host.e2e.test.ts` flake (5 s timeout; signatures ECONNRESET / "baseline-bundle fetch failed (500)" / "head moved again" are the resync code PATH it exercises, not the failure) is the **TASK-5/#146 load-induced class**: each test sequentially spawns ~25‚Äì30 real `git` subprocesses; under full `pnpm -r test` fan-out git startup latency balloons ~10√ó, breaching the default 5000 ms. Fix: per-`it()` `testTimeout` of 30 000 ms on the 3 e2e tests. | Reproduced: isolated host-delete test body ‚âà 514 ms; under 6√ó CPU overcommit the file's bodies hit ‚âà 3.94 s (individual tests flirting with 5 s). Strong precedent ‚Äî every other real-git package (`workspace-git`, `workspace-git-core`, `workspace-git-server`, `ipc-core`) already sets `testTimeout: 30_000`; runner is the lone real-git package with NO override. Per-test arg (not package-wide config) keeps the 5 s early-hang signal for the package's ~28 unit tests (mirrors `sandbox-k8s` keeping 5_000 deliberately, decisions 2026-05-25 TASK-5). | (a) package-wide `testTimeout: 30_000` in vitest.config ‚Äî relaxes the early-hang signal for all 30 runner test files (rejected, over-reach); (b) reduce git spawns in the test ‚Äî rewrites a verified real-path regression test, risk > reward (rejected); (c) `.skip` ‚Äî loses real BUG-W2/resync coverage (rejected). |
| 2026-06-01 | Scope: fix ONLY the two card-named tests. `git-workspace.test.ts` (35 tests, ‚âà560 ms/test, same real-git profile) is at the same latent risk but NOT named by the card and currently green; flag as a follow-up rather than widen scope. | Card acceptance is the two named suites; YAGNI on pre-emptively bumping a passing suite. The follow-up note preserves the lead. | bump git-workspace.test.ts too "to be safe" (rejected ‚Äî scope creep on a green suite; tracked as follow-up). |

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-118 Skills/Catalog tables: lead with human name, demote font-mono IDs

- **The "friendly name" IS the skill `description`.** `SkillSummary` / `AuthoredSkillListing` carry NO separate `name` field ‚Äî only `id` (the slug, e.g. `github-api`) + `description` (the human-readable summary). So "lead with the human name" = make **Description the first/lead column** and demote the `id` to a small muted `font-mono` subline rendered *under* the description in that same primary cell. The dedicated leading "ID" column is removed in all three tables (CatalogTab catalog table; UserSkillsPanelBody catalog table + authored table). The source/default/update-available badges that were attached to the old ID cell move next to the id subline.
- **Raw connector id-badges ‚Üí demoted behind a tooltip.** `SkillSummary.connectors` is `string[]` of raw connector IDs; the skill summary does NOT carry friendly connector names (those live on `ConnectorSummary.name` in @ax/connectors, unreachable here without a new fetch + state ‚Äî that overlaps TASK-119's connector-display scope and adds a runtime cross-plugin concern). So the demotion = render a compact count summary ("N connectors") whose raw ids live behind the shadcn `Tooltip` (installed but previously unused) + a `title` attr for accessibility/testability. Zero connectors keeps the existing em-dash. Rejected: (a) fetch connector summaries to map id‚Üíname in these tables ‚Äî heavier, overlaps TASK-119, adds network+state; (b) leave the raw id-badges as the connectors column unchanged ‚Äî fails acceptance sub-point 2.
- **Localized to table column structure** (per dispatch note: sibling TASK-119 also touches UserSkillsPanelBody) ‚Äî no changes to dialogs, handlers, fetch logic, or the authored-section approve flow.
- **Review fix ‚Äî `aria-label` not `title` on the ConnectorRefsCell trigger.** A `title` attr on a Radix `TooltipTrigger` fires a SECOND native browser tooltip alongside the Radix one (double-tooltip wart). Moved the machine-readable id list to `aria-label` (`"N connectors: id1, id2"`) ‚Äî read by screen readers + reachable by tests, no native tooltip. Regression test in `ConnectorRefsCell.test.tsx` pins `title === null`.

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-109 User-facing connector connect flow (keyMode JIT vs shared-key consent)

- **The connect flow derives the credential plan + consent gate CLIENT-SIDE from the full `Connector` (`getConnector(id)`), NOT a `connectors:resolve` BFF call.** There is no HTTP route for `connectors:resolve` ‚Äî only the 5 `/admin/connectors[/:id]` CRUD routes; `getConnector` already returns `capabilities`. So TASK-96's derivation (`deriveCredentialPlan`/`requiresSharedKeyConsent`/`sharedKeyConsentMessage`/`accountRef`/`serviceTagForSlot`) is **re-declared locally in `lib/connectors.ts`** ‚Äî mirroring the existing local `refForDestination` re-declaration in `lib/credentials.ts`. Rationale: `@ax/connectors` is NOT on eslint's runtime-import allowlist (only `@ax/credentials` is among the credential-ish plugins), and channel-web doesn't even devDepend on it; a runtime import is an I2 violation. A unit test pins the local behavior + the EXACT `SHARED_KEY_CONSENT_COPY` string (the consent text is a security contract). Alternatives rejected: (a) add a `connectors:resolve` HTTP route + lib wrapper ‚Üí new wire surface for data `getConnector` already carries; half-extra. (b) add `@ax/connectors` to the import allowlist for a drift-guard runtime import ‚Üí widens the cross-plugin runtime surface for a test convenience; the `refForDestination` precedent is local-re-decl + pin-by-test, not allowlist-widening.
- **keyMode ‚Üí write route is the EXISTING destination-credential split, no new wire:** `personal`‚Üí`scope:'user'` via `setDestinationCredential`‚Üí`/settings/destinations/account/credential` (server forces ownerId=actor, any authed user); `workspace`‚Üí`scope:'global'` via `/admin/destinations/account/credential` (`requireAdmin`). The consent gate is the design's "act as you" moment surfaced BEFORE the workspace key-entry form is reachable; `requiresSharedKeyConsent` = `keyMode==='workspace' || visibility==='shared'`. A non-admin opening a workspace connector can't store the global key (admin route is admin-gated) ‚Üí surface "an admin provides this shared key", not a raw 403. Destination = `{kind:'account', service: slot.account ?? connectorId}` ‚Üí ref `account:<service>` ‚Äî the SAME row TASK-96/97/112 read/write (divergent-ref trap avoided).
- **Connected/not = REAL credential presence, mirroring `CredentialSlotRow`.** Fetch `myCredentials.list()` (user-plan slots) / `adminCredentials.list()` (global-plan slots) once, match `c.ref===ref && c.scope===planScope`; connected iff every plan slot has a stored credential. **Empty plan** (no credential slots ‚Äî an MCP-no-key connector) ‚áí connected (nothing to prompt). The user list only returns the actor's own creds, so ref+scope match suffices (the JIT account flow already writes with `ownerId:null`).

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-120 ConnectorsTab: explain the orphaned 'Allowed sites' section

- **One muted helper `<p>` under the "Allowed sites" `<h3>`, mirroring the "Connected services" caption (`text-xs text-muted-foreground`).** Copy: "Not connectors ‚Äî these are individual hosts you granted this agent 'always allow' when it asked to reach one mid-task." Ties the section to the connectors above and disambiguates it from them. Semantics taken from the existing in-file comments (lines 90-93/276-279) + the design's durable per-(user,agent) "always allow" host grants (`@ax/host-grants`, TASK-54). Restructured the header flex row: title+caption now stack in a left `<div>`, the agent `Select` stays right-aligned; changed `items-center`‚Üí`items-start` so the taller left block top-aligns with the Select.
- **No hook/IPC/boundary/dep change ‚Äî pure channel-web copy; security-checklist not triggered.** Copy is a static React text node (auto-escaped); contains no mechanism vocab (`command`/`args`/`stdio`/URL/`transport`) so the existing line-132 mechanism-free guard still passes. TDD: added a test asserting a `/always allow/i` caption present whose text also matches `/connector/i`.
- **Phase-5 review substitution:** the `ax-code-reviewer` Task subagent is not dispatchable in this env (no Task/Agent tool surfaced). Logged here per the TASK-116 precedent; substituted a manual invariant walk + `/code-review` over `main...HEAD`. Diff is presentational JSX + one test, no logic/boundary surface.

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-116 KeysTab/CredentialsTab humane errors, no raw-ref leak, friendlier service field

- **Friendlier "Service" field = relabel + silent slugify, NOT a picker.** The card asks for "a friendlier label/picker that does not expose slug grammar." There is NO service catalog anywhere in the codebase ‚Äî `account:<service>` is a free-form slug any skill slot binds to via `account: <service>`; the only sources of service NAMES are the connectors list + the account-usage map (services already referenced). A true picker would need a new catalog wire surface (YAGNI / out of scope). So: keep the text input, relabel to "Which service is this key for?" with a human-name placeholder ("e.g. Linear, GitHub, Notion"), drop the slug-grammar validation copy + `ACCOUNT_SERVICE_RE` early-validation, and add `toServiceSlug()` that lowercases + hyphenates + caps-64 the user's input on SAVE so the result always satisfies the server grammar `/^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$/` (`credentials-admin-routes/destination-routes.ts`). Save enabled iff `toServiceSlug(input).length>0 && value.length>0`. Inferable from code+conventions (not a human product call): the contract row is unchanged, grammar is enforced silently rather than surfaced.
- **Humane error = sibling pattern + fixed next-step.** Replace the 5 `setError(String(e))` with a module-level `humanError(e) = e instanceof Error ? e.message : String(e)` (exact ConnectorsTab/ConnectorConnectDialog idiom). The destructive Alert leads with the card-mandated next-step sentence ("We couldn't save your key. Check it's correct and try again ‚Äî your admin can help if it keeps failing.") and shows the technical message as a secondary muted detail.
- **Unknown ref (`other` shape) no longer renders raw `kind:value`.** Map the `kind` segment to a human noun (`provider‚ÜíModel provider`, `mcp‚ÜíConnector`, `routine‚ÜíScheduled task`, fallback "Other credential") and a calm "Managed elsewhere" caption; never render the bare `provider:anthropic`-style string. Rows stay read-only.
- **No hook/IPC/boundary/dep change ‚Äî pure channel-web UI; security-checklist not triggered** (untrusted ref text still renders through auto-escaped React text nodes, same as before).
- **Review (Phase 5, ran `/code-review --effort high` ‚Äî the `ax-code-reviewer` Task subagent isn't available in this env, logged substitution) caught a prototype-key footgun:** `OTHER_KIND_LABEL[kind] ?? 'Other credential'` returns the INHERITED function for `kind==='toString'`/`'constructor'` (and an object for `'__proto__'`), which would crash the row render. Fixed with `Object.hasOwn(OTHER_KIND_LABEL, kind)` + regression test. General rule for a plain-object lookup keyed by ANY external string (even server-issued metadata): guard with `Object.hasOwn` / `Object.create(null)` / a `Map` ‚Äî a bare `obj[k] ?? fallback` leaks the prototype chain.

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-110 Connector-list polish: defaultAttached on ConnectorSummary + retire My Skills modal

- **Add `defaultAttached: boolean` to `ConnectorSummary` (the LIST shape) so the user connector list badges admin default-on connectors.** Before this, `ConnectorsTab` called `connectorSource(c)` where `c: ConnectorSummary` carried only `visibility` ‚Äî so an admin-curated default-on connector with `visibility:'private'` wrongly showed NO Catalog badge (the `defaultAttached === true` branch in `connectorSource` never had data). The fix is purely making `defaultAttached` flow into the summary: the store's `scopedConnectors` already `selectAll`s the column (so `listForUser` had the data, just dropped it in `rowToSummary`). Touch points (5): (1) `packages/connectors/src/types.ts` ‚Äî add field to `ConnectorSummary` interface + `ConnectorSummarySchema`; (2) `store.ts rowToSummary` maps `row.default_attached === true` (same coercion as `rowToConnector`); (3) `packages/channel-web/src/lib/connectors.ts` ‚Äî add field to its `ConnectorSummary` interface (and `Connector extends ConnectorSummary` then no longer re-declares it); (4) `mock/admin/connectors.ts toSummary` maps it; (5) `ConnectorsTab.tsx` needs ZERO change ‚Äî it already passes the whole `c` to `connectorSource`. NOT a backing-mechanism leak (`defaultAttached` is a storage-agnostic curation boolean already on the full `Connector` + every other hook shape; leak-guard `LEAKY_FIRST_CLASS_FIELDS` excludes it). NOT a boundary-review concern (additive field to an existing return shape, same field already on `connectors:get`/`list-defaults`).
- **Retire the user-menu "My Skills" modal entry; the Skills settings tab is the sole entry.** Remove: `UserMenu.tsx` menu button (+`onOpenUserSkills` prop +`BookOpen` import) ‚Üí `Sidebar.tsx` prop pass-through ‚Üí `App.tsx` `userSkillsOpen` state + `UserSkillsPanel` render + prop + import. `UserSkillsPanel.tsx` then has NO remaining consumer ‚Üí DELETE it (Half-Wired Code Policy: don't leave dead modal chrome). `UserSkillsPanelBody.tsx` STAYS (it's the shared content, rendered by `SkillsTab`).
- **Preserve the deep skill-body coverage by retargeting `UserSkillsPanel.test.tsx` ‚Üí `UserSkillsPanelBody.test.tsx`.** `UserSkillsPanel.test.tsx` (580 lines) held ALL the behavioral coverage (delete/share/authored/JIT-approve) but tested through the modal (`{open,onClose}` + a `My Skills` title). Deleting the modal would orphan that coverage. So: rename the file, render `<UserSkillsPanelBody active />` instead, drop the 3 modal-chrome tests (`open=false` not-rendered, the `My Skills` title-present tests), keep every behavioral test. The `SkillsTab.test.tsx` already lightly covers the tab‚Üíbody seam (list/badge/empty); the retargeted body test restores the deep behavior coverage. Alternatives rejected: (a) keep `UserSkillsPanel.tsx` as dead code (Half-Wired Code Policy forbids); (b) delete `UserSkillsPanel.test.tsx` outright (loses ~20 behavioral tests for live code).

## 2026-06-01 ‚Äî TASK-114 Connectors walk polish: re-propose dedup + Vite /settings dev-proxy

- **Re-propose dedup belongs in `connectors:install-authored`, NOT the orchestrator card path or the `connector_propose` tool.** Bug (TASK-101 walk): a warm-turn re-propose of an ALREADY-ACTIVE connector reset the authored draft to `pending`, and `fireUpfrontConnectorCards` (orchestrator) re-fired the upfront approval card every turn (it keys off a pending draft; `applyAuthoredConnectorGrant` clears `upfrontConnectorCardsByConv` on approval so every warm turn re-evaluates). Root cause = `installAuthoredConnector` always (re)wrote a pending draft with no check against the registry TASK-113 promoted into. Fix at the single chokepoint: pass the plugin's OWN live `localStore` (the registry, `ConnectorStore`) into the handler alongside the authored-draft store (both same-plugin ‚Üí no cross-plugin import, no new `calls` edge), and BEFORE upserting, `registry.getByIdNotDeleted(ownerUserId, connectorId)` ‚Äî if non-null it's a NO-OP (write nothing, return `{connectorId, status:'active'}`). No pending draft re-created ‚üπ orchestrator card path sees nothing to card. ONE fix covers BOTH acceptance sub-points. The tool path needed no parallel guard (it calls the hook).
- **Equivalence rule = pure id match, owner-scoped (simplest-correct, per the card's scoping note).** An active (not-deleted) registry connector owned by the SAME user with the SAME connector id. NOT a capability-fill comparison (that would be a product decision the card said to avoid). `getByIdNotDeleted` already filters `owner_user_id` + `deleted_at IS NULL`, so: (a) a different user's connector never triggers dedup (pinned by a cross-owner test), and (b) a SOFT-DELETED (un-approved/removed) connector returns null ‚Üí falls through to the normal pending+card path ‚Üí re-approval required (correct security posture ‚Äî tombstone never silently resurrects reach).
- **Wire change = widen `InstallAuthoredOutput.status` `'pending'` ‚Üí `'pending'|'active'`** (+ its zod `InstallAuthoredOutputSchema` union + the `@ax/tool-connector-propose` `ConnectorProposeOutput.status` mirror, which already passes `out.status` through). Only hook-surface change; `status` is a lifecycle verdict, storage/transport-agnostic, no leak; no boundary-review concern. SECURITY: the short-circuit only fires when an ALREADY-APPROVED (human-gated, TASK-113-promoted) connector exists ‚Äî it grants ZERO new reach (writes nothing) and cannot escalate/bypass approval; if no registry match, the pending+card path is byte-for-byte unchanged.
- **Vite dev-proxy `/settings` gap (item 2):** `packages/channel-web/vite.config.ts` proxy forwarded only `/auth`,`/admin`,`/api` to `AX_BACKEND_URL`; the connector connect/credential write POSTs to `/settings/*`, so a local Vite walk 404'd. Added `'/settings': { target: backendUrl, changeOrigin: false, ws: false }`. Config-only, no test: the MOCK middleware (offline mode) has no `/settings` connector handlers and the walk uses PROXY mode (real backend); real deploys are same-origin so unaffected. (Distinct config from TASK-106 but same dev-parity theme.)
- **Alternatives rejected:** (a) dedup in the orchestrator `fireUpfrontConnectorCards` card path ‚Üí symptom-patch, leaves the spurious pending draft (fails acceptance sub-point 1's "no pending draft re-created"). (b) dedup in the `connector_propose` tool ‚Üí the tool has no registry access without an `@ax/connectors` runtime import (I2 violation). (c) capability-fill equivalence ‚Üí product decision, out of scope.

## 2026-05-31 ‚Äî TASK-104 Fix postgres-testcontainer teardown 57P01 flake at root

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | Fix the uncaught `57P01` ("terminating connection due to administrator command") teardown flake with ONE shared helper `stopPostgresContainer(container)` in `@ax/test-harness`, and migrate all 105 postgres-testcontainer suites (106 call sites) to call it in `afterAll` in place of `await container.stop()`. The helper installs a temporary `uncaughtException`+`unhandledRejection` guard that swallows ONLY the benign 57P01 shape (by `code==='57P01'` OR the message substring), awaits `container.stop()` + one macrotask tick (the socket error surfaces async AFTER stop() resolves), then removes its listeners. No-ops on `undefined`. | Root-caused + reproduced: when `container.stop()` SIGTERMs postgres, the server kills every connection still bound to an OPEN `pg.Pool`. A test-created `pg.Pool` has NO `'error'` listener, so Node re-emits the connection error as an **uncaughtException** ‚Äî and vitest counts an uncaught exception during teardown as a suite failure even when every assertion passed (exact card symptom "This error originated ... while it was running"; control run = `Tests 1 passed / Errors 1 error ‚Üí EXIT 1`, helper run = EXIT 0). The card's two options are "drain pools before stop" (already mostly done in per-package `afterEach`, but a tick-late socket error still races) and "swallow the benign 57P01" ‚Äî the helper does the swallow as a deterministic BACKSTOP so the residual race can't red the suite, applied through one helper to avoid per-package drift (the card's stated preference). Typed against a minimal `{ stop(): Promise<unknown> }` so `@ax/test-harness` does NOT take a runtime dep on `@testcontainers/postgresql`. Every postgres package already devDepends on `@ax/test-harness`, so no package.json changes. | (a) Per-package `afterEach` pool-draining only ‚Äî rejected: it's necessary but not sufficient; the error surfaces a tick AFTER `destroy()`/`close()` resolves and races `container.stop()`, and TASK-94 already saw it red CI despite drained pools. (b) A global vitest `setupFiles` process guard installed for the WHOLE run ‚Äî rejected: it would mask a real 57P01 raised DURING a test (not just teardown); scoping the guard to the `stop()` window keeps real errors loud. (c) `fileParallelism:false` / serialize the suites ‚Äî rejected: masks the race, slows CI, doesn't root-cause. (d) Add `pool.on('error')` to every test pool ‚Äî rejected: ~100-file churn vs one helper, and still leaves the unawaited-rejection variant. |

## 2026-05-31 ‚Äî TASK-92 Skill manifest gains additive connectors[] reference list

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|

| 2026-05-31 | Connector-id grammar/bounds mirror the @ax/connectors store (`/^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9_-]*$/`, ‚â§128 chars), re-declared inline; count cap 64. | Same id space so a reference resolves later; re-declared (not imported) per I2 since `@ax/skills-parser` is a pure parser package. ## 2026-05-31 ‚Äî TASK-89 Make server early-bind authoritative (retry bind + 503 POST) to close cold-respawn 404 at the source

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | **Replace the single best-effort early-bind in `channel-web/src/server/routes-chat.ts` `postMessage` with a bounded-retry loop, then 503 the POST if the bind never lands.** New helper `bindActiveReqIdAuthoritative(bus, ctx, {conversationId, sessionId, reqId, logger})` ‚Üí boolean. Loop: capped-exponential backoff (start 25ms, √ó2, cap ~150ms) gated on a `Date.now()+BIND_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS` deadline (BIND_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS=400). On success ‚Üí return true (‚Üí 202). On bind throw ‚Üí keep the existing `chat_bind_session_failed` warn telemetry, sleep the clamped backoff, retry. Budget spent ‚Üí return false ‚Üí POST `res.status(503).json({error:'bind-unavailable'})`. | Card contract is "retry the bind, then 503 the POST if it can't be established." 400ms is small (sub-perceptible to a user; the SSE GET race is microseconds) yet absorbs a read-after-write replica lag race or a brief DB blip ‚Äî the realistic transient causes of a first-try bind failure when the row was JUST created/fetched in the same request. The happy path binds first try (one call, zero added latency) ‚Üí 202 exactly as today. 503 (not 202) on persistent failure means the client never gets a reqId whose `GET /api/chat/stream/:reqId` can never 200 ‚Äî it surfaces the existing CONNECTION_LOST banner + manual retry (TASK-88's client path), which re-POSTs the whole turn. This fix REDUCES how often TASK-88's ~30s client SSE-open budget is even exercised (the 404 window no longer opens on the happy path), without contradicting it. | (a) keep single best-effort + rely only on TASK-88's client retry (rejected: that's the mitigation, not the source fix this card asks for; leaves the 404 window open); (b) await the orchestrator's post-open-session bind instead (rejected: that's seconds later for a cold pod ‚Äî the exact latency this closes; and routes-chat fires agent:invoke fire-and-forget, it can't await the orchestrator); (c) huge retry budget / unbounded (rejected: a genuinely-missing conversation would hang the POST; 400ms bounds it and 503 lets the client retry cleanly). |
| 2026-05-31 | **If `bus.hasService('conversations:bind-session')` is false, return 503 immediately (do not 202).** Keep the `hasService` guard (matches the orchestrator's identical convention ‚Äî bind-session is NOT a manifest-declared call; both routes-chat and orchestrator.ts gate it via `hasService`). | A bind service that isn't registered means the bind can NEVER be established ‚Üí a 202 would hand back a reqId whose stream can never open, which is exactly the failure this card kills. In prod the k8s preset ALWAYS co-deploys @ax/conversations (verified: only preset booting channel-web, and it boots conversations), so this branch is effectively unreachable in prod; it's the correct contract-honoring fallback for a degenerate preset. Not declaring it in the manifest preserves the established peer convention and keeps blast radius off every harness's verifyCalls walk. | (a) promote bind-session to a hard manifest `call` (rejected: churns every channel-web test harness's verifyCalls + diverges from the orchestrator's hasService convention for the SAME hook ‚Äî one source of truth for the convention); (b) keep silent fall-through to 202 when absent (rejected: that's the bug ‚Äî 202 for an un-openable reqId). |
| 2026-05-31 | **Phase-5 review substitution: the `ax-code-reviewer` subagent + the Agent/Task dispatch tool were UNAVAILABLE in this orchestrated env (same gap as TASK-87/34/35), so I ran the `code-review` skill ‚Äî whose finder/verifier angles ALSO need the Agent tool ‚Äî and performed its 9 angles myself directly over the in-context whole-branch `main...HEAD` diff.** No actionable findings: the retry loop is bounded (no infinite spin ‚Äî `remaining<=0` returns false before sleeping; wait clamped to remaining budget; happy path = 1 call, returns true immediately); telemetry + `existingActiveSessionId ?? placeholder` behavior preserved; the only behavior change (absent service / persistent failure ‚Üí 503 instead of silent 202) is the card's intent. REUSE angle: no shared backoff/retry util exists (`@ax/core/util` has only safe-path + with-timeout; transport.ts's client loop is a different runtime/semantics ‚Äî I2 makes a cross-boundary util premature), so inlining matches precedent. Test-race check: `chatRunMockPlugin`'s `agent:invoke` mock does NOT call `conversations:bind-session`, so the happy-path `bindCalls===1` assertion is deterministic (not racy on the fire-and-forget orchestrator bind). The PR's hosted reviewers (CodeRabbit/CodeQL/semgrep/gitleaks) are the second pair of eyes in CI. | Block on the missing subagent (rejected: env capability gap, not a code issue; small additive pure-control-flow diff, 7 tests, hosted-reviewer-covered). | ‚Äî |
| 2026-05-31 | **Scope strictly server-side (channel-web) ‚Äî do NOT touch transport.ts.** The card's "client retries the whole turn" is already satisfied: transport.ts `sendMessages` throws on any non-OK POST ‚Üí runtime onError ‚Üí CONNECTION_LOST-class banner + manual retry (a deliberate re-POST). A POST 503 flows through that existing path unchanged. | Card explicitly says "Scope (server-side ‚Äî channel-web)". TASK-88 owns the client. Auto-re-POSTing a 503 client-side would risk duplicating a turn (FAULTA-5 forbids automated re-POST) ‚Äî the manual-retry affordance is the safe re-POST path. | (a) auto-retry the POST in transport (rejected: out of scope + FAULTA-5 duplicate-turn hazard); (b) special-case 503 vs other POST failures client-side (rejected: out of scope; the existing banner already handles it). |

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |

The single-source-of-truth fix is to make the parser (the one contract authority, shared by global/user/authored/promote flows) reject the misplaced keys, so a dropped/stripped-cap manifest is a loud structural reject regardless of which flow or which doc drift produced it. Defense-in-depth that holds even if the docs drift again. | (a) Make the GATE re-derive caps from the raw manifest text (REJECTED: duplicates the parser, a second source of truth, I4 violation); (b) have the gate treat "empty caps + a body that mentions hosts" as pending (REJECTED: unbounded heuristic on untrusted body text, false-positive minefield, not a real boundary); (c) silently MOVE top-level caps under `capabilities` in the parser (REJECTED: silently rewriting an adversarial manifest is exactly the wrong instinct ‚Äî fail loud, make the author re-draft). |

The docs were the drifted artifact (TASK-74 wrote `id`+semver+top-level caps). Moving the docs to the parser keeps ONE documented contract; changing the parser to accept `id`/semver/top-level would weaken the validation surface. | Change the parser to accept `id` as an alias (REJECTED: two identity keys = ambiguity + a wider attack surface; `name` is already the established key across every other skill flow). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Boundary review: no hook-surface change.** The parser change is internal to `@ax/skills-parser` (a stricter branch of an existing reject path). Invariant: no half-wired/dead code. | Keep it "just in case" (REJECTED: dead export = drift trap, and the card explicitly lists it for removal). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Boundary review for the new `skills:authored-activate` hook + the `status` field added to `agents:resolve-authored-skills`.** Alternate impl: the activate flip could be a direct store call if @ax/skills and the orchestrator were one plugin ‚Äî but they're separate plugins, so it MUST cross the bus (I2). Leak check: payload is `{ownerUserId, agentId, skillId}` + `{activated:boolean}` ‚Äî all storage-agnostic, no sha/bucket/pod/socket vocab. `status` ‚àà {active,pending,quarantined} is a gate-verdict enum, backend-neutral. | Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | **Re-point `conversations:drop-turn` from the git workspace (`workspace:list`/`read`/`apply` glob of `.claude/projects/**/<sid>.jsonl`) to the TASK-67 transcript rows: read bytes via `store.getTranscriptBytes(conversationId)`, run the EXISTING pure `dropTurnFromJsonl(bytes, turnId)` helper, split the rewritten bytes back to lines, write via `store.replaceTranscript(conversationId, lines)`.** No hook-signature change (DropTurnInput/Output unchanged). | TASK-67 gitignored the resume jsonl + moved it to `conversations_v1_transcripts` rows; the `workspace:list` glob now hits no git-tracked file ‚Üí `paths.length === 0` ‚Üí silent return (the no-op TASK-70 decisions.md:12 flagged out-of-scope). | 2026-05-30 | **The read-then-`replaceTranscript` (DELETE+re-INSERT, seq renumbered `1..N`) in drop-turn drops git's CAS-parent without a replacement version check, and this is SAFE.** The transcript store is single-writer-per-session (decisions.md:542 design note, NOT git CAS); drop-turn fires from `chat:turn-end` AFTER the turn shipped + completed, so the runner isn't mid-append. `getTranscriptPrefixHash` hashes line CONTENT + `\n` terminators in seq ORDER (not seq VALUES), so dense renumbering after a drop is hash-invisible ‚Äî a resume reads the new max+bytes consistently. A worst-case stale-`fromSeq` append after a drop hits the existing host delta-ship guard ‚Üí `resync-required` ‚Üí runner re-ships via replace-transcript (fail-safe, same posture as git's old parent-mismatch). | Removing the CAS-parent looked like a regression vs. the git path's `read.version`-as-parent (TASK drop-turn-against-git test). It isn't: the row store's concurrency model is single-writer + the resync net, not optimistic-CAS. Adding a bespoke version check would duplicate machinery the append guard already provides. | (a) add a version/optimistic-lock arg to replaceTranscript (REJECTED: re-creates CAS the store deliberately doesn't use; the resync guard covers the race); (b) read+rewrite inside one DB transaction (REJECTED: getTranscriptBytes + replaceTranscript are separate hooks/store calls; the single-writer invariant already serializes, and cross-call txn would need a new store method for no real-world race). |

## 2026-05-30 ‚Äî TASK-68 Attachments & artifacts onto the blob store; /ephemeral working tier (drop attachments:commit)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | **Add the REQUEST-direction binary IPC channel as `client.callBinaryUpload(action, payload, bytes)`** ‚Äî POSTs the raw blob bytes as `application/octet-stream` body with the JSON metadata in the `x-ax-payload` header; host dispatcher reads the RAW body (NOT `readJsonBody`, so it bypasses the 4 MiB `MAX_FRAME` cap, like the existing response-direction streaming) up to a 100 MiB ceiling. First (and only) action: `blob.put`. Returns small JSON `{sha256,size}`. | callBinary today is response-direction only (host‚Üírunner, streams bytes to a temp file). Upload is the mirror: runner‚Üíhost raw bytes, JSON envelope back. Octet-stream body matches design Part A ("bytes ride the callBinary octet-stream channel, never the 4 MiB JSON frame"). Header-carried JSON keeps the body pure bytes so the host streams it without a multipart parse. | (a) base64 the bytes into a JSON `blob.put` body (rejected ‚Äî re-introduces the 33% tax + 4 MiB cap that BUG-W3 removed); (b) multipart (rejected ‚Äî heavier parse, no benefit over header+raw-body for a single blob). |
| 2026-05-30 | **`blob.get` over IPC is response-direction: extend the EXISTING `callBinary` action union to include `blob.get`** (JSON request `{sha256}` ‚Üí octet-stream response streamed to a temp file). The runner reads the temp file. | The runner-side materialization of `/ephemeral/uploads` needs blob bytes from the host store; the response-direction callBinary already streams binary to disk under the disk-bounded cap ‚Äî `blob.get` is exactly that shape. No new transport, just a new action name in the union + a host dispatcher path. | A JSON `blob.get` returning base64 (rejected ‚Äî same cap/tax problem). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Artifacts: keep the sandbox-side `artifact_publish` executor's lstat‚Üísize-cap‚Üíread‚Üísha256, re-point the path allowlist to `/ephemeral/artifacts/**`, then the executor streams the read bytes to the host via `callBinaryUpload('blob.put', ‚Ä¶)` and calls a new host IPC action `artifact.publish` to insert the metadata row** `{conversationId, sha256, displayName, mediaType, size}`, returning `ax://artifact/<id>`. Durability is observable at `artifact_publish` return (the blob.put success), not turn-end. | Design Part C, outbound. The executor already does the validation + sha256; it gains the blob.put + metadata insert. The host owns the metadata row (the runner has no DB). The two IPC calls (blob.put bytes, artifact.publish metadata) are idempotent on sha256 so a retry is safe. | Have the host re-read the file (rejected ‚Äî host can't reach the sandbox `/ephemeral`); single fused IPC action carrying bytes+metadata (rejected ‚Äî bytes must ride octet-stream, metadata is JSON; splitting keeps the body pure). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Artifact namespace moves to `/ephemeral/artifacts/**` but ALSO keep `/permanent/workspace/**` publishable (Pattern A double-home).** The allowlist gains `/ephemeral/artifacts/` (primary) and retains `/permanent/workspace/` (the rare ax-hosted-project case the design's "what git keeps" section calls an intentional double-home). Drop `/permanent/.ax/artifacts/`. | Design: `/ephemeral/artifacts/` is the new artifact namespace; `/permanent/workspace/` Pattern A code may still publish a snapshot as an artifact ("git holds editable history, the blob holds the immutable shared snapshot"). The old `.ax/artifacts/` namespace is retired with the git artifact path. | Keep `.ax/artifacts/` (rejected ‚Äî that's the git artifact path Part C removes); `/ephemeral/artifacts/` only (rejected ‚Äî drops the legit Pattern A double-home the design names). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Inbound uploads: `attachments:store-temp` already holds the bytes; on send, REPLACE `attachments:commit‚Üíworkspace:apply` with a new `attachments:commit` impl that calls `blob:put` host-side + inserts an `attachments_v1_files` metadata row** `{conversationId, sha256, displayName, mediaType, size, path}` and returns the same `CommitOutput` shape (path now `.ax/uploads/<conv>/<turnId>/<file>` kept as the stable transcript reference key). NO git commit. The shared-mirror parent-mismatch race is gone with the `workspace:apply` call. | Design Part C inbound: store via blob:put host-side, attachments row, drop the git path. Keeping the `attachments:commit` hook NAME + output shape means routes-chat.ts and the transcript `attachment` block path reference are unchanged ‚Äî minimal blast radius, and the path string stays the download/scope key. | Rename the hook (rejected ‚Äî churns routes-chat + transcript schema for no gain); store at upload time instead of commit time (rejected ‚Äî the conversationId/turnId binding only exists at send/commit, and store-temp is pre-conversation; commit is the right chokepoint). |
| 2026-05-30 | **Download (`GET /api/files` ‚Üí `attachments:download`): resolve path‚Üírow‚Üí`blob:get`‚Üístream instead of `workspace:read`.** Keep the full ACL ladder (normalize ‚Üí owner-gate via conversations:get ‚Üí path-scope via transcript scan ‚Üí fetch). The path-scope check still scans the transcript (unchanged); only the final byte-fetch swaps `workspace:read` for a metadata-row lookup keyed by (conversationId, path) ‚Üí sha256 ‚Üí `blob:get`. Artifacts resolve the same way (artifact row keyed by (conversationId, path or artifactId) ‚Üí sha256 ‚Üí blob:get). | Design Part C download. The ACL is the load-bearing security boundary and is untouched; only the storage backend behind it changes. The translation reader reads the now-local file instead of `workspace.read`. | CONFIRMED by code: the model reads uploads from `<workspaceRoot>/.ax/uploads/...` = `/permanent/...` today (pre-tool-use re-root + the mistakes.md cluster-walked fix). Move uploads off git ‚üπ the file is no longer in `/permanent`, so it MUST be materialized to a path the agent can Read. `/ephemeral/uploads/` is the design's named home. Session-start is correct: the conversationId is known at boot (session.get-config), uploads are immutable per conversation, and a lazy-per-turn fetch can't satisfy a model that Reads the path before any attachment-translation runs. The path KEY stored in the transcript stays `.ax/uploads/<conv>/<turnId>/<file>` (stable download/scope key); only the on-disk materialization root changes. | Lazy write-through at translation time (rejected ‚Äî a model can Read the path on a turn with no new attachment block, before translation fetches it; session-start guarantees presence); keep workspace.read/git (rejected ‚Äî git path removed). |

## 2026-05-30 ‚Äî TASK-71 @ax/blob-store-s3 backend + MinIO-in-kind + GCS Workload-Identity chart

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | Implement `@ax/blob-store-s3` as a SECOND registrar of the EXISTING `blob:put/get/stat/delete` hook surface (TASK-65). Re-export structurally-identical `Blob*Output` types + `Blob*OutputSchema` zod schemas (the I2 two-backend pattern, like storage-sqlite/storage-postgres). Do NOT change the hook contract: payloads stay sha256/bytes/size only; bucket/endpoint/region/creds are plugin CONFIG, never payload fields. | Card scope + invariant I1 (storage-agnostic hooks). The schemas co-locate per-registration (ARCH-13 drift guard); a structurally-identical copy keeps the two backends honest. | Import the schemas from blob-store-fs (REJECTED ‚Äî cross-plugin import, invariant I2). |
| 2026-05-30 | Use `@aws-sdk/client-s3` pinned EXACT (no caret) to the latest 3.1057.0 ‚Äî the one new dependency. S3Client with `forcePathStyle:true` (MinIO/GCS need path-style), `endpoint`+`region` config, credentials resolved via the SDK's default provider chain when not given (so Workload Identity / IRSA / GKE metadata works with NO static keys in the tree). MinIO dev keys come from config (sourced from the credential vault / a k8s Secret), never hardcoded. | Card names @aws-sdk/client-s3; exact-pin matches the repo's "pin everything" posture + makes pnpm audit deterministic on the pinned range. Default provider chain is exactly how Workload Identity injects creds with zero static keys. | aws4fetch / minio SDK (REJECTED ‚Äî card names @aws-sdk; one impl covers all S3-compatible targets); caret range (REJECTED ‚Äî repo pins). |
| 2026-05-30 | Reuse the SAME content-addressed store SEMANTICS as fs: object key = `<sha[0:2]>/<sha[2:4]>/<sha>` within the bucket; put hashes bytes in-process (compute sha256, PutObject under the key); get re-verifies the digest and throws `corrupt` on mismatch; stat = HeadObject; delete = DeleteObject (idempotent, swallow NotFound/404); put idempotent via HeadObject fast-path before PutObject. Same SHA256_REGEX gate before building any key (no traversal via key). | Mirrors fs backend's integrity guarantees so the shared conformance suite passes identically; the key prefix is irrelevant to S3 but keeps parity + avoids one giant flat prefix. | Let S3 compute checksums (REJECTED ‚Äî we want digest re-verify on read regardless of backend; content-addressing is OUR invariant). |
| 2026-05-30 | Per-deployment registrar selection in the k8s preset via a new `blob` config block (discriminated `backend: 'fs' \| 's3'`), driven by `AX_BLOB_BACKEND` env (default `fs`). Exactly ONE of createBlobStoreFsPlugin / createBlobStoreS3Plugin is pushed ‚Äî mirrors workspace local/git-protocol. fs root defaults to a sibling dir on the workspace PVC; s3 reads endpoint/region/bucket/forcePathStyle + optional access-key/secret-key env. NOTE: blob-store-fs was NOT yet wired into the preset by TASK-65 (no consumer) ‚Äî this card wires BOTH backends in as the selectable seam (closes the half-wired window for fs too, justified because the canary round-trip exercises whichever is selected). | Invariant I3 (no half-wired): the s3 backend must be reachable via config. Wiring the selection is the only way "a deployment can select fs OR s3" is true. The canary test boots the selected plugin through bootstrap. | Wire only s3, leave fs dangling (REJECTED ‚Äî selection requires both arms; and fs being unwired is the pre-existing gap this card naturally closes). |
| 2026-05-30 | MinIO in kind: render a MinIO Deployment+Service+Secret in the chart, gated `minio.enabled` (default false in prod values, true in kind-dev-values), single-replica emptyDir (dev parity, not durable). Prod GCS: `blob.backend: s3` with endpoint=`https://storage.googleapis.com`, Workload-Identity ServiceAccount annotation, NO static keys (creds via the SDK metadata provider). The s3 backend's bucket/endpoint/region are plugin config; access keys (dev/MinIO only) ride a k8s Secret ‚Üí env, NEVER committed. | Card scope (Phase 6) + design Part A. emptyDir MinIO is fine for dev/test parity; durability is a prod-GCS concern. Workload Identity = the design's "no static keys" requirement. | Bitnami MinIO subchart (REJECTED ‚Äî heavier, another chart dep + Bitnami's flaky index; a small Deployment is enough for dev parity). |
| 2026-05-30 | Phase-5 review caught a CONFIRMED runtime-compat bug: AWS SDK JS v3 ‚â• early-2025 (3.1057 here) defaults `requestChecksumCalculation: WHEN_SUPPORTED`, adding an x-amz-checksum-crc32 / STREAMING-‚Ä¶-TRAILER header to PutObject that MinIO (pre-trailer releases) and GCS's S3 endpoint REJECT ‚Äî so a plain blob:put would fail against exactly the dev (MinIO) + prod (GCS) targets this backend exists for. The in-memory fake can't see it (no real HTTP). Fix: pin `requestChecksumCalculation` + `responseChecksumValidation` to `WHEN_REQUIRED` in buildS3Client (restores pre-2025 behavior every S3-compatible server accepts) + a build-client.test.ts regression guard that fails if the pin is dropped. | This is the design's "MinIO-in-kind round-trip ACTUALLY works" acceptance criterion ‚Äî without the pin it silently doesn't. Our own digest re-verify-on-read is the integrity guarantee, so dropping the SDK's redundant checksum costs nothing. | Leave the default (REJECTED ‚Äî breaks MinIO+GCS); per-server conditional (REJECTED ‚Äî WHEN_REQUIRED is correct for AWS too; no downside). |
| 2026-05-30 | Phase-4 whole-branch gate caught a real integration break: wiring blob-store-fs into the preset by DEFAULT made every preset acceptance test that boots via `bootstrap` with `backend: git-protocol` try to `mkdir /var/lib/ax-next/blobs` (the prod default fs-root for the non-local workspace backend) ‚Äî EACCES in the test sandbox. Fix: add explicit `blob: { backend: 'fs', root: path.join(tmp, 'blobs') }` to each preset-booting test config (the prod `/var/lib/ax-next/blobs` default is CORRECT ‚Äî the chart mounts a PVC there; only the test env needs the override). The local-backend tests were already fine (root derives under their tmp repoRoot). | Per-test override is explicit + mirrors how those tests already pass an explicit workspace; the prod default stays correct. The break is exactly the "shared-table / repo-wide" class the whole-branch gate exists to catch (yolo-ship Phase 4). | Change the preset's git-protocol default to a tmp path (REJECTED ‚Äî wrong for prod); skip the blob plugin in those tests (REJECTED ‚Äî they boot the REAL preset on purpose; dropping it hides the wiring). |
| 2026-05-30 | Lockfile recipe DIVERGES from TASK-65's "splice importer block only": this package adds a NEW third-party dep (@aws-sdk/client-s3) with a large transitive tree (@smithy/*, etc.) absent from the lockfile today, so new snapshot entries ARE required. Approach: targeted `pnpm add` of the exact-pinned dep in the new package, then verify `pnpm install --frozen-lockfile` is internally consistent and `pnpm audit --audit-level moderate` is clean (CI gate). Keep the diff scoped to the new importer + its transitive snapshot additions; revert any unrelated peer churn. | The TASK-65 predecessor learning's "no new snapshot entries" clause only held because that package had all-existing deps. A genuinely new dep needs its tree in the lockfile. | Full --no-frozen-lockfile (RISK ‚Äî drags unrelated peer churn; scope tightly + revert noise). |

| 2026-05-25 | **TASK-24 #2 recovery UX ‚Äî FINAL (after 5 Codex rounds): MANUAL retry banner for ALL drop/error cases; auto-retry filed as a follow-up needing idempotency infra.** Codex round 5 closed the last hole: even an orchestrator `error` frame (the "provably-dead" path I'd gated auto-retry to) can arrive AFTER the runner already executed a host tool or wrote a partial transcript turn ‚Äî so auto-`regenerate()` re-runs NON-IDEMPOTENT side effects a second time without user consent. Across 5 rounds EVERY auto-recovery variant (same-reqId silent resume ‚Üí lossy on host restart; broad auto-retry ‚Üí duplicates sendMessages-rejection turns; narrow auto-retry on the dead-turn frame ‚Üí duplicates post-side-effect turns) had a correctness hole. This is the FAULTA-5 invariant in full: with the current non-idempotent / non-transactional turn model there is NO client-side auto-retry that is loss-free AND duplicate-free. So #2 ships as the MANUAL-retry banner (the user consents to the re-run, accepting any duplicate) ‚Äî which is FAULTA-5's already-proven-correct behavior ‚Äî and a visible follow-up: a true auto-retry needs turn-level idempotency (server-side dedupe of a re-invoked reqId) + durable/seq-stable runner‚Üíhost events. **This is the explicit-clarification tension flagged in the handoff for the human:** the clarification asked for auto-retry+message; my analysis shows it's unsafe on current infra, so I shipped the safe subset and surfaced the gap rather than ship a duplicate-prone auto-retry. | 2026-05-25 | **TASK-24 ‚Äî REVERSED the same-reqId silent auto-reconnect; intermediate design = bounded auto-`regenerate()` ONLY on the provably-dead server `error` frame + honest banner on CONNECTION_LOST.** (Superseded by the row above after Codex round 5.) Codex (round 2) proved the same-reqId resume is SILENTLY LOSSY across a host RESTART: runner‚Üíhost `event.stream-chunk`/`event.turn-end` are one-shot `client.event().catch()` (NOT retried by Task-1's deadline, which only covers `call()`), AND the host chunk-buffer + its per-reqId `nextSeq` cursor are in-memory (lost on restart, re-minted from 1). So after an OOMKill restart the reconnected client (lastSeq=N) receives a replay starting at seq 1 ‚Üí all `seq<=lastSeq` ‚Üí silently deduped as duplicates ‚Üí the entire post-restart answer vanishes (or hangs if `done` is also deduped). Indistinguishable client-side from a safe same-host replay-overlap. This is the exact FAULTA-5 "auto-retry against a stateful server is almost always wrong" trap. | The reported bug is FIXED by Task-1 alone (runner survives + turn COMMITS ‚Üí no silent loss; visible on next history hydration). For #2, auto-retry is only loss-free AND duplicate-free when the turn is PROVABLY DEAD ‚Äî the orchestrator's `chat:turn-error` (server `error` frame, reason e.g. sandbox-terminated) means the runner is gone, so `regenerate()` routes to a fresh sandbox (no duplicate). | 2026-05-25 | TASK-21: a reloaded text/json/yaml/csv attachment rendered as RAW INJECTED TEXT (`User attached 'x.txt' (text/plain, 92 bytes):\n\n<file content>`) instead of a download chip. Root cause: `attachment-translation.ts` has TWO mention formats ‚Äî the fallback `formatAttachmentMention` (`...' at <path> (<mediaType>)`, single-line, path-bearing, which PR #120's read-path `reconstructAttachmentBlocks` recognizes) AND the inlineable-text branch's ad-hoc `User attached '<name>' (<mediaType>, <N> bytes):\n\n<content>` which (a) DROPS the path and (b) doesn't match `ATTACHMENT_MENTION_RE`. Small text files take the inline branch (weak-model accommodation), so they were never reconstructible on read. Fix: (1) add a shared `formatAttachmentInline(fields, content)` in `@ax/ipc-protocol` whose preamble IS the canonical `formatAttachmentMention(fields)` line (path-bearing) + `\n\n` + content; runner inline branch calls it. (2) extend `reconstructAttachmentBlocks` so a user-turn text block whose mention is the FIRST content line is the inlined-attachment shape ‚Üí emit the chip and DROP the trailing model-view content (don't surface it). | I4 single-source-of-truth: one producer/consumer pair, mirroring PR #120's `formatAttachmentMention`/`parseAttachmentMention`. The user's typed prompt and the attachment are SEPARATE content-array elements (main.ts:529-537) and `parseJsonlToTurns` keeps user blocks separate, so the inlined-attachment text is its OWN block ‚Äî dropping it can't clobber the typed prompt. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-21 Phase 5 (ACCEPTED ‚Äî real regression): Codex flagged a P2 ‚Äî my first read-path fix used a blanket `break` after converting the first in-prefix mention to drop the inlined model-view content. But the SDK can COALESCE adjacent user text blocks into one newline-joined block (the same reason the pre-existing `prompt\nmention` test exists), so a turn with MULTIPLE bare (non-inlined) attachment mentions would become `mention1\nmention2\ntext` in one block ‚Äî and the `break` dropped mention2 + trailing text on reload (a functional regression vs the pre-TASK-21 per-line behavior that converted EVERY matching line). | 2026-05-25 | TASK-19: "add $HOME/bin to PATH so agent-installed binaries persist between sessions." KEY FINDING resolving the card's literal "make .bashrc add it" wording: the agent's runtime `$HOME` is **`/permanent`** (`agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/main.ts:735` `HOME: env.workspaceRoot`, default `/permanent` ‚Äî env.ts:105), the git-bundled-and-restored workspace, NOT the image's `/home/axagent`. So `$HOME/bin` = `/permanent/bin`, exactly the persisted location. And the SDK Bash tool runs a **non-interactive** shell whose PATH comes ENTIRELY from the explicit `query({options:{env}})` allowlist (`proxy-startup.ts` forwards `process.env.PATH`; its comment: "Without forwarding PATH, the SDK's Bash tool executes `ls` and gets exit code 127" ‚Äî proof no rc file is sourced, else a default PATH would exist). A plain `.bashrc` is interactive-only ‚Üí the agent's shell would NOT source it. DECISION: do BOTH minimal layers ‚Äî (a) the **Dockerfile** writes a `.bashrc` to the image home that adds `$HOME/bin` to PATH (satisfies the literal ask + covers any interactive/BASH_ENV shell + is the discoverable convention), and (b) the **load-bearing** fix: add `${env.workspaceRoot}/bin` to the forwarded `PATH` in `main.ts`'s SDK env literal so the non-interactive Bash tool actually sees `/permanent/bin`. **APPEND, not prepend (codex Phase-5 [P2], accepted):** `$HOME=/permanent` is model-WRITABLE + restored across sessions, so PREPENDING would let a prompt-injection/malicious-tool-output `/permanent/bin/git` (or node/python) PERSISTENTLY shadow the trusted image/venv binary in every future session ‚Äî an I5/capability-minimization violation. Appending keeps installed tools discoverable (the goal) while trusted base+venv bins win on name collisions. (My original prepend rationale "the agent already controls its session" missed the cross-session PERSISTENCE + injection angle codex flagged.) Regression test: assert the SDK-subprocess PATH ENDS with `:<workspaceRoot>/bin` AND does NOT start with `<workspaceRoot>/bin:` (catches both a dropped-append regression and a re-introduced prepend) + a Dockerfile-content guard in `scripts/__tests__/dockerfile-home-bin-path.test.js` (runs unconditionally every PR via `pnpm test:scripts`, NOT package-affected-gated) asserting `.bashrc` carries `PATH="$PATH:$HOME/bin"` and NOT the prepend form. | Honors card INTENT (binaries found across sessions) via the mechanism that works for THIS runtime, not the one the card's wording assumes. `/permanent/bin` is the only dir that both is `$HOME/bin` AND persists (git-bundled); a binary in the image's `/home/axagent/bin` is neither writable by the agent's session nor where `$HOME` points. (b) is required because (a) alone is dead code for the SDK's non-interactive shell. | (a) ONLY the .bashrc, as the card's words say (rejected: the SDK Bash tool doesn't source .bashrc ‚Üí the agent never gets it ‚Üí half-wired/dead per the no-half-wired invariant); (b) ONLY mutate main.ts PATH, skip .bashrc (rejected: the card explicitly asks for the Dockerfile/.bashrc change + .bashrc is the human-discoverable convention for any future interactive shell); (c) set BASH_ENV in the forwarded env to point at a script (rejected: heavier, and the explicit-PATH forward is the established seam the venv/cache code already uses ‚Äî mutate PATH the same way `buildPythonVenvEnv` does); (d) bake binaries into image `/home/axagent/bin` (rejected: misreads "persists between sessions" ‚Äî that's the workspace tier, not the image) |

On a source-only change (packages/lockfile/`*.ts`) neither moves, so WITHOUT this the gha cache would satisfy the apt layer from cache and the build would NEVER re-resolve the Debian index ‚Äî exactly the rotted-pin scenario the guard exists to catch would sail through green. `no-cache-filters` takes Dockerfile STAGE NAMES (verified against docker/build-push-action + buildx docs); both Dockerfiles name their final stage `runtime`, so one value covers both. Keeps caching the expensive `builder` stage (pnpm install + tsc + deploy) ‚Äî only the cheap runtime stage re-runs. | `no-cache: true` (rejected: nukes the builder-stage cache too ‚Üí every run redoes the multi-minute pnpm build, the exact cost the cache exists to avoid); drop the cache entirely (rejected: same cost problem); leave as-is and accept the gap (rejected: it silently defeats the guard's stated purpose ‚Äî Codex is right) |

| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: `manifest.optionalCalls` is `{ hook: string, degradation: string }[]` (object array, not bare strings) ‚Äî distinct from `calls` (required) | The card's whole intent is a human-readable degradation note **per** optional call, so the note must be a first-class field, not a comment. Object array is the only shape that carries it. Motivating real case: `@ax/credentials` calls `storage:get`/`set`/`delete-prefix` only behind `bus.hasService(...)` and degrades to in-memory; today it can't declare them (would break `verifyCalls` in store-blob-only harnesses) so they hide in a code comment. | bare `string[]` like `calls` (rejected: drops the note, the point of the card); separate `degradationNotes` map keyed by hook (rejected: two fields that must be kept in sync = a leak waiting to happen) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: optionalCalls are **non-fatal** in `verifyCalls` (missing = fine) but **still form call-graph + topo-order edges when the producer IS present** | Non-fatal is the entire distinction from `calls`. But an optional edge is a real dependency when the producer exists: it must (a) be ordered after its producer so `hasService` is true by the consumer's `init()`, and (b) count toward cycle detection ‚Äî an optional call can still close a cycle. So `buildCallGraph` includes optional edges (already guarded by `prod !== undefined`); only `verifyCalls` skips them. | Ignore optional edges entirely in the graph (rejected: a present-producer optional call could hide a cycle, and could init before its producer making `hasService` flaky) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-4: a hook in BOTH `calls` and `optionalCalls` is a manifest error, caught at schema-refinement time | Required-AND-optional is a contradiction; silently picking one would mask a manifest mistake. Zod `.superRefine` on the schema rejects the overlap with the offending hook named, alongside the existing field validation, so bootstrap's `invalid-manifest` path reports it. | Let `calls` win silently (rejected: hides author error); check only at bootstrap not schema (rejected: schema is the canonical validation point ‚Äî keep it co-located) |

| 2026-05-22 | Sub-project B Basic-auth transform uses a **per-request re-arming HTTP/1.1 framing state machine** in the MITM client‚Üíupstream path, not single-head-per-connection as design ¬ß4.2 literally describes | git smart-HTTP reuses ONE CONNECT tunnel for `GET /info/refs?service=git-upload-pack` (no body) **then** `POST /git-upload-pack` (body), and with creds in the URL libcurl sends `Authorization: Basic` **preemptively on both**. Single-head buffering would transform the GET but leave the POST's base64 placeholder corrupted ‚Üí fetch fails after refs succeed. State machine: buffer head‚Üítransform Basic‚Üí`Content-Length`-counted body then re-arm to head; `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` or oversized head ‚Üí flush + verbatim passthrough, no re-arm (the chunked POST is the clone's last request, so not re-arming after it is safe). Header-only rewrite; bodies keep existing verbatim per-chunk sub (honors I1). | Single head per connection (rejected: corrupts the POST auth on keep-alive); full chunked de-framing to re-arm after chunked bodies (rejected: YAGNI ‚Äî git's chunked POST is terminal; adds a chunk-size parser for no MVP gain); line-scan for `Authorization:` anywhere in the stream (rejected: false-matches inside POST bodies could corrupt them) |
| 2026-05-22 | B canary parity: run the canary scan on the **decoded** `user:pass` inside the transform, before re-encode | Canary scanning today is inline `chunk.includes(token)` on raw decrypted bytes (`listener.ts`), not a registry function ‚Äî a base64-wrapped canary in a Basic blob would slip past it once we start decoding. Design ¬ß4.5 mandates parity.
