The crash is `Error: Claude Code returned an error result: No conversation found with session ID: X` ‚Äî thrown when `query({resume:X})` finds **no parseable user/assistant message** for X (jsonl missing/empty/metadata-only/user-line-truncated/garbage). | Repro matrix: control/truncated-line/dangling-tool_use ‚Üí success; deleted/empty/metadata-only/truncated-user/garbage ‚Üí "No conversation found"; lone-user / user+assistant ‚Üí success. Matches the cluster symptom (~2s after pod_ready, pre-API). Architecture: commits fire only at turn-end (main.ts:995/1149), so a turn killed before its first commit never persists a transcript ‚Äî but the host **bind fires at `system/init`** (main.ts:774), so it persists `runner_session_id=X` pointing at nothing ‚Üí retry resumes X ‚Üí crash. | Trust the handoff/TODO "truncated transcript" hypothesis (rejected: repro disproved it ‚Äî would have shipped a useless jsonl-repair) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a fix = **(root) move the `conversation.store-runner-session` bind from `system/init` to the first host-ACCEPTED turn-end commit**, gated on `conversationId!==null && bootRunnerSessionId===null && once-only`; **(defense-in-depth) a resume guard** (`hasResumableTranscript`) that omits `resume` + logs when a bound session has no parseable transcript, instead of letting the SDK hard-crash | Root fix makes `runner_session_id` set IFF a resumable transcript is durable on the host ‚Üí the stale-binding window can't form ‚Üí retry sees NULL ‚Üí clean fresh start (no rebind needed; no host change; the once-only host bind at plugin.ts:1003 stays intact). The init-bind was already useless pre-commit (conversations:get globs the jsonl, which isn't committed until turn-end). Guard is the literal TODO ask + converts any future bound-but-missing-transcript (materialize/git regression) from a hard `exit 1` to graceful degradation. Bind-failure at turn-end is self-healing (flag left unset ‚Üí next accepted commit retries) rather than fail-loud, since the turn already streamed to the user. | (a) Resume-guard alone (rejected: omit-resume mints a fresh id ‚Üí init-bind hits host `conflict` ‚Üí another exit 1 ‚Äî must move the bind); (b) seed a minimal transcript under X so resume works (rejected: hand-crafting the SDK jsonl line schema is fragile across SDK pins); (c) new `unbind-runner-session` host hook + rebind (rejected: bigger cross-plugin surface; `unbindSession` clears active_session_id, not runner_session_id); (d) SDK start-fresh-with-id (rejected: SDK has no such option ‚Äî only resume/forkSession) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a: implement **INLINE strict TDD**, not per-task subagents | Single package (agent-claude-sdk-runner), fully mapped (init handler, both commit sites, commit-notify outcome, transcript format from the live repro); ~3 surgical edits + 2 test files; context well under cap; ship loop is where lean context matters. Mirrors decisions 19/38/50/58/63. | Per-task subagents (rejected: re-deriving the held context costs more + divergence risk on a subtle bind-timing change) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a: security-checklist NOT formally invoked; brief PR-body note | No NEW hook/IPC surface (store-runner-session signature unchanged ‚Äî only its call SITE moved), no new capability, no new dependency, no new untrusted-content ingestion (guard reads only line `.type`, not content; transcript was already model output on a trusted path). No boundary-review trigger fires. | Full security-checklist (rejected: no trigger) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 2 (High) ACCEPTED: bind failure must distinguish 409 conflict (terminal) from transient (self-heal) | My initial swallow-all "self-healing" was too broad. A `conversation.store-runner-session` 409 (HOOK_REJECTED, per ipc-core/handlers/conversation-store-runner-session.ts) means another runner already bound the conversation to a DIFFERENT id ‚Äî a concurrent fresh-boot race. Swallowing+retrying lets the LOSER keep streaming + committing an orphan transcript, defeating the host's once-only bind. Fix: `bindRunnerSessionIfNeeded` re-throws on `IpcRequestError && status===409` ‚Üí propagated past both commit catches ‚Üí outer catch ‚Üí `terminated` (surfaced by F2b); transient (network/5xx, client already retried 5xx) stays self-healing. The 409 in the commit try can only come from the bind (commitNotifyWithResync swallows its own IPC errors). | Keep swallow-all (rejected: orphan + double-bind race, Codex-flagged); make ALL bind failures fatal (rejected: fatal-after-a-streamed-turn on a transient blip is incoherent UX) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 3 (Medium) ACCEPTED: self-heal test rewritten to the realistic multi-turn shape | My first self-heal test relied on the post-`result` FINAL commit retrying the bind ‚Äî but in production the final drain commit is usually empty (null) because the per-turn commit already captured the turn. Rewrote it: turn-1 per-turn bundle + turn-2 per-turn bundle + final ‚Üí null (`mockResolvedValueOnce` chain), bind transient-fails on turn 1 and succeeds on turn 2's accepted commit. Proves the retry comes from the NEXT TURN, matching prod. | Keep the final-commit-retry test (rejected: optimistic vs prod where final is null) |
| 2026-05-24 | F2a Codex finding 1 (High ‚Äî demotion-path orphan) DEFERRED to a tracked follow-up, NOT fixed in this PR | When the resume guard demotes a stale binding (bound id with no resumable transcript), the row stays bound to the stale id (the host bind is once-only ‚Äî a rebind would `conflict`), so `conversations:get` reads the stale path and the fresh transcript is orphaned; this repeats every boot. Deferring is defensible because: (a) the ROOT fix means `runner_session_id` is set only after a durable commit, so NEW conversations can never form a stale binding ‚Äî the demotion path is reachable ONLY for pre-existing rows already broken by the very bug being fixed (which TODAY crash on resume) or a hypothetical future materialize/git regression; (b) my fix turns those from a hard `exit 1` crash into a functional-but-empty-history chat ‚Äî a strict improvement; (c) full repair needs a host-side rebind/overwrite capability (new IPC action + hook + boundary review) = a separate scoped change; (d) making the demotion path attempt a rebind WITHOUT host support would hit the once-only conflict ‚Üí with finding-2's terminal-conflict that becomes a crash-LOOP for legacy rows ‚Äî worse UX than silent-functional. The gate therefore stays `runnerSessionId===null` (demotion never binds). Tracked in TODO.md (host-rebind repair for legacy/regression stale rows). | Fix in-PR via a host rebind hook (rejected: cross-plugin scope creep on a runner-side fix; gated on whether legacy stale rows matter in practice); make demotion bind+conflict-terminate (rejected: crash-loop for legacy rows) |
| 2026-05-24 | **auto-ship/yolo-ship live per-card progress block + crash recovery; loosen "agents never write the board" ‚Üí routing-fields-only.** The building yolo-ship agent appends fine-grained per-phase heartbeat lines (`brainstorm done` ‚Üí `task k/N done` ‚Üí `codex review clean` ‚Üí `PR #n opened` ‚Üí `CI green ‚úÖ`, `‚öÝ`-prefixed exceptions) to a delimited `<!-- AUTOSHIP-PROGRESS -->` block in **its own** card body; the orchestrator stays sole writer of the **routing fields** (`Status`, `Depends on`) + sole card-mover. On run-start/resume only, auto-ship reconciles orphaned In Progress/In Review cards (CLI death kills agents+poller): **PR exists ‚áí Phases 0‚Äì5 done ‚áí route to merge queue; no PR ‚áí reset to To Do + discard the partial branch**. | "While the agent is implementing" rules out funneling through the orchestrator (it only hears at the ‚â§150-word handoff). **One writer at a time is structural** (agent owns the body while In Progress; orchestrator only at terminal Done/Parked, after the agent exited) so no lock needed; the orchestrator dropped its PR-link body-append so there's never a 2nd writer. **Token discipline:** the read-modify-write is **shell-side** (`append_progress` in `github-project.md ¬ß6`) ‚Äî the growing body never enters model context (orchestrator adds 0 tokens; it never reads In-Progress bodies). Progress writes are **best-effort** (never block a ship) and land on In-Progress cards so they don't trip the To-Do poller. Recovery leans on yolo-ship opening the PR only in Phase 6. `.gitignore` switched to a `.claude/auto-ship-*` wildcard for the new helper+lock. | Funnel progress through the orchestrator (rejected: not live ‚Äî only at handoff); model-side RMW / hold the body in context (rejected: body grows, pollutes context + tokens); coarse happy-path updates (rejected: user chose fine-grained ‚Äî the per-phase heartbeat is what flags a wedged agent across parallel cards); resume the partial branch on a no-PR orphan (rejected: fragile; pre-PR work is cheap to redo); let the agent own a real lock / write routing fields (rejected: serialized merge queue + routing stay orchestrator-owned to avoid races) |
| 2026-05-24 | **`.claude/memory/` is now COMMITTED** ‚Äî reversing the prior keep-uncommitted default. CLAUDE.md ("Codex Memory Bootstrap" + Skills line) and the `claude-memory` skill (frontmatter, bootstrap step 3, store-boundary table) updated to "update and commit memory files after any change"; the misleading `.gitignore` comment fixed. | Vinay directive 2026-05-24: memory SHOULD be updated and committed. The post-merge fast-forward collision (PR #126) that motivated keeping memory local came from INCONSISTENT state (some rows committed, divergent local rows not) ‚Äî committing consistently removes the divergent-uncommitted class. The files were already tracked in git (the "gitignored" claim was never true), so this aligns instructions with reality. | Keep uncommitted (rejected: user reversed it); actually gitignore `.claude/memory/` (rejected: opposite of the directive) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-5: ship `@ax/sandbox-protocol` as a pure zod-schema contract package, modeled on `@ax/ipc-protocol` / `@ax/workspace-protocol` (no `@ax/core` dep, just zod) and added to the eslint `no-restricted-imports` allow-list | Both sandbox backends + the orchestrator structurally re-declare `ProxyConfigSchema`, `InstalledSkillSchema`, `McpServerSchema`, `OpenSessionInputSchema`. They already drifted: subprocess's `ProxyConfigSchema` is `.min(1)` + `.refine(exactly-one-of endpoint/unixSocketPath)`; k8s's is bare `.optional()` (accepts neither/both). A shared contract package keeps the no-cross-plugin-import rule (it's allow-listed like the other `*-protocol` packages) while killing the drift. | Type-only shared package (rejected: the duplication is the *runtime zod validation*, not just types ‚Äî types alone wouldn't stop strictness drift); leave duplicated (rejected: that's exactly the drift the task targets) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-5: adopt the STRICTER subprocess `ProxyConfigSchema` (min(1) + exactly-one-of refine) as the canonical shared schema | The orchestrator's `endpointToProxyConfig` already guarantees exactly-one-of at construction; the strict schema documents+enforces that invariant. k8s's lax schema accepted neither/both ‚Äî a latent bug (a both-set or neither-set proxyConfig would pass k8s validation and stamp inconsistent env). Converging UP to the stricter schema is the safe direction. | Adopt k8s's lax schema (rejected: weakens a trust-boundary check on the k8s pod-env path); make strictness configurable (rejected: YAGNI, one true shape) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-5: keep `OpenSessionInputSchema` construction in each backend; the shared package exports the field schemas (`ProxyConfigSchema`, `InstalledSkillSchema`, `McpServerSchema`, `AgentConfigSchema`) + a shared `OpenSessionInputSchema` both compose | The task names the four duplicated concepts; all are now single-sourced. | 2026-05-24 | ARCH-3: chose **Approach 1 (git-runner protocol package)** over Approach 2 (storage-neutral "runner snapshot transfer" protocol). ## ARCH-2 ‚Äî IPC dispatcher dependency metadata (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | Export a single `DISPATCHER_DEPENDENCIES` const from `@ax/ipc-core` (`requiredCalls: readonly string[]`, `optionalCalls: readonly OptionalCall[]`, `dynamicCallPatterns: readonly string[]`). Both `@ax/ipc-http` and `@ax/ipc-server` spread it into `manifest.calls = [...requiredCalls]` and `optionalCalls = [...optionalCalls]`. | The dispatcher is the single source of truth for what services it transitively invokes; transports must not re-derive it (drift = the ARCH-2 bug). `@ax/ipc-core` is allowlisted in `no-restricted-imports`; both transports already runtime-import `dispatch`/`authenticate` from it. | Per-transport hardcoded lists (status quo ‚Äî drifted); a function returning the manifest fragment (over-engineered, no alternate impl ‚Äî a 2-array spread is clearer). |
| 2026-05-24 | required = unconditional dispatcher calls whose producer is present in BOTH transport consumers (`session:resolve-token`, `session:claim-work`, `tool:list`, `session:get-config`, `workspace:read`). optional = guarded/branch-conditional OR not-guaranteed-present (`conversations:store-runner-session` [unconditional on its route, but the local CLI loads ipc-server WITHOUT @ax/conversations ‚Äî Codex P1 caught this], `conversations:get-metadata` [conversationId!==null], `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` [hasService], `workspace:apply-bundle` [bundle path], `workspace:list` [non-bundle materialize fallback]). dynamic prefix = `tool:execute:`. | `verifyCalls` fails boot if a REQUIRED producer is absent; promote to required ONLY if the producer is guaranteed present wherever a transport loads. The two real consumers are `packages/cli/src/main.ts` (loads workspace-git + session-inmemory + tool-dispatcher, NO conversations) and `presets/k8s` (loads everything). So `conversations:store-runner-session` MUST be optional. | All-required (breaks the CLI boot ‚Äî the bug Codex flagged); all-optional (loses the missing-service boot check for genuinely-mandatory deps). |
| 2026-05-24 | "Stay in sync" test = source-scan (`dependency-sync.test.ts`): read every handler + `auth.ts`, regex-extract each `bus.call('lit')`/`bus.hasService('lit')` hook string + each `namespace:action:`-shaped template-literal prefix, assert each is covered by required ‚à™ optional ‚à™ dynamic-prefix; plus a reverse "no dead declared hook" check + `DISPATCHER_PATHS` non-empty check. | A new handler adding an undeclared `bus.call` is exactly the drift ARCH-2 prevents; a static-equality test is a tautology. The dynamic prefix is matched from the `const hookName = `tool:execute:${...}`` template (a variable, not inline at the call site), filtered to hook-shaped prefixes so error-message template literals don't masquerade as hooks. | Hardcoded expected-list equality (tautology). |
| 2026-05-24 | CLI-3: digest-pin **only the uv image ref** in `container/agent/Dockerfile` (`COPY --from=ghcr.io/astral-sh/uv:0.11.16@sha256:440fd6477af86a2f1b38080c539f1672cd22acb1b1a47e321dba5158ab08864d`), keep the `0.11.16` tag visible + a comment. Do NOT digest-pin the `node:20-bookworm-slim` base. | The card names uv/uvx + the tini/ca-certs follow-up; the base-image pin is a SEPARATE tracked follow-up (Dockerfile lines 45-47) explicitly gated on "the image build pipeline lands" with the documented intent of letting local builds float as Node rolls patch releases. Digest-pinning the base now would (a) freeze Node patches and (b) exceed CLI-3's scope. uv digest came from `docker buildx imagetools inspect` (the multi-arch OCI index digest, not a per-platform manifest). | Pin the base image too (rejected: separate gated follow-up, contradicts the float-on-patches intent); resolve via `docker manifest inspect` per-arch digest (rejected: that pins one platform, not the multi-arch index) |
| 2026-05-24 | CLI-3: version-pin the apt deps (`ca-certificates=20230311+deb12u1`, `tini=0.19.0-1+b3`, `git=1:2.39.5-0+deb12u3`, `git-lfs=3.3.0-1+deb12u1`, `python3=3.11.2-1+b1`) in the runtime stage's `apt-get install`. Apt isn't digest-addressable in the install line; "content-addressed" maps to a hard version pin for apt. Versions resolved live from the signed `bookworm/main` binary Packages.gz over HTTPS. | The card asks to fold the tini/ca-certs follow-up in. The signed Debian archive's per-`.deb` checksums already provide content-addressing on download; the version pin makes the install reproducible. RESIDUAL RISK: a hard `=version` pin rots when a Debian point release supersedes it and drops the old from the pocket ‚Äî and there is NO docker-build step in ci.yml and NO local docker daemon here (vpulim not in `docker` group, no passwordless sudo), so the build is UNVERIFIABLE locally and a rotted pin would break the image build undetected. Mitigation: surface a follow-up to add a CI docker-build guard. | Leave apt unpinned (rejected: the card explicitly folds in the tini/ca-certs follow-up); pin only tini+ca-certs and leave git/git-lfs/python3 floating (rejected: half-measure ‚Äî "all image deps content-addressed" means the whole install line, and mixed pinned/unpinned is the confusing state the card removes) |
| 2026-05-24 | CLI-3: cannot run `docker build`/`docker run` to verify the image (no daemon access in this sandbox). ## ARCH-6 ‚Äî returns schemas for public service hooks (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: scope the `returns`-schema rollout to **IPC-reachable + security/tenant-boundary service hooks**, deferring the long tail. In-scope hooks: workspace (`workspace:read`, `workspace:list`, `workspace:apply`, `workspace:diff`), session (`session:resolve-token`, `session:get-config`, `session:claim-work`, `session:create`, `session:is-alive`, `session:terminate`), agents (`agents:resolve`), conversations (`conversations:get-metadata`, `conversations:store-runner-session`), credentials (already done: `credentials:get`/`resolve:setting`; ADD `credentials:list`, `credentials:list-kinds`). Sandbox `sandbox:open-session` ‚Üí see separate decision (handle-bearing, special-cased). | The card itself says ship the IPC-reachable + security-boundary subset well rather than half-wire the full ~120-hook surface. IPC-reachable set derived from `@ax/ipc-core/handlers/*` `bus.call` sites: session:resolve-token (auth gate), session:get-config, session:claim-work, workspace:read/list, conversations:get-metadata/store-runner-session, plus the workspace bundle hooks (already typed in their own protocol pkg). Tenant-boundary: agents:resolve is the J1 ACL gate every conversations hook chains through. | Full rollout across all ~120 hooks (rejected: card explicitly says ship the subset, defer remainder ‚Äî half-wiring everything risks the strip-by-default trap on many handlers at once); skip non-IPC security hooks (rejected: agents:resolve is the tenant gate, must be in) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: schemas live **co-located in each registering plugin** (next to the I/O interfaces), NOT in a new `@ax/*-protocol` package ‚Äî mirroring the EXISTING credentials precedent (`CredentialsResolveOutputSchema` in `credentials/src/plugin.ts`). Each backend that registers a hook owns its own `returns` schema. For session (two backends `inmemory`/`postgres` register identical hooks), each carries its own copy of the schema, matching how they ALREADY duplicate the I/O interfaces structurally (I2 ‚Äî no cross-plugin import; the drift is the documented boundary cost). | The `returns` schema is a per-registration, in-process, defense-in-depth shape assertion ‚Äî it is NOT an inter-plugin wire contract (that's `@ax/ipc-protocol`, already zod-validated at the untrusted runner‚Üîhost wire). A `*-protocol` package is the right tool when the SHAPE is the shared contract across plugins; here the shape is already pinned by the TS interfaces and the wire schema. Adding a protocol package would be premature abstraction (boundary-review: can't name a second consumer that ISN'T the registering backend). credentials set the precedent; follow it. | Shared `@ax/session-protocol` etc. (rejected: premature ‚Äî no consumer beyond the registering backend; the wire contract already lives in ipc-protocol; would be a bigger surface than the card warrants); schemas in @ax/core (rejected: I1 ‚Äî core stays storage-neutral, and these are per-plugin contracts) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: `sandbox:open-session` gets a **`.passthrough()` schema validating only `runnerEndpoint: z.string().min(1)`**, NOT a strict object schema. The hook's `OpenSessionResult` carries `handle: { kill(): Promise<void>; exited: Promise<ExitInfo> }` ‚Äî live functions + a Promise. A strict zod object schema STRIPS undeclared keys (hook-bus.ts:141-147), which would silently delete `handle` and break the orchestrator's session lifecycle. `.passthrough()` keeps `handle` intact while still asserting the one storage-agnostic serializable field the I1 boundary cares about. | The hook-bus comment explicitly warns: zod object schemas strip undeclared keys by default; declare `returns` as a faithful shape OR add `.passthrough()` for hooks that return extra keys. A handle-bearing hook is exactly the `.passthrough()` case. Validating `runnerEndpoint` still catches a backend that forgets to set the opaque URI (the field that crosses the I1 boundary). | Strict `z.object({runnerEndpoint})` (rejected: strips `handle` ‚Üí breaks lifecycle ‚Äî the strip-by-default trap); `z.custom()` no-op (rejected: validates nothing, defeats the point); skip sandbox entirely (rejected: it's a named security-boundary surface in the card) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: handle the strip-by-default trap GLOBALLY by auditing every in-scope hook's output for non-data fields (functions / Promises / Date / branded strings / Uint8Array) before writing its schema. Branded `WorkspaceVersion` ‚Üí `z.string()` (brand is compile-time only). `Date` ‚Üí `z.date()`. `Uint8Array` ‚Üí `z.instanceof(Uint8Array)`. Lazy `contentBefore?/contentAfter?: () => Promise<Bytes>` on `WorkspaceChange` (in `workspace:apply`/`diff` delta) ‚Üí schema must NOT include them as data OR must `.passthrough()` the change objects, else the lazy fns get stripped and subscribers lose content access. | This is THE correctness risk of the whole task ‚Äî a `returns` schema that strips a load-bearing field is worse than no schema (silent data loss vs. honest TS-only). Each schema is paired with a drift-guard test (round-trip a fully-populated interface value through `.parse`, assert `toEqual`) per the credentials `return-schemas.test.ts` precedent ‚Äî that test FAILS if the schema strips any field. | Trust hand-written schemas without round-trip guards (rejected: the credentials precedent added the guard for exactly this reason; a stripped field is invisible without it); use `.passthrough()` everywhere (rejected: defeats the shape assertion ‚Äî only use it where a live non-data field genuinely rides the result, e.g. sandbox handle) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-6: REVISE scope ‚Äî workspace `returns` schemas cover ONLY the IPC-reachable, clean-data hooks `workspace:read` + `workspace:list`. DEFER `workspace:apply` and `workspace:diff` to a follow-up. | `WorkspaceApplyOutput`/`WorkspaceDiffOutput` carry `delta.changes[].contentBefore?/contentAfter?: () => Promise<Bytes>` ‚Äî lazy functions. A strict zod object schema strips them (hook-bus strip-by-default), which (a) breaks `@ax/test-harness/workspace-contract.ts:145-154` (`expect(typeof ch.contentAfter).toBe('function')`) and (b) silently severs `@ax/routines/sync.ts:82`'s `change.contentAfter` content access. Validating apply/diff correctly needs the change objects `.passthrough()`-ed AND the contract test re-confirmed across BOTH the git backend and the mock ‚Äî a focused follow-up, not a rushed add here. read/list return plain `{found,bytes,version?}` / `{paths}` ‚Äî no lazy fields, safe to schema now. | Schema apply/diff with `.passthrough()` on changes now (rejected: needs coordinated contract-test verification across backends + risks the strip trap on a security-critical write path under time pressure ‚Äî exactly the "ship the subset well, defer the rest" case the card calls for); skip workspace entirely (rejected: read/list ARE IPC-reachable + safe) |

## ARCH-12 ‚Äî returns schemas for workspace:apply + workspace:diff (lazy-fn delta) (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: schemas (`WorkspaceDeltaSchema`, `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema`, `WorkspaceDiffOutputSchema`) live in `@ax/core/workspace.ts` next to the ARCH-6 read/list schemas. The `changes[]` element schema uses `z.object({ path: z.string(), kind: z.enum([...]) }).passthrough()`. | Verified empirically (zod 3.25.76): `.passthrough()` keeps function-valued keys by **reference identity** ‚Äî `parsed.contentAfter === fn` is true, both as a bare object and inside `z.array(...)`. So the lazy `contentBefore?/contentAfter?` survive `.parse()` untouched (no wrapping, not stripped). Validating `path`+`kind` still catches a backend that emits a malformed change. The branded `WorkspaceVersion` (`before`/`after`) ‚Üí `z.string()`, `before` nullable; `reason?`‚Üí`z.string().optional()`; `author?`‚Üí`z.object({...}).optional()`. The shapes already live in core (storage-neutral, `WorkspaceVersion` is a compile-time brand), so this follows the ARCH-6 read/list precedent of co-locating in core ‚Äî NOT a `*-protocol` pkg (no consumer beyond the registering backend). | Declare `contentBefore/contentAfter` as `z.function().optional()` (rejected: zod can wrap/coerce functions and may choke on absent-vs-undefined; passthrough identity is safer + simpler); strict object on changes (rejected: strips the lazy fns ‚Äî the exact ARCH-6-deferred trap) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: attach `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema` at the **`@ax/core` facade** (`registerWorkspaceApplyFacade`), NOT at the three backend `workspace:apply-internal` sites. Attach `WorkspaceDiffOutputSchema` at each backend's `workspace:diff` registration (git-core, git-server-client, mock) ‚Äî diff has no facade. | `workspace:apply` IS the facade; it returns the internal's result unchanged, so validating once at the facade covers all backends (one source of truth, I4) and the public hook is what callers + IPC see. `apply-internal` is backend-private; double-validating there is redundant churn. `workspace:diff` has no facade, so its schema rides each of the 3 direct registrations (matching how read/list already attach per-backend). | Attach apply schema at all 3 `apply-internal` sites (rejected: redundant ‚Äî facade already validates the identical output; 3√ó the edit surface for no extra coverage); skip the facade and only validate internal (rejected: the public hook is the IPC-reachable + security-boundary surface the card names) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12 (Codex P2 fix): validate the `workspace:apply` output INSIDE the facade with `WorkspaceApplyOutputSchema.safeParse` BEFORE firing `workspace:applied`, throwing `invalid-return` on failure ‚Äî do NOT rely on the service-hook `{ returns }` option for this hook. Fire/return the ORIGINAL `applied` object (validation is a gate, not a transform). | The `{ returns }` option is enforced by `HookBus.call` only AFTER the handler returns, but the facade handler fires `workspace:applied(applied.delta)` from inside itself ‚Äî so a malformed backend delta would reach observe-only subscribers (e.g. `@ax/routines` sync `change.contentAfter`) BEFORE `invalid-return` is raised. On a security-critical write path that defeats the point. Validating up front makes the facade the unbypassable chokepoint for both the subscriber boundary and the caller. Using the original object (not zod's reparsed `parsed.data`) preserves reference identity that subscribers + the `applied`-fires-the-same-delta test (e) rely on, and keeps the lazy `contentBefore/contentAfter` fns by reference. Regression tests (f2)/(f3) in `workspace-apply-facade.test.ts`. | Keep `{ returns }` on the facade registration (rejected: validates too late ‚Äî after `applied` already fired; that's the bug); move schema to `apply-internal` (rejected: still leaves the facade's public output ungated against the `applied` fire, and the schema's home stays at the facade per the prior decision); fire `parsed.data` (rejected: breaks reference identity test (e) + needlessly clones the delta) |
| 2026-05-24 | ARCH-12: drift guards live in `packages/core/src/__tests__/workspace-return-schemas.test.ts` (extend the ARCH-6 file: round-trip a fully-populated `WorkspaceApplyOutput`/`WorkspaceDiffOutput` incl. live `contentBefore`/`contentAfter` fns + assert the fn refs survive `.parse`). PLUS re-confirm the existing cross-backend contract assertion (`workspace-contract.ts:145` `typeof ch.contentAfter === 'function'`) still passes once the live `workspace:apply`/`diff` calls route through the now-schema'd facade/registration ‚Äî that contract suite already runs against BOTH the mock AND `@ax/workspace-git` backends, so it IS the both-backends drift guard the card asks for. | The card explicitly requires `workspace-contract.ts` re-verification across the git backend AND the mock. The contract suite is already parameterized over backends (`runWorkspaceContract(label, makePlugin)`), and its `contentAfter is lazy` test exercises a real `workspace:apply` through the bus ‚Äî so once the schema is attached, a green contract run on both backends IS the proof the schema didn't strip the fns end-to-end. The core unit round-trip is the fast/targeted guard; the contract run is the integration guard. | Add a brand-new both-backends test file (rejected: the existing contract suite already covers both backends through the bus ‚Äî duplicating it is redundant); only the core unit round-trip (rejected: doesn't prove the *attached* schema survives a real bus call, which is the security-critical path) |

## TASK-7 ‚Äî parallel-agent memory race (2026-05-24)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-24 | TASK-7: fix the parallel-agent memory race with **approach (a) ‚Äî standardize that agents write+commit `.claude/memory/` ONLY to their own worktree/branch copy, NEVER the shared main checkout** ‚Äî NOT approach (b) a lock. | (1) Memory is now COMMITTED (decision 83) so a branch-copy write lands on merge like every other file; (2) yolo-ship Phase 0 already REQUIRES a per-agent worktree, so the branch copy is the natural race-free write target; (3) the worktree copy is NO LONGER empty ‚Äî `git worktree add origin/main` carries the *tracked* `.claude/memory/` in (confirmed: worktree decisions.md = 100 lines), obsoleting the old "write to main checkout, worktree is empty" rationale (decisions 48/55/60/67/73); (4) a lock is exactly the heavy orchestration shape v2 avoids and doesn't even fix the deeper race ‚Äî last-writer-wins on `git commit` HEAD in a shared checkout still stomps; the serialized merge queue + `git pull --ff-only` already serialize landing, and divergent memory rows become a visible git merge conflict, not a silent drop. | (b) serialize main-checkout writes behind a lock (rejected: adds acquire/release/stale-recovery infra, doesn't address shared-checkout HEAD races, contradicts v2's no-heavy-orchestration ethos); keep the contradictory status quo (rejected: that IS the bug ‚Äî decisions 48/55/60/67/73 say "main checkout", ARCH-3 decision 89 says "branch copy", agents race) |
| 2026-05-24 | TASK-7: deliverable = **convention change** (CLAUDE.md "Codex Memory Bootstrap" + claude-memory skill: write/commit memory in the worktree branch copy, never the shared main checkout) PLUS a **lightweight, fully-wired, tested helper** the convention tells agents to use: `scripts/memory-write-target.sh` prints the correct `.claude/memory/` dir for the current cwd ‚Äî the linked-worktree's own copy when run inside one, else the primary copy ‚Äî using `git rev-parse --git-common-dir`/`--git-dir`/`--show-toplevel`. The convention's "write memory here" step calls it, giving it a real caller (not half-wired); a vitest test exercises both the primary-tree and linked-worktree branches in temp git repos. | The card asks for convention + a guard "if feasible, lightweight + testable; don't half-wire". A pre-commit BLOCK is the wrong shape: no husky infra here, it's bypassable, and it'd mis-fire on a legit solo human editing memory on main. An ESLint rule lints source ASTs, not fs/git location. A path-resolver helper IS the feasible, testable, genuinely-wired form ‚Äî it has a real caller (the documented memory-write step), is exercised by a hermetic vitest test (create a temp repo + a linked worktree, assert the resolved path), and *positively guides* agents to the branch copy instead of negatively blocking. | (a) pre-commit husky hook that blocks main-checkout memory writes (rejected: no husky, bypassable, mis-fires on legit human main edits, can't tell "agent" from "human"); (b) ESLint rule (rejected: wrong tool ‚Äî fs/git location isn't a source AST); (c) CI lane that fails on any `.claude/memory/**` diff (rejected: INCOHERENT ‚Äî committing memory to the branch copy IS the desired behavior); (d) convention-only, no helper (acceptable fallback per the card; rejected here only because the resolver IS cleanly testable + wired, clearing the card's bar) |

## 2026-05-25 ‚Äî ARCH-11: shared golden-vectors drift test for MCP validators (no cross-import)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Date | 2026-05-25 |
| Decision | Detect drift between the runner's hand-rolled `validateMcpEntry` (`packages/agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/installed-skills.ts`) and `@ax/sandbox-protocol`'s `McpServerSchema` via a single shared JSON fixture of golden vectors, asserted by TWO independent test suites ‚Äî one in each package ‚Äî both reading the same fixture file. A divergence (one validator accepts what the other rejects) fails one suite ‚Üí CI red. |
| Rationale | The CRITICAL INVARIANT (and the ARCH-5 design intent) is that the runner stays independent of the host contract package: NO `@ax/sandbox-protocol` import (not even devDependency) in the runner, so the sandbox-side re-validation is genuine defense-in-depth, not a thin wrapper. A shared JSON fixture is data, not code ‚Äî neither package imports the other. Each side reads the fixture via `join(__dirname,'..','..','..','..',<path>)` (the idiomatic worktree-safe repo-root pattern from cli/e2e.test.ts), then maps its own validator over the vectors. |
| Alternatives | (a) Have the runner import McpServerSchema and delegate ‚Äî REJECTED, destroys the independence that is the whole point. (b) Cross-reference comment only ‚Äî REJECTED by dispatch: a comment doesn't *detect* drift. (c) Put the drift test in one package importing the other's validator ‚Äî REJECTED: sandbox-protocol is a pure zod package, pulling in the runner (with its SDK dep) reverses+bloats the dep graph; and importing the schema into the runner-side test re-creates the forbidden coupling. Two-sided fixture is the only shape with zero cross-import. |
| Fixture home | `packages/sandbox-protocol/src/__tests__/fixtures/mcp-server-golden-vectors.json` ‚Äî sandbox-protocol OWNS the canonical schema, so the canonical vectors live with it. The runner-side test reaches it read-only via repo-root-relative path (no package dep). |
| Scope of vectors | Only the security-relevant fields BOTH validators enforce: name regex, transport enum, command presence/non-empty, args max(32)/len(256), env Record<string,string> shape + size caps, url validity, and the stdio/http transport refine (cross-contamination). EXCLUDED: cases hinging purely on `allowedHosts`/`credentials` ‚Äî the runner intentionally ignores those (it only emits name/transport/command/args/env/url into .mcp.json), so they are a KNOWN, documented benign divergence, not drift. Each vector is normalized to drop allowedHosts/credentials before the runner sees it, OR the runner-side harness ignores them (the runner already does). |
| Known benign divergence | runner `validateMcpEntry` does not look at `allowedHosts`/`credentials`; `McpServerSchema` defaults+validates them. Documented inline in both the fixture header and a cross-reference comment on `validateMcpEntry`. |

### 2026-05-25 ‚Äî ARCH-11 follow-on: assertion SEMANTICS (runner may be stricter; symmetric on the security-critical core)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Decision | Each golden vector declares its expected verdict per side: `schema: 'accept'|'reject'` and `runner: 'accept'|'reject'`. The test asserts BOTH sides match their declared verdict. This models the legitimate asymmetry (runner = defense-in-depth, allowed to be a strict-superset rejecter) WITHOUT letting silent drift hide: any future change to either validator that flips a verdict breaks the test, forcing a conscious fixture update + cross-reference review. A `sameVerdict` invariant subset (the security-critical shape rules: name regex, transport enum, transport refine, command presence, url validity, args caps) is additionally asserted to be IDENTICAL on both sides ‚Äî those MUST never diverge; only the env entry-count/length caps are runner-stricter-by-design. |
| Rationale | Found a real today-divergence: runner caps env to ‚â§32 entries and ‚â§256-char keys/values; `McpServerSchema` (`z.record(z.string(), z.string())`) caps neither. The dangerous direction is "schema accepts, runner accepts, but it's malicious" ‚Äî the runner is the LAST gate, so runner-stricter is the safe direction and must be allowed. The unsafe direction is "schema rejects but runner accepts" (a hole past the last gate) ‚Äî vectors with `schema:'reject', runner:'accept'` are the ones we never want to exist; the test would surface any. |
| Decision on the env-cap gap | Do NOT "fix" it by loosening the runner or tightening the schema in THIS card (scope = drift DETECTION, per dispatch). Encode the current reality in the vectors (env-oversize: `schema:'accept', runner:'reject'`) + a documented note, and return "tighten McpServerSchema env caps to match runner (‚â§32 entries, ‚â§256 key/val)" as a deferred follow-up for auto-ship to file. Tightening the schema is the right eventual fix (host should reject early) but it changes the host contract + needs its own boundary review. |
| Human-owned? | No ‚Äî resolvable from code + the documented defense-in-depth design intent. Not escalating. |

### 2026-05-25 ‚Äî ARCH-11 codex review [P2]: runner drift half invisible to PR affected-package selection ‚Äî FIXED

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Finding | codex exec review --base main: the runner-side drift test reads the sandbox-protocol fixture by hard-coded path, so there's NO pnpm dependency edge runner‚Üísandbox-protocol (by design). CI's PR test selection is `pnpm --filter "...[$BASE_SHA]"` (affected + dependents). A PR touching ONLY packages/sandbox-protocol (fixture or schema) therefore would NOT select the runner ‚Üí the runner half of the drift guard wouldn't run on the PR, only post-merge on main's full suite. A drift-introducing fixture edit could pass the PR. |
| Verdict | VALID (verified against .github/workflows/ci.yml lines 32-45). Accepted + fixed in this PR. |
| Fix | In the PR test step, detect `git diff --name-only "$BASE_SHA"...HEAD | grep -Eq '^packages/sandbox-protocol/'` and, when matched, append `--filter @ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner` (built as a bash ARRAY to avoid shellcheck SC2086) to BOTH the affected-package list-probe and the run. actionlint-clean. The symmetric case (runner-only change) is already covered: `...[SHA]` selects the runner so its drift test runs; the schema didn't change so the schema-side test can't newly fail. |
| Why not a dep edge or root-script test | A dep edge would re-create the forbidden coupling (defeats the whole card). A root `scripts/` test would need to import/build both packages from a third location, widening reach. A path-scoped CI inclusion keeps the fix entirely in CI config ‚Äî zero production-code or dependency-graph change ‚Äî and is the project's established pattern (see helm-render / image-build path-scoped lanes in the same workflow). |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 (Faults B/D ‚Äî host bounce / network drop ‚Üí silent finalize): fix the `@ax/channel-web` client's `done`-less SSE close so it no longer synthesizes a `finish` (`finishReason:'stop'`) that looks like a successful turn. Instead: (1) transport's `processResponseStream` `flush()` (the no-`done`-frame branch) emits an AI-SDK `error` UIMessageChunk whose `errorText` is a NEW shared sentinel `CONNECTION_LOST` (`'Connection lost. Retrying‚Ä¶'`-class wording), exported from `transport.ts`; (2) the runtime's `onError` (runtime.tsx) tracks a per-turn retry count in a ref ‚Äî on the FIRST connection-lost error it SILENTLY retries via `regenerate()` (sets the agent-status row to a transient working "Connection lost ‚Äî retrying‚Ä¶" label, NO error banner), and on a SECOND failure (or any non-connection-lost error) it falls through to the existing `applyTurnError` error banner + retry affordance. Distinguish connection-lost from orchestrator `error`-frame errors by matching `error.message === CONNECTION_LOST`. Reuses the existing AgentStatus row (error mode = red dot + retry button; working mode = "Connection lost ‚Äî retrying‚Ä¶") ‚Äî NO new shadcn primitives. | The task scopes this as a transport-`flush()` concern, NOT an orchestrator-terminated-outcome (Fault A/F2b, already handled by the `error`-frame path). Root cause confirmed in code: `transport.ts` flush (lines 570-578) enqueues `{type:'finish',finishReason:'stop'}` on a `done`-less close, indistinguishable from success ‚Äî so a host bounce (Fault B, process dies ‚Üí in-memory chunk-buffer gone ‚Üí reqId 404 on reconnect) or network drop (Fault D, TCP severed ‚Üí no `done`/`error` frame ever arrives) silently finalizes a half-streamed turn. In-transport SSE re-open of the SAME reqId is NOT viable: the server's chunk-buffer (`chunk-buffer.ts`) replays the FULL tail on reconnect (‚Üí duplicate text) AND is replica-local with a 60s TTL that's wiped by a host bounce (‚Üí 404). So the robust silent-retry primitive is the runtime's existing `regenerate()` (re-POSTs the last user turn ‚Üí fresh reqId ‚Üí fresh sandbox ‚Üí re-answers), which `applyTurnError`'s retry already uses. The sentinel is an INTERNAL `@ax/channel-web` contract (not a hook payload) shared exactly like the existing `DEFAULT_TURN_ERROR` between transport.ts + turn-error.ts ‚Äî no I1/I2 violation. | (a) silent retry INSIDE the transport by re-GETting the same reqId (rejected: buffer-replay duplicates already-rendered text + host bounce 404s the reqId ‚Äî unreliable); (b) just emit the SAME error banner immediately on done-less close, no silent retry (rejected: task explicitly wants "silent retry first, THEN banner"); (c) a custom Error subclass to type the retryable error (rejected: the AI-SDK reconstructs a PLAIN `Error` from the chunk's `errorText`, so a subclass doesn't survive to `onError` ‚Äî match on the message sentinel instead); (d) infinite silent retries (rejected: a persistent outage would loop forever ‚Äî cap at one silent retry, then surface the banner) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex review (2 P2 findings, both ACCEPTED + fixed against verified AI-SDK source): (1) **defer the silent `regenerate()`** ‚Äî the AI SDK (`ai@6` `chat.ts` `makeRequest`) calls `onError` INSIDE the failed request's `catch` (line 753), BEFORE the `finally` (758-773) sets `this.activeResponse = undefined`. A SYNCHRONOUS `regenerate()` from `onError` re-enters `makeRequest`, sets a NEW `activeResponse`, then the ORIGINAL request's finally nukes it ‚Üí the retry loses its abort handle and its `onFinish` throws on `this.activeResponse!` (undefined) ‚Üí `silentRetriedRef` never resets. Fix: wrap the silent `regenerate()` in `setTimeout(‚Ä¶,0)` so the failed request fully unwinds first (the manual banner-retry needs no defer ‚Äî it's already outside the request lifecycle). (2) **hard network drop wasn't covered** ‚Äî the transport `flush()` only fires on a GRACEFUL body close; a real mid-turn fetch drop (Fault D) ERRORS the fetch-body ReadableStream, SKIPS the TransformStream flush, and the AI SDK surfaces the raw fetch `TypeError` to onError (it even flags `isDisconnect` via the same heuristic). So the original diff showed the banner immediately on a true network drop instead of silently retrying. Fix: broaden `isConnectionLost` (turn-error.ts) to ALSO match a `TypeError` whose message includes "fetch"/"network" (mirrors the SDK's own `chat.ts` disconnect heuristic) ‚Äî covering BOTH the graceful done-less close (CONNECTION_LOST sentinel) and the hard drop. Added 4 unit tests (Bug Fix Policy) pinning the fetch/network-TypeError silent-retry + the second-failure‚Üíbanner + unrelated-TypeError‚Üíbanner negative. | Both findings are dead-on and go to the CORE behavior the card demands (silent retry on a genuine network drop; a clean retry lifecycle). Verified each by reading `ai@6` `node_modules/ai/src/ui/chat.ts`: the catch‚Üífinally ordering (1) and the `TypeError`+`includes('fetch'/'network')`‚Üí`isDisconnect` path (744-751) that bypasses our flush (2). Codex is a colleague ‚Äî I confirmed against source rather than deferring blindly, and the AI-SDK heuristic is exactly the one I mirror. | (1) alt: `queueMicrotask` instead of `setTimeout` (rejected: a microtask still runs within the same async continuation as the awaited rejection's finally on some engines; `setTimeout(0)` macrotask guarantees the finally's `activeResponse=undefined` has executed). | 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 2 (1 P2, ACCEPTED + fixed): the silent-retry one-shot cap LEAKED ACROSS TURNS. A `silentRetriedRef` boolean reset only on a clean `onFinish` or a manual banner click ‚Äî so after a connection-lost turn spent its retry AND the retry also failed (both onFinish calls carry error/disconnect flags ‚Üí no reset), the ref stayed `true`; if the user then SUBMITTED A DIFFERENT message instead of clicking the banner, that fresh turn's first drop saw `isFirstFailure=false` and went straight to the banner, skipping its own silent retry. Dropped the `onFinish` handler entirely (the per-turn key makes it redundant). | 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 3 (2 P2, both ACCEPTED + fixed): (A) **non-idempotent silent replay** ‚Äî broadening `isConnectionLost` to match any fetch/network `TypeError` (round-1 fix #2) was TOO broad: a `TypeError('Failed to fetch')` can come from the non-idempotent `POST /api/chat/messages` or the initial `GET /api/chat/stream/:reqId` ‚Äî BOTH run in `sendMessages` BEFORE a stream is returned. Moving the mid-stream-error‚Üísentinel conversion INTO the transport is the right boundary: the transport alone knows whether the stream was established (= safe to retry the already-started turn) vs failed at request time (= unsafe). | 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 4 (1 P1, ACCEPTED ‚Äî fundamental rework): an automatic `regenerate()` on a CLIENT-SIDE mid-stream drop DUPLICATES a live server turn. Verified against the server: a client SSE disconnect only triggers `stream.onClose`‚Üí`cleanup()` which UNSUBSCRIBES the per-connection bus subscribers (sse.ts:196) ‚Äî it does NOT terminate the runner or evict the reqId buffer (eviction is turn-end/turn-error/60s-TTL only). And every `POST /api/chat/messages` MINTS A NEW reqId + dispatches a fresh `agent:invoke` (routes-chat.ts:51-55) ‚Äî `regenerate()` re-POSTs, so on a Fault-D network drop (host fine, turn still running) it queues a DUPLICATE prompt + duplicate tool side-effects while the original turn finishes. **Rework:** move the silent retry OUT of the runtime's regenerate and INTO the transport as a same-reqId RECONNECT loop. `sendMessages` POSTs ONCE (one reqId, one agent:invoke ever), then returns a single continuous outer `ReadableStream` whose `start` loops: GET `/stream/:reqId`, parse one attempt; a terminal `done`‚Üífinish or server `error` frame closes the outer stream; a NON-terminal end (graceful done-less close OR hard body error) RECONNECTS by re-GETting the SAME reqId (the server is purpose-built to replay the buffer tail ‚Äî sse.ts:214-238) ‚Äî NO new POST, so it can NEVER duplicate the turn. To avoid double-rendering the replayed tail, the transport tracks `emittedContent` count and SKIPS that many content chunks on each reconnect attempt. Bounded at `MAX_RECONNECTS` attempts; when the GET 404s (Fault B host bounce ‚Äî reqId+buffer gone) or the cap is exhausted, emit the CONNECTION_LOST `error` chunk ‚Üí the runtime surfaces the BANNER with a manual-retry (regenerate) affordance. The runtime's onError NO LONGER does a silent regenerate at all ‚Äî silent recovery is 100% transport-side reconnect (idempotent); the banner's manual retry (a deliberate user action) is the only path that re-POSTs. | Codex's P1 is correct and decisive ‚Äî the regenerate-based silent retry was unsafe for the exact Fault D the card names. Considered escalating to the human (the "silent retry" requirement vs the no-duplication correctness constraint is a genuine tension given the POST-always-creates-a-new-turn server contract), but it's self-answerable: the correct primitive is reconnect-to-same-reqId (GET-only, idempotent), which the server already supports, and it honors BOTH the requirement (silent retry first) AND correctness (no duplicate turn). Rejected AI-SDK `resumeStream()`/`reconnectToStream`: on resume it mints a NEW message id (ai@6 chat.ts makeRequest) ‚Üí pushes a SECOND assistant bubble and replays the full buffer into it (duplicate visible answer), and `reconnectToStream` isn't handed the reqId. | 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 5 (3 P2 in the new reconnect logic, all ACCEPTED + fixed): (A) **abort treated as connection-loss** ‚Äî on user-Stop/teardown the AI SDK aborts the fetch; the body read rejects ‚Üí `consumeSseAttempt` returns 'lost' ‚Üí my `abortSignal?.aborted` branch emitted CONNECTION_LOST = a spurious retry banner for an intentional cancel. (B) **stale carry corrupts reconnect** ‚Äî `ctx.carry` retains a partial `data:` line stranded by a mid-line drop; the reconnect reuses the same ctx, so the replayed buffer's first frame gets prefixed with the stale fragment ‚Üí JSON parse fails ‚Üí a frame dropped. Fix: `ctx.carry=''` on every reconnect (alongside the skipContent reset). (C) **over-skip past the replay window** ‚Äî the server ring buffer retains only its last ~256 chunks; once `emittedContent` exceeds that, a reconnect's PARTIAL replay can't be count-deduped (skipping the full lifetime count eats live chunks = silent loss). | 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 7 (1 P2, ACCEPTED ‚Äî confirms count-dedup is fundamentally unsound; final design): the round-5 `emittedContent <= SERVER_REPLAY_WINDOW(200)` guard checks the WRONG quantity. The real hazard is the SERVER outrunning its 256-chunk ring buffer WHILE THE CLIENT IS DISCONNECTED: client emitted e.g. 50 chunks (emittedContent=50, under the guard), but during the disconnect the agent streamed to 400 ‚Üí the buffer now holds chunks 144‚Äì400 (0‚Äì143 evicted). On reconnect the replay tail starts at #144, NOT #51 ‚Äî `skipContent=50` skips 144‚Äì193 and the client NEVER sees 51‚Äì193 (silent loss). The client CANNOT detect this without a per-chunk sequence number the wire doesn't carry. **Final resolution: gate silent reconnect on `emittedContent === 0` (PRE-CONTENT only).** Before any content streams, the replay is necessarily complete-from-the-start, dedup is a no-op, and silent recovery is loss-free ‚Äî this covers the common "blip before the first token" case (sandbox-starting, proxy idle-cull, tab refocus). Once ANY content has streamed, a drop surfaces the CONNECTION_LOST banner (manual retry) instead of risking a lossy resume. Removed the now-dead `skipContent` field + the per-frame skip-gate + `SERVER_REPLAY_WINDOW` (Half-Wired Code Policy ‚Äî no longer reachable). Rewrote the reconnect tests to the new semantics (pre-content drop ‚Üí silent resume incl. hard body error; content-then-drop ‚Üí banner no-reconnect; 404 ‚Üí banner; cap; abort variants). Net 522 channel-web green. The pre-content gate is the maximal SAFE silent-retry slice; it still delivers the task's "silent retry first" for the most common blip and degrades to the required "error banner with retry" once content is in flight. This is a defensible scope line: the loss-free silent recovery ships now; the mid-content resume needs a server wire change (sequence number) that's out of this client-side card's framed scope ‚Üí tracked as a follow-up rather than silently shipping a lossy resume or unilaterally expanding scope. | (a) banner-only, no silent reconnect at all (rejected: drops the "silent retry first" requirement even for the safe pre-content case); (b) ship count-dedup accepting rare silent loss (rejected: silent data loss is non-negotiable here); (c) expand THIS card to add the server sequence number (rejected: card is framed as a client-side transport flush concern, not an SSE wire-protocol change ‚Äî file as follow-up); (d) escalate to human as blocked (considered ‚Äî the requirement-vs-correctness tension is real ‚Äî but self-answerable: the pre-content gate is the unambiguously-correct safe subset that honors the hard requirement (no silent finalize + banner+retry) AND a meaningful slice of the soft one (silent retry for the common blip), with the residual tracked) |
| 2026-05-25 | FAULTA-5 Phase-5 Codex round 8 (1 P2, ACCEPTED ‚Äî collapses to the simplest correct design): even the round-7 PRE-CONTENT-only reconnect can silently lose output. | 2026-05-25 | TASK-23: SSE per-chunk seq for loss-free silent turn-resume (FAULTA-5 follow-up). seq is assigned by channel-web's `ChunkBuffer` (the replica-local per-reqId stateful structure that already owns the chunk ring), NOT in ipc-core's `fireEventStreamChunk` and NOT on the `@ax/ipc-protocol` `EventStreamChunkSchema` IPC wire. `ChunkBuffer.append` mints the next per-reqId monotonic int (1-based) and stores it on the buffered frame; the buffer-fill subscriber stamps it onto the outgoing `chat:stream-chunk` payload by RETURNING the seq-stamped payload (bus contract `result!==undefined ‚Üí current=result`, NOT an implicit mutation) so the per-connection live SSE subscriber and `tail()` replay both carry the SAME seq. `SseFrame` content variants gain an optional `seq: number`. The buffer is already per-reqId, replica-local (J7), TTL-evicted ‚Äî the natural monotonic authority. Host assigns (not runner) so untrusted runner content never controls the dedup cursor (I5). seq is a plain monotonic int = transport/storage-agnostic (I1, no git/sqlite/k8s vocab). | 2026-05-25 | TASK-23 (Codex review rounds, 4 findings, all fixed): (P1) the channel-web ChunkBuffer's IDLE_TTL sweep used to fully `map.delete` a still-live reqId entry that went quiet > 60s mid-turn (e.g. a long tool call); the next live chunk recreated it at seq 1, and a still-connected client with lastSeq>0 silently DEDUPED (dropped) it ‚Äî the exact loss seq exists to prevent. Fix: sweep now reclaims the heavy fields (chunks/phase) into a lightweight cursor-only SHELL but keeps `nextSeq` monotonic; only `evictReqId` (real turn-end/turn-error) resets the cursor. (P2a) client used to accept ANY first seq as a baseline ‚Äî a first frame at seq 257 (256-cap dropped the head before connect) rendered the tail as a complete answer, silently omitting 1..256. Fix: servers mint from 1, so a FIRST seq-bearing content frame > 1 ‚áí truncated head ‚áí CONNECTION_LOST (not silent render). (P2b) a content turn ending via chat:turn-error with NO SSE listener stored the error but no evictor ran; the reclaim path would keep its dead cursor shell forever. Fix: sweep FULLY deletes any entry holding a terminal turnError (cursor dead ‚Äî no chunks follow a turn-error) before the reclaimed-shell check. (P2c) an orphaned shell (runner crashed before any terminal hook) leaked one map entry each. Fix: reap a reclaimed shell once it ages past a ceiling. (P2d) the client's locally-detected seq-gap return('lost') left the fetch body OPEN (finally only releaseLock'd) ‚Äî the server kept per-connection subscribers/writes alive until turn-end/timeout. Fix: reader.cancel() (propagates upstream to the HTTP body) before returning, and skip the now-redundant releaseLock. (P2-round2) the fixed 15-min shell ceiling sits BELOW an operator-raised AX_CHAT_TIMEOUT_MS ‚Äî a legit quiet turn past 15 min would get its cursor reaped ‚Üí seq reset ‚Üí silent loss. Fix: ChunkBufferOptions.shellMaxAgeMs is configurable; ChannelWebServerConfig.chatTimeoutMs (sizing hint, NOT a 2nd source of truth ‚Äî orchestrator owns the timeout) ‚Üí shellMaxAgeMs = chatTimeoutMs + 5min slack; preset/k8s passes orchestratorCfg.chatTimeoutMs (covers CLI `serve` too via createK8sPlugins). | Codex is a colleague: each finding was verified against the code before fixing (the P1/P2b/P2c interplay is real ‚Äî the reclaim shell I added for P1 created the P2b/P2c leak surfaces, which the subsequent rounds tightened). All fixes are test-first (Bug Fix Policy): chunk-buffer.test.ts gained cursor-monotonic-across-sweep, evict-resets-after-sweep, turn-error-full-reap, orphan-reap-after-ceiling, configurable-ceiling; transport.test.ts gained first-frame>1‚Üíbanner, gap‚Üícancel-body. | Per-finding alternatives rejected: (P1) "surface reset as connection loss" ‚Äî buffer can't see live connections, so keep the cursor instead; (P2b) keep the shell + reap later ‚Äî wrong, a turn-error turn is terminated so its cursor is dead, full delete is correct; (P2c) unbounded shells ‚Äî rejected (leak); (P2-round2) hardcode a bigger fixed ceiling ‚Äî rejected (still breaks for an even-larger operator timeout; configurable+derived is the only correct fix that stays above the max live turn for ANY configured timeout) |

## 2026-05-25 ‚Äî TASK-25: npm binary-download egress (docs + actionable error)

## 2026-05-25 ‚Äî TASK-26: no-TTY CLI stdout (env-hints)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-26: TTY-detecting CLIs (cliffy/Deno e.g. @schpet/linear-cli, ink, many Rust/Go tools) emit ZERO stdout in the detached sandbox because the SDK Bash tool's child has no controlling TTY. Fix = ENV-HINT route (NOT a pty): a new pure helper `buildTtyHintEnv()` in `@ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner` returning `{ TERM:'xterm-256color', COLUMNS:'120', LINES:'40', FORCE_COLOR:'1', CI:'1' }`, spread into the SDK `query({options:{env}})` literal in main.ts FIRST (before proxyStartup.anthropicEnv) so a real forwarded TERM/COLUMNS from process.env still wins. These flip the common detectors: FORCE_COLOR (chalk/supports-color), TERM+COLUMNS+LINES (cliffy/Deno isTerminal heuristics + width), CI=1 (CI-aware tools choose plain non-interactive writers). | Per the card's explicit scope guidance, prefer env-hints; a pty is ON the table only if hints insufficient AND no significant sandbox-security concern. A pty MEANINGFULLY weakens the boundary (allocating a real `/dev/pts` master+slave for untrusted model-driven Bash adds a kernel-object + ioctl surface, complicates the gVisor/read-only-rootfs k8s pod, and grants the sandboxed process an interactive control channel it doesn't need ‚Äî capability-minimization I5 says no). Env-hints are inert strings, change zero capabilities, and `TERM`/`COLUMNS`/`LINES` are ALREADY in proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST (just never set in the detached host), so the precedent is set. ‚Üí pty TAKEN OFF THE TABLE. | (a) pseudo-TTY for the Bash child (rejected: significant sandbox-boundary cost per above, and env-hints suffice for the targeted class); (b) only FORCE_COLOR (rejected: color isn't the gate ‚Äî the tool emits NOTHING incl plain --help; need TERM+size+CI too); (c) document the limitation only (rejected: card's desired outcome is a CODE FIX that makes tools emit, plus a compat note ‚Äî not docs-only) |
| 2026-05-25 | TASK-26: helper lives in the RUNNER (`@ax/agent-claude-sdk-runner/tty-hint-env.ts`), spread into the single SDK env literal in main.ts ‚Äî NOT in the per-backend sandbox env (sandbox-subprocess open-session.ts / sandbox-k8s pod-spec.ts). | One source of truth (I4): both sandbox backends funnel their session env into the runner, which then builds the SINGLE `query({options:{env}})` env the SDK Bash tool actually inherits (proven by home-bin-env.ts / tool-cache-env.ts living there for exactly this reason ‚Äî the Bash tool is a non-interactive shell that gets PATH only from this literal, no rc sourced). Putting hints in both pod-spec + open-session would duplicate + risk drift; putting them in the runner covers BOTH backends with one edit and matches the existing buildHomeBinEnv/buildToolCacheEnv pattern. SPREAD FIRST (before anthropicEnv) so a genuinely-forwarded TERM/COLUMNS (if the host ever has a TTY) overrides the default ‚Äî defaults are a floor, not a clamp. | (a) set in sandbox-subprocess + sandbox-k8s env (rejected: two edits, drift risk, and those envs feed the RUNNER process not the SDK Bash child directly ‚Äî the runner rebuilds the SDK env from an allowlist, so a TERM set on the runner only reaches the Bash child if it's in ENV_ALLOWLIST AND set, which is the current gap); (b) add FORCE_COLOR/CI to proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST + set them on the sandbox env (rejected: same two-place + allowlist-coupling problem; the runner env literal is the clean single seam) |

## 2026-05-25 ‚Äî TASK-24: Host OOMKill mid-turn silently loses the turn

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-25 | **Root cause (3 cascade points):** (1) the runner's IPC client (`ipc-client.ts`) retries transient errnos (incl ECONNREFUSED) only `maxRetries=5` with 100‚Üí30s-cap backoff = ~3.1s total, far shorter than a host OOMKill+pod-reschedule+boot. (2) After the budget exhausts, `commitNotifyWithResync` catches the throw ‚Üí `kept` ‚Üí turn never committed ‚Üí `conversations:get` = 0 turns. (3) The NEXT `inbox.next()` (`session.next-message` long-poll) also throws the terminal `HostUnavailableError` ‚Üí propagates to `userMessages()` ‚Üí out of SDK `query()` ‚Üí top-level catch ‚Üí `exitCode=1` ‚Üí `terminated`. Both the logged "commit-notify failed" AND the exit-1 are the same too-short retry budget. | The report attributed it to commit-notify alone, but the exit-1 is the inbox poll. Fixing only commit-notify would still crash the runner on the next poll. | ‚Äî |
| 2026-05-25 | **#1 commit-notify resilience: lengthen the IPC client's transient-error retry budget to ~2min (TASK clarification: 2min max), retry/backoff (NOT buffer-and-replay).** Add a per-call `maxElapsedMs` deadline to `ipc-client.ts withRetry` so transient/5xx retries keep going (backoff capped at 30s) until ~120s elapsed, then throw. This single change fixes BOTH the commit-notify drop AND the inbox-poll runner crash, because both go through the same client retry loop. A host OOMKill+restart on kind completes well within 2min, so the turn commits and the poll reconnects ‚Äî runner survives, turn persists. | retry/backoff chosen over buffer-and-replay: the IPC client already has a retry loop; adding a wall-clock deadline is a ~10-line surgical change vs. a whole disk-spool buffer subsystem. Buffer-and-replay would also need idempotency on the host commit-notify (it has it via parentVersion, but spooling adds complexity for no UX gain ‚Äî the user is already waiting on the turn). The 2min bound caps how long a genuinely-dead host hangs the user. | buffer-and-replay (rejected: heavier, no UX win); raise only maxRetries count (rejected: count is a poor proxy for wall-clock; a wall-clock deadline is the right knob for "survive a restart"). |
| 2026-05-25 | **#2 recovery UX: auto-retry the whole turn + show a "session interrupted, retrying" message.** TASK clarification mandates auto-retry (vs FAULTA-5's deliberate manual-retry-only stance). This case differs from FAULTA-5's: here the turn produced **0 committed turns** (nothing persisted, no partial replay hazard) ‚Äî so auto-retrying the whole turn is loss-free and duplicate-free (the server-side history is empty for this turn; `session:terminate` already cleared `active_session_id` so the retry routes to a fresh sandbox). Implement in channel-web transport/runtime: on the CONNECTION_LOST / sandbox-terminated path, auto-invoke `regenerate()` ONCE with an interim "Session interrupted ‚Äî retrying‚Ä¶" status, falling back to the manual-retry banner if the auto-retry also fails. | FAULTA-5's manual-only stance was about mid-stream connection-lost where the server turn was LIVE (duplicate side-effect risk). TASK-24's OOMKill case = turn fully lost, host restarted, fresh sandbox on retry ‚Üí safe to auto-retry. Bounded to ONE auto-retry so a persistently-dead host doesn't loop forever; then manual banner. | keep manual-only (rejected: TASK clarification explicitly wants auto-retry + message); unbounded auto-retry (rejected: infinite loop on a hard-down host). |
| 2026-05-25 | **#3a memory: raise host limit 512Mi‚Üí2048Mi in kind-dev-values.yaml** (TASK clarification). Bump request 128Mi‚Üí256Mi to keep the request/limit ratio sane for the scheduler. | Per TASK clarification. 512Mi was tipped over by one heavy proxy-MITM turn atop the orchestrator. | ‚Äî |
| 2026-05-25 | **#3b proxy buffering caps: (a) cap the plain-HTTP request-body buffer in `handleHTTPRequest` (currently UNBOUNDED `Buffer.concat`) at 16 MiB ‚Üí 413; (b) add write-backpressure on both MITM data pumps (`clientTls.write`/`targetTls.write` ignore the bool return ‚Üí unbounded socket buffer on a slow consumer) by pausing the source socket when write() returns false and resuming on 'drain'.** Builder's-recommendation cap = 16 MiB request body (generous for any legit upload; a multi-GB upload OOMs the 512Mi/2048Mi host otherwise). | The report's case is an HTTPS-MITM *download* (response) ‚Äî the response side already streams chunk-by-chunk but WITHOUT honoring write backpressure, so a slow runner-pod consumer lets chunks pile in the host's socket buffers unbounded. Backpressure is the real per-request buffering cap for the MITM download path. The plain-HTTP request-body concat is a separate unbounded vector worth capping in the same PR. | cap response body size (rejected: a legit large download should succeed, just not OOM ‚Äî backpressure bounds memory without capping size); leave plain-HTTP unbounded (rejected: it's a live OOM vector). |

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Followed the locked impl plan `docs/plans/2026-05-26-jit-per-user-skill-attachment-orchestrator-union-impl.md` verbatim after verifying every code anchor against worktree HEAD (zero drift). | The card says "decisions locked (design ¬ß4 + Appendix); implementation-only" and the plan ships real code for every step. Verifying anchors first (per receiving-code-review discipline) confirmed the orchestrator's exact 1045-1046 anchor, the `buildSkillsHooks`/`buildProxyHooks` test helpers, `TEST_AGENT.id='test-agent'`/userId='test-user', and the canary capture harness ‚Äî so no re-derivation needed. | Alt: re-brainstorm scope ‚Äî rejected, card is implementation-only and the plan's Self-Review already covers spec/placeholder/type/stale-anchor checks.
- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Per-user attachment ownership lives in `@ax/skills` (new `skills_v1_user_attachments` table + `skills:attach-for-user`/`skills:list-user-attachments` hooks), NOT `@ax/agents`. `agent_id` stored as an opaque scoping key (no FK to agents_v1_agents, no agents:resolve validation). | Design ¬ß11.2 names the hooks `skills:*`; @ax/skills already owns the user's private skill world (`skills_v1_user_skills`); agent-global attachments remain @ax/agents' admin-managed config ‚Äî genuinely separate concept (admin-global vs self-serve), so one source of truth per concept (invariant #4). Capabilities minimized: a dangling attachment to a deleted agent simply never resolves at session open. | Alt: store in @ax/agents next to skill_attachments ‚Äî rejected (mixes admin-global with self-serve, and hooks are named skills:*).
- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Three-source union precedence implemented by redefining the orchestrator's single `attachments` list as `[...userAttachments, ...agentGlobal.filter(id not in userAttachedIds)]` ‚Äî per-user FIRST, agent-global same-id copies dropped. | The whole downstream chain (resolve(ownerUserId), the per-attachment credential/host merge loop, defaults filter via explicitIds, installedSkills build) already keys off that one `attachments` list, so per-user > agent-global > default + per-user-binding-wins fall out with no other orchestrator change. Content override (user-scoped skill content wins) is already handled by skills:resolve(ownerUserId) mergeUserWins. | Alt: a separate merge pass post-resolve ‚Äî rejected, more code + duplicates the existing slot-owner logic.

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | Accepted Codex P1: `skills:list-user-attachments` read failure now FAILS CLOSED (terminate turn, reason `user-attachments-failed`) instead of fail-open (`[]`). | The read is credential-bearing ‚Äî it decides which credential refs reach `proxy:open-session` and the per-user > agent-global precedence. Fail-open could silently spawn a session with the admin's agent-global ref for a slot the user activated a per-user override on (a credential the user never chose). This matches the `skills:resolve` fail-closed precedent in the SAME orchestrator function; the impl plan's original "throws non-fatal ‚Üí []" copied the wrong sibling (`skills:list-defaults`, which is fail-open ONLY because defaults are instruction-only and can't carry credentials). Added a regression test (orchestrator.test.ts: thrown list-user-attachments ‚Üí terminated + proxy never opened). | Alt: keep fail-open per the plan ‚Äî rejected, it's a credential-confusion bug; availability cost of fail-closed is acceptable (a per-user read fault would likely fail the subsequent skills:resolve too).

- `2026-05-26` (TASK-33) | REJECTED Codex P2 ("don't register skills:attach-for-user before its caller ‚Äî half-wired"). | The half-wired write window is an EXPLICIT, design-locked decision (impl plan "Half-wired window" + design ¬ß11): the write hook is registered + unit-tested + CANARY-REACHABLE (the canary's per-user cases call skills:attach-for-user through the real plugin stack to create the rows the orchestrator's read path then unions ‚Äî so it's load-bearing for THIS PR's own acceptance test, the opposite of dead infra), the READ path it feeds is fully wired into the orchestrator (returns [] today ‚Üí byte-unchanged behavior), and the closing card (TASK-36, the post-approval host-side caller) is named. Invariant #3's "reachable from the canary acceptance test" clause is satisfied. The PR body states "half-wired window OPEN (write path), CLOSES in TASK-36". Splitting the write hook out would break the canary. Codex's accompanying tsc exit-2/127 lines are its own verification-shell env issue (my `pnpm typecheck` passed clean), not code findings. | Alt: defer the write hook to TASK-36 ‚Äî rejected, it would leave the read path + canary without a way to create rows, and contradicts the locked plan.

## 2026-05-26 ‚Äî TASK-44: persist grant is best-effort (don't 500 a successful live grant)

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| Decision | In `routes-allow-host.ts`, wrap the `host-grants:grant` persist call in try/catch (log `host_grant_persist_failed` + swallow). A persist failure returns `{ added }` 200, not 500. |
| Rationale | The LIVE `proxy:add-host` widen already succeeded before the persist attempt, so the host works for the current session. A persist-only failure (grant-limit at the 256 cap, or a transient DB blip) shouldn't surface as a request error ‚Äî it would confuse the user (the host IS live) and the only loss is durability, which the user recovers by re-hitting the wall next fresh spawn. Same fail-direction as the orchestrator's fail-open load: a failure yields fewer persisted hosts, never more, so it can't widen egress. Found in the `/code-review --effort high` substitute pass (Codex was usage-limited this session). |
| Alternatives | (a) Let it propagate ‚Üí 500 on cap/DB-blip even though the live grant worked (rejected: bad UX, dishonest about the live state). (b) Map `grant-limit` ‚Üí a specific 4xx (rejected: still fails a successful live grant; the persist is genuinely secondary). |

| 2026-05-26 | Untrusted bundle content (paths, SKILL.md body, file contents) renders as escaped text in `<pre>`/text nodes only; never dangerouslySetInnerHTML, never markdown‚ÜíHTML | Security: admit/file-view renders agent-authored UNTRUSTED bytes in a privileged admin surface. | 2026-05-26 | Admit decidedByUserId taken from authenticated actor server-side, never request body | I5 capabilities-minimized; catalog-routes test asserts a client-supplied `decidedByUserId: 'u-evil'` is ignored. | Trust client body ‚Äî spoofable, rejected. |

| 2026-05-26 | catalog decision route uses zod `.strip()` not `.strict()` for the decision body | `.strict()` 400s on extra fields; an attacker appending a spoofed `decidedByUserId` would get a revealing 400. `.strip()` silently drops it ‚Äî the route always uses `actor.id`. Matches the plan's "ignores any client-supplied decider" test (admit must still succeed with the extra field present). | `.strict()` ‚Äî fails the ignore-decider test. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex review found 2 P2s ‚Äî fixed both (test-first) | (1) Admit button enabled before bundle diff loaded / despite load error ‚Üí admin could promote un-reviewed untrusted bytes, bypassing the review surface. Fixed: split error into loadError (blocks Admit) vs decideError (doesn't); canAdmit requires entries loaded + no loadError. (2) diffLines LCS allocates (m+1)*(n+1) cells ‚Üí a valid 256KiB file with tens of thousands of lines OOMs the admin tab on opening the dialog. Fixed: cap at DIFF_LCS_MAX_LINES=2000, degrade to faithful whole-file replace (remove-all+add-all) above it ‚Äî bounded O(m+n), no bytes dropped. Both have regression tests. | Rejected nothing ‚Äî both findings were valid security-relevant correctness issues. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 2 found a P1 ‚Äî fixed (test-first) | A submitted bundle file with path `__proto__`/`constructor`/`prototype` is VALID (passes server PATH_RE: lowercase+underscores, not reserved) and catalog:admit promotes it verbatim. On a plain `{}` map, `map['__proto__']=...` is the prototype setter, not an own key, so Object.keys in compareBundles omitted it from the review diff ‚Üí admitted-but-never-shown, a review-gate bypass. Fixed: build the submitted + current path maps with `Object.create(null)` in BundleReviewDialog. Regression tests at both compareBundles and dialog level. | Rejected nothing ‚Äî valid review-gate bypass. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 3 found a P2 ‚Äî the plan's Task 3 premise was WRONG; fixed by OMITTING files | The plan claimed skills:upsert wipes files when `files` is omitted. FALSE: store.upsert (store.ts:105) only rewrites the bundle tree when `input.files !== undefined`; absent = leave unchanged (plugin.ts:372-375 confirms). So my Task 2/3 re-read+re-send of existingFiles was redundant AND harmful: (a) stale-read could clobber a concurrent file change, (b) PUT name-mismatch (caught only AFTER the upsert) copied the path id's files onto the wrong parsed id before the 400. Fix: omit `files` entirely in both PUT update and PATCH setDefaultAttached ‚Äî the store preserves them. Removed the redundant skills:get in PUT. Added a name-mismatch regression test (400 + no id created). LESSON: verify plan premises about store/hook semantics against the actual code before building on them. | Rejected nothing ‚Äî the finding was correct and exposed a wrong plan premise. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 4: fixed P3 (route unwind), accepted P2 (PATCH stale-text race) as documented residual + follow-up | P3: registerCatalogRoutes threw before returning unregisters, leaking an already-live route on partial-init failure. Fixed: wrap the loop in try/catch that unwinds accumulated unregisters before rethrowing (+ unit test with a fake bus failing on the 2nd call). NOTE: the sibling registerAdminSkillsRoutes/registerSettingsSkillsRoutes share this latent gap ‚Äî aligning them is a deferred follow-up (not regressing passing code in this card). P2: PATCH setDefaultAttached read-then-writes manifest/body because the store has only full `upsert` (no flag-only setter, no optimistic version) ‚Äî same race class already documented+accepted in plugin.ts:407 (credential purge). Documented as a KNOWN LIMITATION; proper fix needs a new store-level atomic partial-update primitive = out of scope for this UI card ‚Üí follow-up. | Rejected inventing a half-baked optimistic check (could regress); rejected refactoring the two passing sibling registrars in this card. |

| 2026-05-26 | TASK-45 codex round 5: fixed P2 (unbounded diff DOM nodes) | diffLines bounds the LCS *computation*, but BundleDiffView still rendered one <div> per physical line; a valid 256KiB mostly-newline file = ~hundreds of thousands of DOM nodes ‚Üí freezes the review dialog on an untrusted share. Fixed: cap rendered rows at MAX_RENDERED_DIFF_LINES=500 in FileBody, show the first N + a "‚Ä¶ N more lines not shown inline (file too large to diff in full)" notice. Honest (never silent), bounded DOM. New BundleDiffView.test.tsx asserts the cap + escaped-content + status badge. | Rejected virtualization (heavier, needs a lib) ‚Äî a cap+notice is sufficient for a review surface where oversized files are themselves a review signal. |

## 2026-05-26 ‚Äî TASK-53: JIT broker cold-start (fire catalog:submit on miss, design ¬ß13)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-53 scope = broker-side TRIGGER only.
