No new store/hook/migration. | The card title says "search/request miss" and design ¬ß13 says "broker finds no catalog hit ‚Üí files an admit-request (deduped)". Both broker tools are the no-hit boundary. catalog:submit's cold-start kind takes exactly `{skillId, requestedByUserId, description}` ‚Äî a perfect fit. Dedup is store-side (one pending per skillId) so repeated misses collapse, no queue spam. | (a) fire only on request_capability not-found (rejected ‚Äî card says search too; an exploratory search that finds nothing IS the strongest "the catalog lacks X" signal and is where the model lands first); (b) build a new "wishlist" hook (rejected ‚Äî TASK-41 already shipped catalog:submit cold-start for exactly this; would be a duplicate source of truth, I4). |
| 2026-05-26 | `catalog:submit` is an `optionalCall` on the broker manifest (hasService-guarded + best-effort try/catch), NOT a hard `calls` dep. A failed/absent submit NEVER changes the tool's return (`not-found` / empty stays) and never throws out of the tool. | Same established broker posture as `credentials:list` (decision 2026-05-26): the broker's core search/request must boot + work on a catalog-less/queue-less preset. The cold-start log is a side-effect, not the tool's contract. Capabilities minimized (I5): broker only gains the ability to FILE a request, never to admit one. | Hard `calls` dep (rejected ‚Äî breaks credential/queue-less presets' boot ordering, and a transient submit failure would fail an otherwise-correct not-found). |
| 2026-05-26 | UNTRUSTED INPUT (I5): for `request_capability` the cold-start `skillId` is the model's already-`SKILL_ID_RE`-validated id (re-validated at the top of the tool); description is a host-templated constant (`A user requested the '<id>' capability‚Ä¶`) ‚Äî NO free model text. For `search_catalog` the untrusted `intent` free-text becomes the request `description` verbatim (capped to a sane length), and the dedup `skillId` slug is DERIVED locally by sanitizing intent to `^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$` (lowercase, non-alnum‚Üí`-`, collapse/trim dashes, fallback `capability`) ‚Äî the broker re-validates the slug against SKILL_ID_RE before submit. The description is stored as a plain text column the admin triages; it is NEVER parsed as a manifest and a cold-start request is explicitly NON-promotable (`cold-start-not-promotable`, verified in skills plugin.test) ‚Äî so injected text can't forge an admitted catalog skill. | Invariant #5: untrusted at every hop. The slug is a dedup key, not code; the description is data, not a manifest. The "request, not a skill" boundary is enforced by TASK-41's admit path rejecting cold-start promotion. requestedByUserId always = toolCtx.userId (host-auth), never model input. | (a) import memory-strata `slugify` (rejected ‚Äî cross-plugin import, I2); (b) use raw intent as skillId (rejected ‚Äî fails SKILL_ID_RE, no dedup, unbounded length). |
| 2026-05-26 | Cap the cold-start description at 280 chars and the derived slug at 64; if a search yields a derived slug that fails SKILL_ID_RE even after sanitizing (e.g. intent is all punctuation ‚Üí empty), fall back to slug `capability`. request_capability's not-found description is the fixed template. | Bounded storage + a guaranteed-valid dedup key. The store column is TEXT but unbounded model text shouldn't ride into a request row; 280 is enough for an admin to triage "what did the user want". | No cap (rejected ‚Äî unbounded untrusted text into a row). |

## 2026-05-26 ‚Äî TASK-55: disable agent-SDK telemetry egress (datadog) in the runner

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-55: disable the SDK's phone-home (datadog telemetry) in the runner via the `query({options:{env}})` literal, NOT a `datadoghq.com` allowlist entry (path (a)) | Product decision pre-resolved (we don't want the agent phoning home). Verified the mechanism from the pinned SDK 0.2.119: the vendored `claude` CLI binary POSTs to `https://http-intake.logs.us5.datadoghq.com/api/v2/logs` (fn `Vn8`/`kn8`=trackDatadogEvent, gated by `initializeDatadog` `LfK`). In the binary `LfK` bails (`NB$=!1`) when `rU()` is true; `rU()=BEDROCK||VERTEX||FOUNDRY||dT8()` and `dT8()=ha6()!=="default"`. `ha6()` (== bridge.mjs `Uf()`) returns `"essential-traffic"` for `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC`, `"no-telemetry"` for `DISABLE_TELEMETRY`/`DO_NOT_TRACK`. So ANY of those three flags makes `rU()` true and skips datadog init entirely. | (b) allowlist datadoghq.com ‚Äî rejected: the task explicitly says zero telemetry traffic should exist, an allowlist would still let the agent phone home. |
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-55: set THREE flags ‚Äî `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC=1` (umbrella, primary), `DISABLE_TELEMETRY=1`, `DISABLE_ERROR_REPORTING=1` ‚Äî in a new `buildTelemetryEnv()` helper, spread AFTER `...proxyStartup.anthropicEnv` in main.ts | Grounded in Anthropic's own docs (code.claude.com): the devcontainer.json example uses `CLAUDE_CODE_DISABLE_NONESSENTIAL_TRAFFIC:"1"`; data-usage page says it "opts out of all non-essential traffic". `DISABLE_TELEMETRY` + `DISABLE_ERROR_REPORTING` are the per-channel kill switches (defense-in-depth + readable intent). Spread AFTER anthropicEnv so a (currently impossible ‚Äî none are in proxy-startup ENV_ALLOWLIST) host-forwarded value can't override; these are non-negotiable security floors, unlike tty-hints which are intentionally overridable. | Single flag only ‚Äî works, but three flags document intent per-channel and survive a future SDK that splits the gate. Also setting DISABLE_AUTOUPDATER/DISABLE_UPDATES ‚Äî rejected: out of scope (not telemetry; the sandbox CLI is pinned/immutable and never self-updates). |
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-55: codex/local review driven instead of waiting on Codex (multi-day usage limit this session) | Dispatch said Codex is limited; substitute `/code-review --effort high` + security-checklist + manual whole-branch review per the orchestration override. | Sit in a Codex wait-loop ‚Äî explicitly forbidden by the dispatch. |
| 2026-05-26 | TASK-61: fix the BundleReviewDialog "expected 404" console error SERVER-SIDE ‚Äî add an opt-in `?missingOk=1` query param to `GET /admin/skills/:id` that returns `200 {skill:null}` (instead of 404) for a missing skill, and have `getSkillOrNull` request that param. | The browser auto-logs EVERY 4xx/5xx network request to the console regardless of how `fetch` handles the resolved Response ‚Äî JS cannot intercept/silence a 404 that already happened. So you can't "swallow" it on the client; you must avoid PROVOKING it. The diff only needs "is there a current catalog version?" ‚Äî turning that probe into a clean 200 removes the console noise. Opt-in param keeps strict `getSkill`/`GET` behavior (genuine 404) unchanged. | (a) Client `console.error` mute ‚Äî impossible (browser logs it before JS sees it). (b) Probe via `listSkills()` (always 200) then conditionally `getSkill` ‚Äî two round-trips + still 404s for a brand-new id whose summary isn't in the list. (c) Make the route ALWAYS 200-null ‚Äî rejected: breaks genuine REST 404 semantics other callers (`getSkill`) rely on. |

The dialog already had a description paragraph; this just promotes it to the semantic primitive. | Manual `aria-describedby={id}` on `<DialogContent>` + `id` on the `<p>` ‚Äî works but reinvents what the installed `DialogDescription` primitive does for free. `aria-describedby={undefined}` to silence the warning ‚Äî hides it without giving AT users a description (worse a11y). |

| 2026-05-27 | The SKILL.md documents the **stricter** skill-id regex `^[a-z][a-z0-9-]{0,63}$` (the runner materialize gate, `agent-claude-sdk-runner/src/installed-skills.ts:25`), NOT the looser tool gate `^[a-z0-9][a-z0-9._-]{0,127}$` (`skill-broker .../install-authored-skill.ts:10`). | The two gates disagree: an id passing the tool but failing the runner installs + gets approved, then SILENTLY fails to materialize. Teaching the strict form prevents agents authoring doomed ids. The underlying gate MISMATCH is a pre-existing latent silent-failure bug this feature makes far more reachable ‚Äî logged as a FOLLOW-UP (align the tool's SKILL_ID_RE to the runner's, or reject-at-tool with a friendly error), NOT fixed in this PR (scope). | tighten the tool regex in this PR ‚Äî deferred to keep scope focused; documented + flagged instead. |
| 2026-05-27 | Channel-web carries `packages?` as OPTIONAL across the three SSE card re-declarations (server/types, transport SseFrame, permission-card-store) even though the broker producer fires it as required. | SSE is a serialization/trust boundary ‚Äî be liberal in what you accept (a payload predating the field, or a non-skill card, must still parse). The `kind:'host'` card branch correctly reconstructs without packages. The render guards on presence. | make consumer types required to match the producer ‚Äî rejected: brittle across the wire boundary. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 (`workspace.materialize failed: response body too large`): fix by streaming the materialize bundle as a raw `application/octet-stream` HTTP response (runner drains it to a temp file, no in-memory base64/JSON round-trip, disk-bounded cap `MAX_BINARY_RESPONSE_BYTES`), NOT by shrinking the bundle. Touches: ipc-protocol (materialize response is now binary, request stays JSON), ipc-core (`HandlerBinary` result variant + `writeBinaryOk` + dispatcher branch + handler base64-decodes the hook output to a Buffer), ipc-client (`callBinary` drain-to-file, materialize off the JSON RESPONSE_SCHEMAS table), agent-claude-sdk-runner (`materializeWorkspace({root, bundlePath})` clones from the file; main.ts call site). The `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` HOOK keeps its base64 contract (used by commit-notify resync) ‚Äî decode happens only at the materialize wire edge. | Removes the 33% base64 tax (which is literally what pushed `ws-3f2c7b71`'s ~3 MiB bundle over the 4 MiB base64 wire cap) AND the in-memory cap wall, while preserving the baseline-OID contract byte-for-byte (same bundle bytes). The runner already temp-files the bundle before cloning, so streaming-to-disk is a natural fit and is memory-friendly for large bundles. | (1) Squash/re-root history to bound growth ‚Äî REJECTED for this fix (deferred as a follow-up): the materialized baseline OID is threaded as the first commit-notify `parentVersion` (main.ts:425) and MUST resolve in the host's git mirror (`exportBaselineBundle({version})`); a squashed OID isn't in the mirror, so bounding growth requires re-rooting the mirror history too ‚Äî a multi-component design change (materialize + commit-notify + mirror force-push + resync + multi-replica), not a bug fix. (3) Raise `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ‚Äî REJECTED as sole fix: keeps base64 + full in-memory buffering on both ends; band-aid only. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 implemented INLINE with strict TDD rather than fanning out per-task subagents. | The change is ONE coherent wire-format change across ~7 interdependent files (the schema change won't compile until every call site updates in lockstep) ‚Äî fragmenting it across subagents would leave each subagent's tree non-compiling. Matches the documented inline-fallback precedent (ARCH-6/TASK-32/41) for fully-mapped, tightly-coupled mechanical work. | per-task subagents ‚Äî rejected: the tasks aren't independently testable/compilable in isolation. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 Phase-5 review: codex native reviewer + CLI both USAGE-LIMITED (resets 2026-05-31, same rolling quota as TASK-53/55/58/59). Substituted `/code-review high` (multi-agent finder+verify) + manual whole-branch trace. Applied 4 findings, rejected 1. | Documented precedent (meta ARCH-11/FAULTA-3, decisions TASK-59): when codex is usage-limited, don't wait ‚Äî substitute /code-review + manual trace. Findings APPLIED: (F1) raised `IPC_TIMEOUTS_MS['workspace.materialize']` 30s‚Üí120s ‚Äî 30s was the new binding ceiling for streaming a large bundle, would relocate the BUG-W3 boot crash to a timeout; (F2) ws write-error (ENOSPC/EROFS) now non-retryable ‚Äî deterministic disk failure shouldn't re-stream for the 2-min window; (F3) Content-Length-vs-bytesWritten truncation guard ‚Üí retryable (defensive; common truncation already surfaces as a retryable res 'error'); (F4) added `callBinary` to 5 test `IpcClient` literals (vitest-tolerates/tsc-rejects latent trap ‚Äî runner tsconfig excludes __tests__ so not a CI break, but type-incorrect). | (F5) restore `RESPONSE_SCHEMAS` to a full `Record<IpcActionName,...>` for compile-time exhaustiveness ‚Äî REJECTED: materialize legitimately has no JSON response schema (it's binary), so `Partial` is the honest type; the `schema===undefined` runtime guard throws loudly for any future action that forgets its entry. |
| 2026-05-28 | BUG-W3 codex re-review (quota recovered) found ONE P2 ‚Äî APPLIED: raised both IPC listeners' `IDLE_TIMEOUT_MS` 60s‚Üí130s (`packages/ipc-http/src/listener.ts`, `packages/ipc-server/src/listener.ts`). | The earlier F1 fix raised the materialize CLIENT per-attempt timeout 30s‚Üí120s, but the host's `server.setTimeout(IDLE_TIMEOUT_MS=60_000)` was left at 60s with no `'timeout'` listener (Node destroys the idle socket). Before the first response byte the materialize socket is IDLE (request received, host still building the bundle via `git bundle create` on a huge aged repo); a 60s idle timeout would reset it mid-build ‚Üí ECONNRESET ‚Üí retryable ‚Üí rebuild ‚Üí loop ‚Üí boot crash, relocating the very BUG-W3 crash. 130s sits just above the 120s client budget so the CLIENT times out first (clean/handled) instead of the server resetting. Server-wide bump is safe: no per-action server timeout exists, the only long-lived actions are materialize (120s) + the 30s long-poll, and a wedged internal IPC socket lingering 130s vs 60s is acceptable (trusted host‚Üîrunner channel). No test pinned the 60s value. | per-route socket timeout (`req.socket.setTimeout` in the dispatcher) ‚Äî rejected: more surface for a constant bump that's safe server-wide; host writing an early keepalive byte to reset the timer ‚Äî rejected: hacky. |
| 2026-05-28 | commit-notify re-sync "response body too large" (SAME bug class as BUG-W3, but on the commit-notify re-sync path instead of materialize): fix by streaming the baseline bundle OUT-OF-BAND via a NEW binary IPC action `workspace.export-baseline-bundle` (octet-stream, drained to a temp file via `callBinary`/`requestOnceBinaryToFile`), NOT inline in the commit-notify JSON response. Host commit-notify now returns only `{accepted:false, actualParent, reason}` at BOTH re-sync sites (export-baseline catch + apply-bundle catch); `resyncEnvelopeFromCause` trimmed to `actualParent`-only. Runner `commitNotifyWithResync` binary-fetches the bundle for `actualParent` then passes the FILE PATH to `resyncBaselineAndReplay` (signature changed `baselineBundleBytes:string` ‚Üí `bundlePath:string`, file-owned/deleted by the callee, mirrors `materializeWorkspace`). `baselineBundleBytes` REMOVED from `WorkspaceCommitNotifyResponse`; new `WorkspaceExportBaselineBundleRequestSchema{version:string.min(1)}` + 120s timeout; `callBinary` Action union widened to the two binary actions. New host handler reuses the existing `workspace:export-baseline-bundle` SERVICE hook (no new hook, no backend import). | The re-sync envelope's `baselineBundleBytes` (base64 git bundle, ~MiB on aged workspaces) was the ONLY uncapped-growth field still on the JSON wire after BUG-W3 migrated materialize; on `ws-3f2c7b71` (~143 files, hundreds of commits) the base64 blew the runner's 4 MiB `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ‚Üí `response body too large` ‚Üí turn never synced ‚Üí 120s `agent:invoke` timeout ‚Üí terminate ‚Üí dying pod's late commit-notify hits terminated session ‚Üí `unknown token` ‚Üí infinite re-ask loop after a skill approval. actions.ts:240 even commented materialize "blew that cap" ‚Äî identical hazard left on commit-notify. Reuses BUG-W3's proven binary infra exactly. | (b) raise `MAX_RESPONSE_BYTES` ‚Äî REJECTED: band-aid, keeps base64+full-buffer on both ends, only defers the cap. (c) call `workspace.materialize` with `actualParent` to reuse THAT binary action ‚Äî REJECTED: materialize's request is `.strict({})` (no version param) and its semantics are "current HEAD / session-start clone"; overloading it for an arbitrary version muddies the contract. A dedicated sibling action keeps each binary action single-purpose and its schema honest. (d) host probes export-baseline-bundle for a FRESHER actualParent before replying (old apply-bundle-catch behavior) ‚Äî REJECTED: pointless now that the host doesn't inline bytes; if the head advanced again the runner's own binary fetch 500s and it re-materializes. |
| 2026-05-28 | commit-notify re-sync P1 (codex whole-branch review of fdd9332d): a FAILED `workspace.export-baseline-bundle` binary fetch on the re-sync path is NOT terminal `'kept'` ‚Äî it means "the head moved AGAIN" (a third writer advanced past `actualParent` between commit-notify returning it and the runner fetching its bundle ‚Üí backend `parent-mismatch` ‚Üí host 500 ‚Üí `callBinary` rejects). Fix: split `commitNotifyWithResync`'s single try-catch into TWO ‚Äî a FETCH catch that `continue`s the bounded loop (same `parentVersion`, same original `bundle`; `attempt` already incremented so a writer storm still terminates at `MAX_RESYNC_ATTEMPTS` ‚Üí rollback), and a RESYNC catch (the git rebase/replay) that stays terminal `'kept'` as before. The host handler is UNCHANGED (sanitized 500 on parent-mismatch is correct; retry logic lives runner-side). `callBinary` already unlinks its own temp file on any failure (ipc-client.ts:864-870) so no per-retry temp leak. | The prior entry's rejection-(d) reasoning ("if the head advanced again the runner's own binary fetch 500s and it re-materializes") was WRONG: the 500 surfaced as a `callBinary` reject inside the resync try-catch ‚Üí terminal `'kept'` ‚Üí on the final/idle commit path the runner exits with the local bundle never applied to the host ‚Üí the turn tail is dropped in exactly this double-writer race. The pre-split code's apply-bundle-catch re-fetched at the fresher head; collapsing both sites onto a single fetch removed that recovery. Re-entering the bounded loop restores it without the host probing. | Make the host handler signal "stale, refetch" distinctly instead of a plain 500 ‚Äî NOT needed: the runner already learns the fresher head from the very next commit-notify's `actualParent`, so a plain 500 + loop re-entry is sufficient and keeps the handler's error envelope sanitized (no leak). |

## 2026-05-30 ‚Äî Skills out of git: DB+blob substrate + hybrid materialization gate (design doc)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|------|----------|-----------|--------------|
| 2026-05-30 | Wrote `docs/plans/2026-05-30-skills-out-of-git-design.md` (Proposed, needs sign-off): skills are the LAST data class still in git after the storage-out-of-git doc. Move authoring to `/ephemeral/skill-draft/<id>/`, agent calls `skill_propose(manifest,files,capabilityProposal,origin)` over IPC, host stores ONE skill row + bundle bytes via `blob:put` (kills TASK-40 isomorphic-git bundle-tree backing). Same DB/blob store for catalog/default/attached/authored = one source of truth (I4). Reuses storage doc's `blob:*` + `/ephemeral` substrate. | Finishes what the storage doc started: authored drafts in `/permanent/.ax/draft-skills/` (git) + bundle bytes in a git tree (TASK-40) + DB rows for installed = split-brain across 3 stores for one concept, and the last reason the per-turn git pipeline stays load-bearing. Skill bundles are opaque content-addressed last-write-wins units (like artifacts), they don't want versioning. | (a) keep skills in git (storage-doc ¬ßE status quo) ‚Äî rejected: split-brain + keeps git on the hot path; (b) Postgres-bytea for bundles ‚Äî viable but blob store is cleaner at scale + dedups by sha. |
| 2026-05-30 | **Hybrid materialization gate** (the key product decision, user chose it over pure-lazy or pure-strict): classify at propose time ‚Äî `clean scan ‚àß origin=authored ‚àß capabilityProposal=‚àÖ` ‚Üí `active`, materialize FREELY (self-authored instruction scaffolding, no reach to consent to). Anything carrying caps (hosts/credentials/mcp/packages) OR `origin‚àà{imported,attached}` ‚Üí `pending`, APPROVE-BEFORE-MATERIALIZE (no bytes project, no caps inject until human approves the card). Scan hit (any class) ‚Üí `quarantined` (omit + reason). | Interruption proportional to risk: silent for style-guide skills, explicit card when the agent asks for network+secrets. Moves the cap gate BEFORE first run for the DECLARED case (stricter AND simpler than phase-4's reactive-at-the-wall timing). Imported zero-cap still gated on provenance (supply-chain hop). | pure-lazy (phase-4 as merged: everything materializes, caps approved reactively at the egress wall) ‚Äî rejected: risky bytes run before consent for declared-cap skills; pure-strict (gate everything incl. self-authored instruction text) ‚Äî rejected: nags on zero-risk scaffolding. |
| 2026-05-30 | Re-times phase-4 reactive cap approval ‚Üí before-materialize, BUT KEEPS: the TASK-35 approval-card SSE frame + `proposal‚à©approved` store (only the trigger changes), the `0555` ephemeral projection + `materializeInstalledSkillsFromEnv` (fed from `blob:get` not git), quarantine-as-host-state (phase-2), session-dirty‚Üíre-spawn trigger, AND the TASK-37 runtime reactive egress wall as a safety net for UNDECLARED reach (its proper job, independent of skill approval). | The reactive wall is still right for "a skill tries a host it never proposed" ‚Äî that's a runtime egress guard, not skill approval. Only the DECLARED-cap approval moves upfront. Most of phase-3/4 survives substrate-swapped, not thrown away. | ‚Äî |
| 2026-05-30 | **Spawn-time discovery constraint** (stated loudly in the doc): a skill materialized mid-session is INVISIBLE to the running model ‚Äî (1) awareness: skill name+desc are injected into context AT SPAWN, writing to disk mid-turn doesn't edit context already sent; (2) readability: the `0555` dir is projected at spawn, post-spawn writes may not appear in the running sandbox. Adopt **version (a): re-spawn on next turn** ‚Äî host flips row to `active`, user's next message runs a fresh sandbox that projects+enumerates the skill. Reuses pending-turn re-spawn orchestration (2026-05-26-jit-pending-turn...). Build req: harness/system-prompt must TELL the agent it's on the (a) boundary so it words turn-1 right ("ready on your next message") and doesn't try to invoke a just-proposed skill. | No new machinery; honest fit for spawn-time discovery. The approval card IS the pause that hides the re-spawn (user reads card + pastes key > re-spawn cost). UX: gated "make a Linear skill" = ask‚Üíapprove‚Üíuse across 2 msgs, feels normal; "create AND use in one breath" degrades to ONE extra "go" message (agent tees it up), never breaks. | version (b) live injection (writable dir + system-reminder context frame) ‚Äî DEFERRED: forks discovery into 2 paths + gives up 0555 immutability; if same-turn ever needed, cleaner form is transparent re-spawn + replay (single discovery path). |
| 2026-05-30 | Canonical UX example throughout = the Linear skill (matches the lazy-redesign doc's own motivating example). Linear needs `api.linear.app`+`LINEAR_API_KEY` ‚Üí lands in the GATED class ‚Üí user sees the approval card with named hosts+credential, pastes key (‚Üí vault, never bundle/blob/git), skill live next turn. Contrast: "commit-message style skill" = zero-cap self-authored ‚Üí free, no card, live next turn. | The gate only appears when there's actual reach to consent to ‚Äî that's the whole point of hybrid. Wording points FORWARD ("ready on your next message"), not back ("you may need to restart") which leaks the mechanism + reads like a bug. | ‚Äî |

| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **blob:* slice ships the host-side service hook + @ax/blob-store-fs backend + a canary blob:put‚Üíblob:get round-trip ‚Äî and DEFERS the IPC `blob.*` binary action / `callBinary` request-direction wire to the Part C card that introduces the first runner-side caller (artifact_publish/attachments‚Üíblob:put).** Adding a `blob.*` IPC action now with no runner caller would be a half-wired plugin (I3). The hook payload is SHAPED for the eventual wire today: bytes are a raw `Uint8Array` on the bus (NOT base64-in-JSON), the JSON envelope is just `{sha256,size}` ‚Äî so the later card is purely additive (it adds the octet-stream transport + a dispatcher action, no payload reshape). The canary IS the I3 "wire one real caller" proof. | The card's primary acceptance = the storage-agnostic `blob:*` hook reachable via canary round-trip; the "IPC/binary wire plumbing" line describes the eventual sandbox‚Üíhost transport whose only consumer (Part C) is a later card. I3 forbids dead infra. Sandbox-side bytes-up (`blob:put`) needs a NEW request-direction binary channel anyway (today's `callBinary` is response-direction only ‚Äî materialize/export-baseline-bundle drain a body to disk); that belongs with its consumer. | (a) ship a dead `blob.*` IPC action now ‚Äî rejected (I3 half-wired); (b) base64 bytes through the JSON `call()` path ‚Äî rejected (card forbids the 4 MiB JSON frame for bytes + design says callBinary octet-stream). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **Did NOT wire @ax/blob-store-fs into `presets/k8s` in this slice.** No host-side consumer of blob:* exists yet (attachments/artifacts/skills onto blob = Part C/D). Wiring it into the preset with no caller is half-wired at the preset level (and the preset's `preset.test.ts` "every calls entry satisfied" derives sets dynamically ‚Äî a registrant with no caller is fine there, but it's still dead weight). The package-local canary (createTestHarness‚Üíbootstrap) is the reachability proof instead. | Same I3 logic as the IPC defer. The plugin is fully registered + tested + reachable from ITS canary, which the card explicitly accepts ("the canary acceptance test must exercise a blob:put‚Üíblob:get round-trip"). | wire into preset now ‚Äî rejected, no consumer; deferred to the first Part C consumer card. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | **blob:get re-verifies the digest on read and rejects (throws `corrupt` PluginError) on mismatch ‚Äî never returns tampered bytes.** Lifted from lfs.ts's write-side `computed !== oid` check, applied to the READ side per the card's security requirement ("a corrupted/tampered object is rejected, not returned"). Caller-supplied sha is regex-gated (`^[a-f0-9]{64}$`) before any path is built (no traversal; the key is a content hash, never a caller path). Atomic temp-then-rename on put with a collision-safe `.tmp.<pid>.<uuid>` suffix (lfs.ts's concurrent-PUT-collision fix). | Untrusted-content storage substrate: an attacker who tampers a blob on disk (or a bitflip) must not be able to feed corrupted bytes back as if content-addressed-valid. Re-verify closes that. | trust the path (sha == content by construction) ‚Äî rejected: on-disk tamper / bitrot would silently serve bad bytes under a valid-looking hash. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-65) | Codex Phase-5 review flagged ONE P1 ("root tsconfig references packages/blob-store-fs but the package isn't in the tracked diff ‚Üí clean build fails"). REJECTED as a pre-commit artifact: the package files exist on disk + build+test+lint all pass; they were just UNTRACKED because the review ran before the commit (`git ls-files` reports nothing for an unstaged new dir). Resolves entirely on commit ‚Äî verified `git add --dry-run` stages all 11 source files (dist/node_modules/tsbuildinfo correctly gitignored). No code change. | The Codex companion reviews the TRACKED diff; a brand-new package's files are untracked until `git add`, so its own `git ls-files` check spuriously reports them missing. This is a known shape for the FIRST commit of a new package ‚Äî commit, then the diff is whole. | re-run review post-commit to confirm ‚Äî optional; the staging dry-run already proves the files land. |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **Display event log = `conversation_events` Postgres rows owned by `@ax/conversations`** (not a new plugin): append-only, keyed `(conversation_id, seq)`, columns `event_kind` (`turn`/`permission-card`/`turn-error`) + nullable `role` + `payload` JSONB + `created_at`. Persist via a `conversations:append-event` service hook; turn rows come from @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler (awaited persist-before-ack) + the user turn from @ax/chat-orchestrator at dispatch; host-only display events from NEW `chat:turn-error` + `chat:permission-request` subscribers in @ax/conversations. `conversations:get` reads the log instead of `parseJsonlToTurns`; turn events ‚Üí existing `Turn[]` (unchanged renderer path), host-only events ‚Üí a new additive `displayEvents` field on `GetOutput`. | conversations already owns the conversation row + the get read; a separate plugin would split the SoT. Storing turn-end's already-folded `ContentBlock[]` makes redisplay==live by construction for content; host-only events (cards/errors) are absent from the jsonl so they MUST come from the host event stream. | A separate `@ax/display-log` plugin (rejected: splits the conversation SoT, needs its own ACL gate duplicating conversations'); persisting per-`event.stream-chunk` delta (rejected: duplicates the turn-end content, no redisplay benefit). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **persist-before-ack (B3): @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler awaits an ISOLATED `conversations:append-event` (a dedicated `persist` slot on the dispatcher EventSpec) BEFORE the 202, then fires the chat:turn-end broadcast fire-and-forget AFTER.** Only the durability-critical append precedes the ack; the broadcast (bump/clear-reqId/titles-LLM/evictor) stays off the ack path so a slow observer can't delay the runner. `conversations:append-event` is an OPTIONAL dispatcher dep (hasService-gated; CLI single-session skips it). A persist throw ‚Üí 500 + loud `event_persist_failed` (no false ack). | The design's B3 literally requires "persist the turn's frames before the turn-end ack." Isolating the persist from the broadcast avoids coupling the turn-end ack latency to unrelated observers (the title-LLM subscriber). | Awaiting the whole chat:turn-end fire (rejected: title-LLM blocks every ack); persisting in the conversations subscriber (rejected: rides the broadcast, same coupling). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **Client live-vs-reload render-path unification is OUT of scope for this card.** Today live render = `transport.ts` folding SSE frames into assistant-ui (+ separate `permission-card-store`/`turn-error` stores); reload = `history-adapter.ts` fetching `Turn[]`. This card switches the reload SOURCE (jsonl‚Üíevent log) but keeps the existing reload renderer; "same renderer path" holds for CONTENT by construction (turn-end blocks = folded stream-chunk terminal state). Host-only card/error events are PERSISTED + RETURNED on `GetOutput.displayEvents` (so the SoT is complete + tested) but the CLIENT does not yet fold them on reload. | The card scope is "ONLY the display SoT (event log + conversations:get switch)". A literal one-fold client rewrite (reload replays persisted card/error frames through the live transport) touches transport.ts + 2 client stores + history-adapter, isn't coverable by the host-side redisplay test the acceptance asks for, and is a distinct unit of work. The host SoT being complete now is what makes that follow-up cheap. | Full client unification in this PR (rejected: scope creep beyond "event log + conversations:get switch", large untested client surface); NOT returning host-only events at all (rejected: acceptance #3 requires redisplay to INCLUDE host-only UI, and the SoT must carry them even if the client folds them later). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, post-review) | **Persist the USER display turn HOST-SIDE in @ax/chat-orchestrator at agent:invoke dispatch ‚Äî NOT via a runner-emitted user `event.turn-end`.** Codex review caught that the display event log was missing user turns (the SDK runner emits `event.turn-end` only for tool/assistant turns; the user prompt lives only in the jsonl). First attempt: emit a `role:'user'` `event.turn-end` from the runner. REJECTED after finding it fires the broadcast `chat:turn-end`, whose channel-web SSE subscriber closes the live stream on `ctx.conversationId` match (NOT reqId) ‚Üí a user turn-end at turn START sends a premature `{done:true}` and kills the live stream; it also trips one-shot keep-warm + clear-active-req-id. Final: orchestrator calls `conversations:append-event` (kind:'turn', role:'user', blocks = typed text + attachment contentBlocks) once per agent:invoke before the route/spawn decision, off the turn-end path. Gated on `bus.hasService('conversations:append-event')` (same hasService posture as the conversations:* peers; NOT in `manifest.calls`); best-effort. | The orchestrator already holds the user's content + conversationId and is the single host-side dispatch chokepoint; persisting there has zero turn-end side effects. The tool/assistant turns persist via @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler (awaited, isolated, persist-before-ack). Two persist sites, one per audience-of-turn, both host-side. | Runner-emitted user turn-end (rejected: closes the live SSE stream via the conversationId-keyed done-frame subscriber); persisting in channel-web's chat-messages route (rejected: the orchestrator is the canonical dispatch gate that ALL agent:invoke paths ‚Äî warm + fresh ‚Äî funnel through; channel-web would miss non-web callers). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, post-review) | **persist-before-ack moved OUT of the broadcast chat:turn-end subscriber and INTO @ax/ipc-core's event.turn-end handler as an isolated, awaited `conversations:append-event` call.** Codex P2 caught that awaiting the WHOLE chat:turn-end subscriber chain (my first impl) blocks every turn-end ack on @ax/conversation-titles' `llm:call` (it subscribes to chat:turn-end). Fix: the event.turn-end handler does `await bus.call('conversations:append-event', ...)` (ONLY the persist) before firing the fire-and-forget broadcast for the OTHER subscribers (bump/clear-reqId/titles/evictor). `conversations:append-event` is an OPTIONAL dispatcher dep (bus.hasService-gated; CLI single-session skips it). And Codex P2: a persist FAILURE now re-throws ‚Üí the dispatcher writes 500 instead of a false 202, so a turn that never reached the log isn't acked (B3 no-omission). | Isolating the awaited persist keeps persist-before-ack without coupling the turn-end latency to unrelated observers. The dependency-sync test enforces the new optional dep (string-literal hook name at the bus.call/hasService site so the scanner detects it). | Awaiting the whole chat:turn-end fire (rejected: title-LLM latency on every turn ack); a dedicated new `chat:turn-end-persist` hook (rejected: extra protocol surface for no gain over the optional bus.call). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **Final persist-before-ack shape: a dedicated `persist` slot on the dispatcher EventSpec (awaited before 202) SEPARATE from `fire` (broadcast, fire-and-forget AFTER 202).** Re-review caught that my first split still awaited `fireEventTurnEnd` which itself awaited the chat:turn-end broadcast ‚Üí titles' LLM still blocked the ack. Fix: `event.turn-end` now has `persist: persistEventTurnEnd` (the isolated conversations:append-event call, awaited) and `fire: fireEventTurnEnd` (just the broadcast, kicked off `void` after the 202). The dispatcher awaits `persist`, writes 202, then `void fire(...)`. A persist throw ‚Üí 500 + loud `event_persist_failed` log. Guard tests: a slow conversations:append-event holds the 202 (persist-before-ack); a slow chat:turn-end subscriber does NOT (P2a regression). | Only the durability-critical append must precede the ack; everything else (bump/clear-reqId/titles/evictor) is observation. Coupling them was the latency bug. | Awaiting the whole fire (the bug); a 2nd hook (rejected ‚Äî extra surface). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **appendEvent retries on the (conversation_id, seq) unique-violation (SQLSTATE 23505), bounded (8).** Re-review caught that `INSERT ... SELECT COALESCE(MAX(seq),0)+1` is NOT race-safe across two CONCURRENT statements (a permission-card persist racing the turn-end persist for the same conversation) ‚Äî both read the same MAX, one hits the PK. Retry recomputes MAX and re-inserts. Tested with 20 concurrent appends ‚Üí 20 distinct contiguous seqs, none dropped. (NB: the host-only-event subscribers persist async/independently, so this race is real, not theoretical.) `isUniqueViolation` matches `err.code === '23505'` (pg driver SQLSTATE; storage-internal, never on a hook payload). | A monotonic per-conversation seq with concurrent writers needs either a DB sequence or retry-on-conflict; retry is the smaller change and the contention is tiny. | A Postgres SEQUENCE per conversation (rejected: unbounded sequence objects); an advisory lock (rejected: heavier than retry for rare contention). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review) | **projectDisplayEvents folds by keeping the LAST event per (kind,foldKey) but ORDERS the result by the terminal event's seq** (not Map insertion order). Re-review caught that `Map.set` preserves the original insertion position, so a card resolved later would render in its pending-frame slot, before host events that actually happened between. Fix: track `{event, seq}` per key, then `sort((a,b)=>a.seq-b.seq)`. Tested: card A pending (seq1) ‚Üí card B (seq2) ‚Üí A resolved (seq3) ‚áí order [B, A-approved]. | Replay must reflect the real timeline; the terminal frame's seq is when the card reached its shown state. | ‚Äî |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66, re-review #3) | **Accepted-for-greenfield scope calls on 3 re-review findings, with followups filed:** (1) a LEGACY conversation (jsonl turns predating this PR) that gets a NEW turn shows only the new event-log turns on reload (the first event row flips conversations:get off the jsonl fallback). Accepted: ax-next has NO production data (context.md 2026-04-29 invariant); the only affected case is a dev conversation mid-deploy; TASK-67/70 retire the jsonl entirely, mooting it. A merge-the-jsonl-prefix fix risks duplication for a non-existent population. (2) The reactive-wall HOST permission card (kind:host, fired from event.http-egress) has no conversationId on its ctx (it is reqId-matched live), so it does not persist ‚Äî only the skill approval card (conversationId-matched) + turn-errors do. Deferred (followup): needs reqId-to-conversationId resolution in the orchestrator egress path. The primary host-only UI (skill cards, surfaced errors) DOES persist. (3) The runner swallows a turn-end 500 (.catch swallow), so a hard-DB-outage persist failure loses that turn's display row despite the 500. Accepted: the realistic concurrent failure (seq race) is handled by the store retry; a hard outage gets the B3 LOUD alarm (event_persist_failed at error + 500) ‚Äî "install the alarm now, swing the hammer only if it rings" (the design's staged-robustness posture). The user still sees the live reply; only redisplay of that one turn degrades. Making the runner non-swallow risks terminating chats on transient blips. | All three are real but each is mooted by greenfield+TASK-67, a narrow secondary variant, or covered by the loud-alarm posture the design stages. Fixing them fully is disproportionate for this card. | (1) merge jsonl prefix (rejected: duplication risk, no population); (2) persist host card now (deferred: orchestrator egress reqId-to-conv resolution is its own unit); (3) runner non-swallow + retry/queue (deferred: B3 escalation territory). |
| 2026-05-30 (TASK-66) | **A literal NUL byte in a TS source file makes git/grep treat it as binary** (grep silently reports nothing / "binary file matches" and hides text matches ‚Äî this bit me repeatedly during the session). It crept into a Map-key template literal and a comment. Fix: escape as the unicode-0000 escape in code; plain space in comments. Detect with `grep -aPn` for the null pattern (the -a forces text mode) or `cat -v` (shows ^@). Scan the whole diff before commit. | A NUL is a fine Map-key separator (no field contains it) but MUST be escaped, never embedded literally, or it breaks every text tool that reads the file. | ‚Äî |

## 2026-05-30 ‚Äî TASK-67 (resume jsonl out of git: opaque row-per-line store + delta-ship)

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | Store resume jsonl as opaque row-per-line in a new `conversations_v1_transcripts` table (conversation_id, seq, raw `line` TEXT/BYTEA verbatim), owned by @ax/conversations ‚Äî same plugin that owns the display log (TASK-66) and the conversation row. | Open Q1 in design leans Postgres rows for both; transactional with conversation row; cheap `max(seq)` resume check; single writer per session = contention-free (NOT git CAS). One plugin owns all conversation-scoped state (I4). | row-per-line in a 2nd plugin (extra cross-plugin hop); whole-file blob (O(n^2) re-upload ‚Äî design rejects). |
| 2026-05-30 | New host service hooks `conversations:append-transcript` / `conversations:replace-transcript` / `conversations:get-transcript` (host-internal, ctx-scoped) + matching IPC actions `session.append-transcript` (JSON) / `session.replace-transcript` (callBinaryUpload octet-stream) / `session.get-transcript` (callBinary octet-stream, resume read). | Mirrors TASK-66 `conversations:append-event` posture (host-internal hook fed by an IPC handler). append carries small JSON (lines[] of opaque strings); replace+read carry whole-file bytes ‚Üí binary channel (TASK-68 callBinaryUpload/callBinary). Storage-agnostic field names: conversationId/fromSeq/prefixHash/seq/lines ‚Äî NO git/jsonl/sqlite vocab. | overload session.get-config to ship the whole transcript (blows the 4MiB JSON cap + 5s timeout on a long session). |
| 2026-05-30 | Resume read ships the joined jsonl bytes back to the runner via a binary `session.get-transcript` action; runner writes them to `$CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR/projects/<slug>/<sessionId>.jsonl` (slug = SDK's realpath(cwd)‚Üí`/.`-to-`-` encoding) BEFORE query({resume}); F2a guard becomes "host says max(seq)>0" (carried on session.get-config as `hasResumableTranscript:boolean`) backed by the DB. | Design B2: host joins ORDER BY seq ‚Üí bytes ‚Üí runner writes them before resume. The git-materialized jsonl is GONE for the common path, so the SDK can't find the file unless the runner writes it. | keep globbing the workspace (defeats out-of-git). |
| 2026-05-30 | Replace commitTurnAndBundle at the result boundary (main.ts:1293) + final flush (main.ts:1450) with the delta-ship: waitForTranscriptUuid (KEEP) ‚Üí read jsonl tail past sentOffset ‚Üí split complete lines ‚Üí session.append-transcript(prefixHash) ‚Üí append|resync. Thread sentOffset/sentSeq/prefixHash across turns like parentVersion. | Card lifecycle steps 1-5. commitTurnAndBundle (git) is the thing being removed for the chat path. Bind-after-append-durable replaces bind-after-commit-accepted (main.ts:1321). | keep git in parallel (violates I4 one-SoT ‚Äî "don't leave two resume backings"). |
| 2026-05-30 | B3 structural divergence detector lives host-side at turn-end (in the event.turn-end persist path, after both display-log append AND transcript append for the turn are durable): compare turn count + role/order sequence between display log (store.listEvents, kind='turn') and resume rows (parse role off each jsonl line, whitelist user/assistant/tool). Mismatch ‚Üí loud `ctx.logger.error` + metric, NEVER throws/blocks. Install ALARM only; NO derivation escalation (YAGNI). | Card + design B3: structural not hash (hash false-positives on redaction). Detector must stay quiet across latency/concurrent-writer/resume. Both stores are host-owned so the host can cross-check. | content-hash compare (rejected by design). |
| 2026-05-30 | KEEP commitTurnAndBundle + the git workspace commit path for NON-jsonl /permanent changes (identity, Pattern A). Only the TRANSCRIPT no longer rides git. The full git-pipeline thinning (gate commit on non-empty non-jsonl diff) is Phase 5 / TASK-70's job, NOT this card. | Card scope is "replace commitTurnAndBundle AT THE RESULT BOUNDARY for the transcript"; design phases the LFS-delete + commit-gating separately (Phase 5). ### 2026-05-30 ‚Äî TASK-67 Phase-5 review (codex exec; companion app-server was down this run)
| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-30 | Codex companion (`codex-companion.mjs review --wait`) failed with "app-server exited unexpectedly (exit 1)" AND `codex exec review --base main` timed out at 9min this run ‚Äî env-flaky, NOT a code issue. Fell back to `codex exec -c model_reasoning_effort=low "<focused prompt>" < /tmp/diff` which DID return findings in <60s. | The companion's app-server is the fragile path; a direct `codex exec` with the diff piped on stdin is the reliable fallback for a Phase-5 correctness pass when the companion is down. | skip the review (not allowed ‚Äî gate is required). |
| 2026-05-30 | Codex finding 1 (FIXED): shipTranscriptDelta's `noop` path left the host transcript STALE when the SDK shrinks/compacts the prefix in-place with no new line ‚Äî the misleading comment claimed it verified the prefix but made no host call. Fix: resync NOW when `fileBuf.length < sentOffset` (the file shrank below what we shipped); extracted `resyncWholeFile` helper. | "never silent staleness" (B3 no-omission spirit). A same-length in-place edit that adds a line is still caught by the append prefix-hash mismatch; the shrink case is the one the noop path missed. | leave it to the next append's prefix-hash check (defers staleness a whole turn). |
| 2026-05-30 | Codex finding 2 (FIXED): restoreTranscriptForResume threaded `sentOffset=buf.length` but `sentSeq=completeLines` ‚Äî inconsistent if the host ever returned non-`\n`-terminated bytes. Fix: `sentOffset = splitCompleteLines(buf).consumed` so offset and seq always agree (a trailing partial is held back). Latent today (store emits trailing `\n`), but internally-consistent is correct. | defense in depth on the state-threading invariant. | leave it (latent ‚Äî store always terminates lines). |
| 2026-05-30 | SDK project-dir slug (resume-write path) is `realpath(cwd).replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g,'-')` truncated to 200 chars + `-${djb2hash}` when longer ‚Äî VERIFIED by grepping the vendored SDK 0.2.119 `sdk.mjs` (`var P0=200`, `kB`/`gE` hash). `encodeProjectSlug` ports it byte-for-byte. `/permanent` (the prod cwd, 10 chars) never hits the cap, but the port removes a latent resume-write-to-wrong-dir bug for long paths. Don't hand-wave the slug ‚Äî grep the binary. | a slug mismatch = silent resume failure (SDK can't find the jsonl). The existing turn-end-uuid code AVOIDS reconstructing the slug (readdir-walk) precisely because it's uncertain ‚Äî but the resume-WRITE needs the exact dir before the SDK creates it. | readdir-walk (can't ‚Äî the dir doesn't exist yet on a fresh-pod resume). |

- `2026-05-30` (TASK-86) ‚Äî **Per-skill credential-slot namespacing fixes the skill-slot-collision LOCKOUT (two active authored skills sharing a slot like LINEAR_API_KEY terminated EVERY chat turn).** Chosen approach (a, human-decided in card Clarifications; (b) relevant-only-union rejected): namespace SKILL slots `skill:<id>:<slot>` in the host-side credentials map handed to `proxy:open-session`, keep AGENT/trusted base creds (`agent.requiredCredentials` / Anthropic default) BARE. Two skills' same-named slots ‚Üí two distinct namespaced keys ‚Üí two distinct `ax-cred:<hex>` placeholders ‚Üí no collision. Skill-vs-agent collision is NO LONGER fatal: the trusted bare credential always WINS the flat sandbox env stamp; a skill's namespaced cred still exists in the proxy map for its own egress but can't hijack the trusted env var (old security guarantee preserved as a benign no-op suppression, not a lockout). KEY ARCH FACT making the bare-env requirement satisfiable: proxy substitution is VALUE-based (`registry.ts replaceAll` replaces `ax-cred:<hex>` wherever it appears, regardless of env-var name), so the env-var NAME is just a placeholder vehicle ‚Äî the orchestrator projects the namespaced `envMap` BACK to bare env names (`projectEnvMapToBareNames`, trusted-wins + deterministic skill precedence) before threading into `proxyConfig.envMap` (the flat sandbox env). Skills share ONE flat sandbox env (no per-skill process/env scope), so two skills sharing a bare slot name still collapse to ONE value in the flat env (precedence wins) ‚Äî IRREDUCIBLE; the win is no-lockout + each cred reaching the proxy independently. git-cred wiring (`buildGitCredentialEnv` @ax/sandbox-protocol) must use each skill's OWN placeholder (threaded as optional `credentials[].placeholder` on InstalledSkillSchema, back-compat falls back to `envMap[slot]`) so per-skill git egress stays correct even when the flat-env stamp went to the other skill. Also in scope (card Clarifications): (T4) tuned `CRED_EXFIL` scanner so benign `curl -H "Authorization: Bearer $X_API_KEY"` against an allowed host stops false-tripping `credential-exfiltration`; (T5) scoped the pending cap-skill JIT "Connect‚Ä¶" card to its PROPOSING conversation (in-memory `pendingSkillConversation: Map<skillId,conversationId>` set in `onSkillsProposed`, same single-replica posture as respawnSessions/upfrontCardsByConv) so it stops persisting across unrelated conversations.

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-88) ‚Äî **SSE-open retry extended from TASK-84's fixed ~1.45s (4-attempt) budget to a wall-clock ~30s budget of capped-exponential backoff (250ms doubling, cap 2s) so a cold-respawn 404 auto-recovers ‚Äî no manual Retry click.** Client-only, `packages/channel-web/src/lib/transport.ts` `openSseStream`. Replaced the counted loop with an open-ended `for(;;)` gated on a `Date.now()+SSE_OPEN_TOTAL_BUDGET_MS` deadline (each retry wait clamped to the remaining budget). Decided budget=30s (card said ~20-30s): a cold kind runner pod spawn + per-reqId bind takes ~5-15s, 30s gives margin; bounded so a turn that died before ANY bind still terminates ‚Üí banner. SAFE per the card's key insight + FAULTA-5 history: the GET only replays a bounded per-reqId buffer (chunk-buffer.ts) and never starts a turn (only POST does), so re-opening it far longer than 1.45s can't duplicate a turn ‚Äî unlike a `regenerate()` re-POST, which FAULTA-5 (decisions 2026-05-25) forbids automating. Retryable set unchanged (404/425/429/5xx + network throw); 401/403/400/413 fail fast on attempt 1 (card: "unchanged"). **Review-fix decision:** the terminal throw now differs by reason ‚Äî a spent budget on a RETRYABLE failure throws `new Error(CONNECTION_LOST)` (the FAULTA-5 sentinel) so the runtime's `onError`‚Üí`applyTurnError` shows the user-facing "Connection lost. Retry to continue." banner + manual-retry button (the card's "fall back to the existing CONNECTION_LOST banner"); a fail-fast NON-retryable status keeps its verbatim `chat-flow SSE open failed: <status>` (a real client error is not a connection loss). TASK-84 had thrown the raw status string on ALL terminal exits ‚Äî that pre-existing gap missed the card's acceptance, so I fixed it with a `failFast` flag set only on the non-retryable break. During the wait surface `agentStatusActions.show(PHASE_LABELS['sandbox-starting'])` ("Starting sandbox‚Ä¶") set LAZILY (only after the first retryable failure) so the happy-path first-open never flashes it. OUT OF SCOPE (handoff follow-up): harden the server early-bind to be authoritative (retry the bind / 503 the POST) so `active_req_id` is guaranteed before the 202. | Rationale: budget-driven (not attempt-count) is self-documenting and decouples the cold-boot window from the backoff curve; CONNECTION_LOST fallback honors the card acceptance + reuses the established sentinel/wording rather than inventing new copy; lazy status avoids a flash on the common warm-path. | Alternatives: (a) keep an attempt count, just bump it (rejected ‚Äî couples timing to count, harder to reason about a "~30s" budget); (b) throw raw status on budget exhaustion like TASK-84 (rejected ‚Äî misses the card's "surfaces CONNECTION_LOST" acceptance + shows dev-ish copy to users); (c) show CONNECTION_LOST for the 403 fail-fast too (rejected ‚Äî a 403 is a real auth error, not a connection loss; "unchanged" per card); (d) eagerly set "Starting sandbox‚Ä¶" before the first open (rejected ‚Äî flashes on every warm turn).

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-90, epic connectors-first-class) ‚Äî **The capability shape now has a NEUTRAL canonical name: `Capabilities` in `@ax/skills-parser` (`packages/skills-parser/src/capabilities.ts`); `SkillCapabilities` is a back-compat `export type` alias of it.** Pure type/export-only refactor, no behavior/hook/table change. Why: per the connectors-first-class design a future connector object references the SAME `allowedHosts`/`credentials`/`mcpServers`/`packages` shape, and CLAUDE.md invariant #2 forbids a cross-plugin import ‚Äî so the shared shape must live under a neutral name in the dependency-free `@ax/skills-parser` (already eslint-allowlisted for both `@ax/skills` and `@ax/agents`). The sub-types (`CapabilitySlot`/`McpServerSpec`/`PackagesSpec`) were ALREADY neutral-named ‚Äî only the top-level interface needed renaming. `index.ts` now re-exports `Capabilities` + `PackagesSpec` (previously unexported) alongside the existing names. Migrated the two INTERNAL `src` consumers (`manifest.ts` `ParsedManifest.capabilities`, `build.ts` input) to the neutral name so `pnpm build` (tsc) is the load-bearing regression guard ‚Äî PROVEN: renaming the export away makes the build go red. External consumers (`@ax/skills`, `@ax/agents`, `@ax/skill-broker`) were left on the `SkillCapabilities` alias (zero churn, alias keeps them compiling). | Rationale: smallest honest diff that satisfies the card + makes the neutral name real and guarded; test files aren't type-checked anywhere in this repo's gate (build excludes `__tests__`, vitest strips types, eslint isn't type-aware) so a type-only test CAN'T be the guard ‚Äî a migrated `src` consumer is. | Alternatives: (a) mass-rewrite every consumer to `Capabilities` (rejected ‚Äî needless churn, the card says "Skills continue to consume the type exactly as before"); (b) add a runtime sentinel value to make the vitest test load-bearing (rejected ‚Äî adds unrequested runtime API, YAGNI); (c) leave both `src` consumers on the alias and rely only on the (unchecked) vitest test (rejected ‚Äî then nothing in the gate guards the neutral export).

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-90, Phase 5 review substitution) ‚Äî The `ax-code-reviewer` subagent / `Task` dispatch tool was NOT available in this orchestrated agent's tool surface (no dispatch tool surfaced via ToolSearch). Fell back to a manual whole-branch (`main...HEAD`) self-review against the six AX invariants + card acceptance. Justified by the diff being tiny and type/export-only (5 src files + 1 doc comment + 1 test, no hook/IPC/runtime/dependency change). Findings: none actionable. Logged here per the "log any review substitution" discipline.

## 2026-05-31 ‚Äî TASK-91 @ax/connectors plugin design decisions

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | New `@ax/connectors` package mirrors `@ax/conversations` structure (migrations/store/scope/types/plugin/index). Postgres-backed via `database:get-instance`; one `connectors_v1_connectors` table. | Established DB-backed-plugin pattern; predecessor learning confirmed the shape is settled. | sqlite-backed (rejected by Clarifications ‚Äî keep Postgres table). |
| 2026-05-31 | `Connector = { id, name, description, usageNote, keyMode:'personal'|'workspace', visibility:'private'|'shared' } + Capabilities`. `Capabilities` TYPE-imported from `@ax/skills-parser` (the only @ax/* type-only import allowed for connectors per eslint allow-list). Zod schema re-declared LOCALLY (no cross-plugin runtime import; invariant #2). | TASK-90 lifted `Capabilities` into skills-parser exactly for this. Re-declaring zod locally avoids a runtime import. | importing a zod schema from skills-parser (would be a runtime cross-plugin import ‚Äî forbidden). |
| 2026-05-31 | Five hooks: `connectors:list`, `connectors:get`, `connectors:upsert`, `connectors:delete`, `connectors:resolve`. Storage/mechanism-agnostic payloads ‚Äî NO `transport`/`command`/`stdio`/`url`/`mcp` as first-class hook fields (they live only inside the spec's `Capabilities`). `keyMode`/`visibility`/`usageNote` are fine. | Card acceptance + boundary review. resolve returns the mechanism-agnostic descriptor (full spec); get/list return metadata + spec. | folding resolve into get (rejected ‚Äî card lists 5 distinct hooks; resolve is the future routing entry point). |
| 2026-05-31 | Store keyed `(owner_user_id, connector_id)`; ownership-scoped. Add `connectors_v1_` to eslint `no-bare-tenant-tables` TENANT_TABLE_PREFIXES and route multi-row reads through `scope.ts`. | Connectors carry ownership + visibility ‚Üí tenant-scoped table, same posture as conversations/skills (invariant I7). | global single-owner table (rejected ‚Äî connectors are per-user-owned per the design's access model). |
| 2026-05-31 | Wire into k8s preset ONLY (per Clarifications). Add to `PLUGINS_TO_DROP` in BOTH acceptance.test.ts + multi-tenant-acceptance.test.ts (postgres-backed). Add reachability assertion in preset.test.ts. | Local CLI is Postgres-free; connectors need `database:get-instance` ‚Üí CLI boot crash (same reason skills/routines/conversations are CLI-absent). | adding Postgres to local CLI (rejected by Clarifications). |
| 2026-05-31 | Half-wired window OPEN by design: the connector store exists but nothing routes through it yet (skill capability block stays authoritative). This is explicitly sanctioned by the card + design Phase 1 ‚Äî NOT an invariant-#3 violation because the plugin is fully registered + tested + reachable; the *consumer* lands in later phases. | Card: "This OPENS the half-wired window". Plugin itself is complete and reachable. | wiring a consumer now (out of scope ‚Äî later phases). |
| 2026-05-31 (TASK-93) | Extend the approved-caps wall to connectors via an ADDITIVE polymorphic-subject: add `connector_id TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT ''` to `skills_v1_approved_caps`, PK ‚Üí 6-col `(owner,agent,skill_id,connector_id,cap_kind,cap_value)`. Grant subject is exactly one of `{skill, connector}`; the unused side carries `''` sentinel (PK cols can't be NULL). Store input is a discriminated `{skillId}\|{connectorId}` ref; existing `{skillId}` callers unchanged. | Card + design ¬ß"reuse the existing wall": extend, don't fork (invariant #4). Empty-string sentinel keeps it purely additive ‚Äî existing skill `WHERE skill_id=X` queries still match (connector rows carry skill_id=''). Migration header bans column rename (‚Üíside-table), so `(subject_kind,subject_id)` rename is out; the additive column is the smaller back-compatible change. | rename skill_id‚Üí(subject_kind,subject_id) (rejected ‚Äî destructive per migration header); nullable connector_id NOT in PK (rejected ‚Äî Postgres PK cols are NOT NULL, and it'd allow dup rows). |

| 2026-05-31 | TASK-91: `connectors:upsert` `created` flag = "no LIVE row existed" ‚Äî resurrecting a tombstoned connector reports `created:true` (a tombstoned row is invisible to its owner via get/list, so re-connecting it is a creation from the user's view). | Matches the user mental model; the alternative (PK-existence) would surface a confusing `created:false` for a connector the user thinks is brand new. | `created` = "no row with this PK at all" (rejected ‚Äî leaks the soft-delete tombstone into the API semantic). |

## 2026-05-31 ‚Äî TASK-96 connector keyMode connect flow + reach-by-attachment

| Date | Decision | Rationale | Alternatives |
|---|---|---|---|
| 2026-05-31 | TASK-96 lands the CREDENTIALS-SIDE connect semantics of a connector's `keyMode` as a tested, genuinely-wired surface ‚Äî NOT the deferred Phase 4 orchestrator/UI routing (AgentForm connector-attachment, connect-flow UI). Connectors are still half-wired (nothing consumes `connectors:resolve`); the card = design Phase 3, Phase 4/5 are separate later cards. | Card acceptance is the keyMode‚Üíscope mapping + no-creds-flag + consent moment, all expressible at the resolution surface without the deferred UI. Building Phase 4 routing would overreach scope. | (a) build the full connect-flow UI now (rejected ‚Äî Phase 4/5, out of scope, would be half-wired without orchestrator union); (b) blocked on premise (rejected ‚Äî the credentials-side semantics ARE buildable + testable now). |
| 2026-05-31 | Extend `connectors:resolve` to also return a derived `credentialPlan: { slot, scope:'user'|'global', ref:'account:<svc>' }[]` (one entry per capabilities credential slot) + `requiresSharedKeyConsent:boolean`. The derivation maps keyMode‚Üíscope: `personal`‚Üí`scope:'user'` (per-user JIT `account:<service>` vault, act-as-yourself); `workspace`‚Üí`scope:'global'` (single admin/company key, shared service identity). | This is the documented future routing entry point (design Phase 5: "resolving slots through the connector instead of the skill"). `connectors:resolve` is already registered+tested+preset-reachable, so extending its return is a REAL exercised path, not half-wired infra. Reach derives PURELY from keyMode‚Üíscope ‚Äî the design's reach-by-attachment, no new credentials column. | (a) a standalone helper nothing calls (rejected ‚Äî half-wired per Half-Wired Code Policy); (b) a new `connectors:connect-plan` hook (rejected ‚Äî premature 2nd hook; resolve IS the routing surface per its own doc comment). |
| 2026-05-31 | The `account:<service>` service tag for each slot = the slot's existing `CapabilitySlot.account` when present, else the connector `id`. Both keyModes use the SAME `account:<service>` ref shape; only the SCOPE differs (user vs global). | Design open-Q #1 lean "share by service": the `account:<service>` vault key is the natural credential identity, reused across connectors/skills naming the same service. The existing JIT flow (skill-broker, applyCapabilityGrant) already binds `account:<service>` for `account`-tagged slots ‚Äî connectors reuse that exact ref so a personal connector and a skill to the same service share one key. | per-connector ref `connector:<id>:<slot>` (rejected ‚Äî would NOT share the key by service, contradicts the JIT vault reuse the rest of the system relies on). |
| 2026-05-31 | Consent gate: `requiresSharedKeyConsent` is true iff the resolved key becomes spendable by an identity the keyholder doesn't solely control ‚Äî i.e. `keyMode==='workspace'` (one key, every allowed agent spends it) OR `visibility==='shared'`. `personal`+`private` ‚Üí false (you only ever act as yourself). The consent COPY ("Sharing this key lets their assistant act as you on <service>. They can't copy the key ‚Äî but they can use it.") is a single exported constant `SHARED_KEY_CONSENT_COPY` + a `sharedKeyConsentMessage(service)` formatter in @ax/connectors. | Design "Consent caveat (invariant #5)": the proxy stops theft, not authorized misuse; the consent is one explicit moment, surfaced BEFORE the key becomes spendable by a shared/team agent. Exporting the copy + a boolean gate lets the future connect surface render it and a test pin it ‚Äî without the deferred UI. | hard-code the copy in the (not-yet-built) UI (rejected ‚Äî then nothing in THIS card surfaces/tests the consent acceptance criterion). |
| 2026-05-31 | NO new visibility/public/private flag on @ax/credentials. Reach derives solely from the credential SCOPE (`global|user|agent`) the key is bound to ‚Äî `personal`‚Üíuser, `workspace`‚Üíglobal, a shared agent‚Üíagent-scope. Pin with a guard test asserting `credentials:set`/`credentials:list` payload shapes carry no `visibility`/`public`/`private`/`shared`/`reach` field. | Card acceptance #2 + design "Credentials: reach by attachment, never by visibility". The existing scope model already expresses every reach (private/shared/personal-default/company-key). | add a visibility column to credentials (rejected ‚Äî directly violates the card + design; reach is already fully expressible via scope). |
| 2026-05-31 | The scope vocabulary (`'user'|'global'`) is re-declared LOCALLY in @ax/connectors (a `CredentialScope`-shaped string literal union), NOT imported from @ax/credentials. | Invariant #2 (no cross-plugin runtime import); same posture as the existing local zod re-declaration of Capabilities. The credential-plan's `scope` strings are a stable contract, not @ax/credentials internals. | import CredentialScope from @ax/credentials (rejected ‚Äî cross-plugin import, forbidden by eslint no-restricted-imports). |

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-96, Phase 5 review substitution) ‚Äî The `ax-code-reviewer` subagent / Task dispatch tool was NOT available in this orchestrated agent's tool surface (confirmed via ToolSearch ‚Äî no dispatch tool surfaced; same as TASK-90). Fell back to a manual whole-branch self-review against the six AX invariants + card acceptance + the security-checklist three threat models. Diff is small + additive (one new `credential-plan.ts` module + two additive `connectors:resolve` return fields + 3 test files; no new package, no package.json/tsconfig/dep change, no IPC/sandbox change). Findings: none actionable. One thing verified during review: the slot `account` field (which flows into the `account:<service>` ref via `accountRef`) is NOT char-constrained by the connectors `CapabilitySlotSchema` ‚Äî but `credentialPlan` only carries it as an opaque plan string; the live `credentials:get`/`credentials:list` consumers (deferred Phase 5 router) apply `validateRef`(REF_RE) at their boundary, fail-closed. This is the identical trust posture the existing skill path uses (skill-broker + applyCapabilityGrant build `account:${account}` the same way). Logged here per the "log any review substitution" discipline.

- `2026-05-31` (TASK-97, post-rebase reconciliation) ‚Äî **TASK-96 merged into main WHILE I built, and it is the one source of truth for a connector slot's credential REF.** TASK-96 added `connectors:resolve` ‚Üí `credentialPlan[]` whose ref = `account:<serviceTagForSlot(slot, connectorId)>` = `account:<slot.account ?? connectorId>` (NOT `connector:<id>:<slot>`). My orchestrator connector fold MUST address the SAME vault row TASK-96's connect flow WRITES, so the untagged-slot ref had to change from my initial `connector:<id>:<slot>` to `account:<connectorId>`. The env-NAME key stays per-connector-namespaced (`connector:<id>:<slot>`) ‚Äî that's just the host-side credential-map key + placeholder vehicle + bare-env-projection join; only the REF (the vault address) must match. Re-derived locally in `connector-union.ts` per I2 (no @ax/connectors runtime import), mirroring `serviceTagForSlot`; `connector-union.test.ts` pins the `account:<svc>` shape. **Lesson: when a sibling same-epic card lands a derivation that produces a durable identifier (a credential ref, a vault key, a path), the orchestrator must CONSUME that identifier's derivation, not re-invent it ‚Äî a divergent ref silently addresses an empty row. Check `git fetch origin main` + diff the shared files BEFORE assuming your base is current; auto-ship merges siblings ahead of you.** Also: `connectors:resolve` does NOT carry `usageNote` (it's the routing descriptor); only `connectors:list-defaults` (full Connector) does ‚Äî private connectors resolved via resolve fall back to a generic synthetic SKILL.md body (acceptable; the note is a nicety, not load-bearing for reach).

No other board card (TASK-96..100) owns the executor/IPC. Design ¬ß"Authoring" line 180 defines the loop as calling install_authored_connector ‚Üí so the tool must exist.

The live runner system-prompt (skillAuthoringNote) uses skill_propose. Narrowing ax-skill-creator must also fix it to the skill_propose reality.

## 2026-05-31 | TASK-95 architecture: host-executed connector_propose tool (NOT a sandbox executor + IPC chain)
- **Decision:** The model-facing connector-authoring tool is `connector_propose`, a HOST-executed tool (`executesIn: 'host'`) in a new package `@ax/tool-connector-propose` ‚Äî mirroring `@ax/skill-broker`'s `request_capability`, NOT `@ax/tool-skill-propose`'s sandbox-executor+IPC pattern. It registers BOTH the descriptor (tool:register) AND `tool:execute:connector_propose`, reads (userId, agentId) from the host-trusted tool ctx, and calls the existing `connectors:install-authored` hook on the bus.
- **Rationale:** connector args are pure structured JSON `{connectorId,name,hosts,slots,packages,mcpServers,usageNote,keyMode}` the model produces inline ‚Äî there is NO draft directory to read from the sandbox FS (unlike skill_propose which must read /ephemeral/skill-draft/<id>/). So the sandbox-executor + IPC-action chain TASK-94's note sketched is UNNECESSARY complexity; the request_capability host-tool shape is the right, smaller fit. The host hook `connectors:install-authored` is the authoritative validator (I5 trust boundary); the tool is a thin scope-stamping adapter (light shape check + clean error map, like request_capability's skillId check).
- **Alternatives:** (a) sandbox executor + connector.install-authored IPC action (TASK-94's literal sketch) ‚Äî rejected: no FS bytes to read sandbox-side; pure overhead. (b) add connector_propose into @ax/skill-broker ‚Äî rejected: broker's identity is skill-CATALOG brokering (hard calls skills:*); a new package per authoring tool matches the @ax/tool-skill-propose convention and keeps the connectors:install-authored dep isolated + hasService-gated.
- New package needs project refs in root tsconfig.json AND presets/k8s/tsconfig.json (TASK-91 gotcha) + an entry in ALWAYS_ON_BROKER_TOOLS so non-wildcard agents see it.

| 2026-05-31 (TASK-111) | **Skill‚Üíconnector cap-resolution bridge: resolve each skill's `connectors[]` via `connectors:resolve` and fold through the EXISTING `foldConnectorCaps` path, deduped against TASK-97's agent effective set.** Add `connectors` to the orchestrator's `ResolvedSkillForOrch` mirror (`skills:resolve` already returns it via @ax/skills `ResolvedSkill.connectors`; the mirror just dropped it). In orchestrator.ts collect the union of `connectors[]` over `unionedSkills`, resolve the not-already-resolved ids (new `resolveSkillReferencedConnectors` helper in connector-union.ts), append to `effectiveConnectors`, then the single existing `foldConnectorCaps` call folds them. NON-FATAL (a resolve failure skips that connector). | Reuses TASK-97 fold verbatim ‚Üí no second materialization path (invariant #4). Skill `connectors[]` stops being dead-on-arrival. Legacy `skill.capabilities` block stays fully functional (half-wired window stays OPEN until TASK-100). | (a) a separate skill-connector materialization path ‚Äî REJECTED, duplicates fold logic, violates one-source-of-truth. (b) resolve inside @ax/skills `skills:resolve` and return folded caps ‚Äî REJECTED, cross-plugin coupling + the orchestrator is the materialization owner. |
| 2026-05-31 (TASK-111) | **`skill_propose` migration is already done at the instruction layer** ‚Äî `ax-skill-creator/SKILL.md` already teaches `connectors:` references + forbids a `capabilities:` block (TASK-92/94), the parser rejects misplaced cap keys, and the skill-propose executor ships raw `manifestYaml` so `connectors:` round-trips to the host re-parse. The remaining gap was purely the orchestrator NOT resolving referenced connectors ‚Üí this card. No SKILL.md rewrite needed; verify-via-test instead. | Avoids a redundant SKILL.md churn; the real missing bridge is orchestrator-side resolution. | Rewriting ax-skill-creator SKILL.md ‚Äî REJECTED, already migrated. |
| 2026-05-31 (TASK-111) | **`request_capability` (skill-broker) folds the requested catalog skill's referenced connectors' reach into the approval card** (resolve each `connectors[]` id via `connectors:resolve`, union their hosts/slots/packages into the card surface) so a connector-declared skill surfaces the connector's reach, reusing the existing `kind:'skill'` card + TASK-93 wall. | 2026-06-01 | **TASK-113 ‚Äî approved authored connectors are PROMOTED into the curated registry on approval (path A, invariant #4).** `applyAuthoredConnectorGrant` (chat-orchestrator) calls `connectors:upsert` with the `shown`-narrowed APPROVED capability surface (hosts/slots/packages from the approved sets + the proposal's mcpServers) + `keyMode`/`usageNote`/`name` from the resolved draft, `visibility:'private'`, owner-scoped to the grant's userId. | 2026-06-01 | **TASK-108 ‚Äî connector Test action = server-side `POST /admin/connectors/:id/test` probe = credential-slot presence + config sanity, NOT a live outbound MCP connection.** The probe returns `{ status: 'reachable' \| 'unreachable' \| 'needs-key', detail? }` (200). Derivation (connectors plugin only, no cross-plugin runtime import): resolve the connector's credential PLAN (existing `deriveCredentialPlan`), then for each slot ask `credentials:list` (metadata-only ‚Äî scope+ref, never values) whether a matching `(scope, ref)` row exists; any unfilled required slot ‚üπ `needs-key`.
